Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Mutual Apostasy and Return: Istihsan Preserves the Marriage
Providing ruling and proof for marriage continuity upon mutual apostasy and return

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marriage continuity when both spouses apostatize together and return together, explain the istihsan basis, and identify the conditions under which the marriage dissolves.

Core Idea
Mutual apostasy followed by mutual return does not dissolve the marriage — istihsan overrides qiyas.

This lesson examines a unique Hanafi ruling: if both spouses apostatize simultaneously and then both return to Islam, their marriage remains intact. The ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) and supported by the practice of the Companions with Banu Hanifa. Understanding this case clarifies the Hanafi approach to reconciling analogy with legal presumption and the importance of intention in marital harmony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its key condition
The matn states: 'If they apostatize together and embrace Islam together, they do not separate.' Focus on the two conditions: both apostatizing together (or order unknown) and both returning together. The ruling is that the marriage remains valid.
The condition 'together' includes cases where the order of apostasy is unknown, presumed simultaneous.
2
Understand the legal basis: istihsan overrides qiyas
By qiyas (analogy), apostasy of either spouse would dissolve the marriage (due to difference in religion). But here istihsan departs from qiyas because mutual apostasy indicates harmony and mutual agreement, removing the basis of conflict.
Istihsan is a Hanafi source allowing exception to qiyas for a stronger reason.
3
Examine the proof from Banu Hanifa
The scholars cite that Banu Hanifa apostatized and later returned to Islam. The Companions did not order them to renew their marriages, implying the marriages were considered valid. This tacit ijma supports the ruling.
The passage also notes a critique from Fath al-Qadir that Banu Hanifa only refused zakat, but the stronger view is that their apostasy was genuine.
4
Clarify the meaning of 'ma'an' (together)
The text clarifies that 'ma'an' does not require absolute simultaneity in time. Rather, if the precedence of one spouse over the other is unknown, the law presumes they apostatized together. This presumption avoids invalidating marriages unnecessarily.
Actual simultaneity is possible (e.g., both prostrating to an idol together) but rare.
5
Note the boundary condition: joining dar al-harb
If after apostasy one spouse joins the land of war (dar al-harb), the marriage dissolves due to physical separation (tabayun), even if both apostatized together initially. This is an exception to the general rule.
This is derived from the author's earlier statement that tabayun causes separation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن ارتدا معاً وأسلما معات لم تبن استحساناً لعدم المنافاة لأن جهة المنافاة بردة أحدهما عدم اتنظام المصالح بينهما والموافقة على الارتداد ظاهرة في انتظامها بينهما إلا أن يموتا بقتل أو غيره، وقد استدل المشايخ بأن بني حنيفة ارتدوا ثم أسلموا ولم تأمرهم الصحابة رضي الله عنهم بتجديد الأنكحة، ولما لم تأمرهم بذلك علمنا أنهم اعتبروا أن ردتهم وقعت معاً إذ لو حملت على التعاقب فسدت أنكحتهم ولزمهم التجديد. والمراد من المعية عدم تعاقب كل زوجين من بني حنيفة، أما جميعهم فلا لأن الرجال جازان يتعاقبوا ولا تفسد أنكحتهم إذا كان كل رجل ارتد مع امرأته معاً وحكم الصحابة رضي الله عنهم بذلك حكم بالظاهر لا بالحمل لأن الظاهر أن قيم البيت إذا أراد أمراً تكون قرينته فيه قرينته . وتعقبهم في فتح القدير بأن ارتدادهم بمنعهم الزكاة كما في المبسوط وهو يتوقف على نقل أن لجحد افتراضها ولم ينقل ولا هو لازم وقتال أبي بكر رضي الله عنه لا يستلزمه لجواز قتالهم إذا أجمعوا على منعهم. حقاً شرعياً وعطلوه، والأوجه الاستدلال بوقوع ردة العرب وقتالهم على ذلك من غير تعيين بني حنيفة وما نعي الزكاة وهو قطعي ولم يؤمروا بتجديد الأنكحة اهـ. وفي الصحاح : حنيفة أبو حي من العرب. ولما قدم المصنف أن التباين سبب للفرقة علم أنهما إذا ارتدا ثم لحق أحدهما بدار الحرب فإنها تبين بالتباين كما في فتح القدير. والمراد بقوله «ارتدا» معاً أعم من أن يعلم أنهما ارتدا في كلمة واحدة أو لم يعرف سبق أحدهما على الآخر. قال في الميحط : وإذا لم يعرف سبق أحدهما على الآخر في الردة جعل في الحكم كأنهما وجدا معاً كما في الغرقي والحرقي. وقيد بالردة لأنه المسلم إذا كان تحته نصرانية فتمجسا معاً قال هـ. قوله : (لا بالحمل أي لا بالحمل على أن كل زوجين ارتد معاً للجهل بالحال كالغرقي والحرقي قوله : (وهو يتوقف على نقل الخ قال في النهر : قد يقال إن قوله في الرواية «فأسلموا» دليل على أن المنع كان جحداً ! . ولا يخفى أنه لا يجدي فإن ذلك محل النزاع أيضاً قوله : (والمراد بقوله ارتد . الخ) قال في النهر : المراد أن لا يعرف سبق أحدهما على الآخر أما المعية الحقيقية فمتعذرة، وما في البحر فيه بعد ظاهر نعم ارتدادهما معاً بالفعل ممكن بأن حملاً مصحفاً وألقياه في القاذورات أو سجدا للصنم معاً.
His statement: (And if they apostatize together and then embrace Islam together, they do not separate, by istihsan, because there is no conflict; because the basis of conflict by the apostasy of one of them is the lack of harmony between them, and mutual agreement on apostasy shows harmony between them, unless they die by killing or other. The scholars have argued by the fact that Banu Hanifa apostatized and then embraced Islam, and the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) did not order them to renew their marriages. Since they did not order them to do so, we know that they considered that their apostasy occurred simultaneously, for if it were taken as successive, their marriages would be invalidated and renewal would be necessary. The meaning of simultaneity is that each couple of Banu Hanifa did not have successive apostasy; as for all of them collectively, no, because men may be successive without invalidating their marriages if each man apostatized with his wife simultaneously. And the Companions' (may Allah be pleased with them) ruling on that was based on apparent circumstances, not on assumption, because the apparent situation is that when the head of a household intends something, his family will join him in it. They were criticized in Fath al-Qadir by saying that their apostasy was because they refused to pay zakat, as in al-Mabsut, which requires a report that they denied its obligation, but that was not reported, nor is it necessarily implied by Abu Bakr's (may Allah be pleased with him) fighting them, since it is permissible to fight them if they collectively refuse a legal right and abandon it. The stronger argument is the occurrence of apostasy of the Arabs and fighting them for that reason without specifying Banu Hanifa, and the fact that they refused zakat is definitive, and they were not ordered to renew their marriages. In al-Sihah: Hanifa is a tribe of the Arabs. Since the author stated that separation is a cause for dissolution, it is known that if they apostatize and then one of them joins the land of war, then she is separated due to separation, as in Fath al-Qadir. And the meaning of his statement 'they apostatized together' is broader: whether it is known that they apostatized in one word or the precedence of one over the other is not known. He said in al-Muhit: If the precedence of one over the other in apostasy is not known, it is considered in law as if they both occurred together, like the drowned and the burned. And it is qualified by apostasy because if a Muslim has a Christian wife and they both become Magians together... he said. His statement: (Not by assumption) means not by assuming that each couple apostatized together due to ignorance of the actual situation, like the drowned and the burned. His statement: (And it depends on a report...). He said in al-Nahr: It may be said that his statement in the narration 'then they embraced Islam' indicates that the refusal was denial! And it is not hidden that this does not help because that is also the point of dispute. His statement: (And the meaning of his statement 'they apostatized...') He said in al-Nahr: The meaning is that the precedence of one over the other is not known. As for actual simultaneity, it is impossible, and what is in al-Bahr has apparent weakness. Yes, their apostasy together is practically possible, such as if they both carried a mushaf and threw it into filth, or both prostrated to an idol at the same time.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This is an expansion probe (sharh) of the matn's ruling on mutual apostasy. The commentator explains that if both spouses apostatize together (ma'an) and then both return to Islam together, their marriage is not dissolved according to istihsan (juristic preference). The reasoning is based on the idea that mutual apostasy does not conflict with marital harmony—since both are in agreement, the basis of conflict (difference in religion) is absent. The proof cited is the incident of Banu Hanifa, a tribe that apostatized en masse and later returned to Islam. The Companions, including Abu Bakr, did not order them to renew their marriages, indicating that their apostasy was considered simultaneous (or at least not shown to be successive). The commentator then clarifies that the simultaneity intended is that each couple's apostasy is not known to be successive; if one knows that one spouse apostatized first, the marriage dissolves. The text also discusses a critique from Fath al-Qadir, which suggests that Banu Hanifa's apostasy was merely refusal to pay zakat, not denial of Islam, but the commentator argues that the stronger proof is the general apostasy of the Arabs. The passage further explains the legal meaning of 'ma'an' (together): if the order cannot be determined, the presumption is that they happened together. The possibility of actual simultaneous apostasy is acknowledged, by giving examples like both together throwing a mushaf or prostrating to an idol.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsān): Juristic preference; here it is the basis for not dissolving the marriage when both apostatize together and return together, because the analogy (qiyas) would have required dissolution.
معية (ma‘iyyah): Simultaneity of apostasy in the legal sense; if the precedence of one spouse's apostasy over the other is not known, they are considered to have apostatized together.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence used by the Hanafi scholars to support the ruling that mutual apostasy and return does not dissolve the marriage?
A) A direct verse from the Quran
B) The practice of the Companions with Banu Hanifa
C) The analogy with the case of sequential Islam
D) A hadith from the Prophet

Key Takeaway
When both spouses apostatize together and return together, the marriage endures due to istihsan, supported by the tacit ijmāʿ of the Companions.

Nikah — Marriage

Dispute on Magian Conversion and Sequential Islam Acceptance
Intra-Hanafi dispute and related rulings on apostasy and marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on the effect of becoming Magian and apply the rule on sequential Islam acceptance.

Core Idea
When both spouses become Magians, does the marriage dissolve? Abu Yusuf says yes, Muhammad says no.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a classic intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: if a Muslim husband and his Christian wife both convert to Magianism, does their marriage dissolve? Abu Yusuf argues that only the husband apostatized, so separation occurs. Muhammad argues that both apostatized together, so the marriage remains. The passage also addresses the ruling when one spouse accepts Islam before the other, and the complexities of a minor's status when parents convert.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key dispute
Locate the two positions: Abu Yusuf holds that the marriage dissolves (furqa taqa'). Muhammad holds that it does not. Understand their respective dalil.
The dispute hinges on whether the wife's conversion to Magianism is considered riddah or a change within kufr.
2
Analyze the underlying reasoning
For Muhammad, both apostatized because the woman's tamajjusa adds a quality to disbelief, making it like originating disbelief. For Abu Yusuf, apostasy is changing the original religion; since the woman was originally Christian, her change to Magianism is not apostasy, only the husband apostatized.
The difference affects the practical outcome of the marriage.
3
Examine the sequential Islam ruling
If one spouse accepts Islam and then the other later, the marriage dissolves because the other's continued disbelief is incompatible with marriage from the start. This applies all the more when only one accepts.
The rule is based on the principle that apostasy or disbelief negates the marriage contract both initially and in continuation.
4
Consider the minor's status
A minor child's religion follows the better of the two parents or the land of Islam. When both parents apostatize, the minor remains Muslim if in Dar al-Islam, but if both become Magians (Christian parents), the child follows them into Magianism.
The comment about 'tamajjusa vs. riddah' distinguishes between Christian parents becoming Magians and Muslim parents apostatizing.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Yusuf, the marriage ends immediately; under Muhammad, it continues. The text does not give a tarjih, so both are recorded.
This ikhtilaf is recorded in al-Muhit as legitimate difference of opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أبو يوسف تقع الفرقة، وقال محمد لا تقع لأنهما ارتدا معاً لأن تمجس المرأة بمنزلة الردة لأنها أحدثت زيادة صفة في الكفر فكان بمنزلة إحداث أصل الكفر؛ لأبي يوسف أنه لم توجد الردة منها لأن الردة ليست إلا بتبديل أصل الدين ولم يوجد منها تبديل أصل الدين فقد وجد ارتداد أحد الزوجين فبانت كذا في المحيط . ولو تهودا وقعت الفرقة بينهما اتفاقاً لأنها ما أحدثت زيادة صفة في الكفر . قوله : (وبانت لو أسلما متعاقبا لأن ردة الآخر منافية للنكاح ابتداء فكذا بقاء، ويعلم به حكم البينونة بإسلام أحدهما فقط بالأولى ولا مهر لها قبل الدخول إن كان المسلم هو الزوج ، وإن كان هي فلها النصف وبعد الدخول لا يسقط شيء مطلقاً ولا ترث منه إن أسلم ومات، فإن أسلمت ثم مات مرتداً ورثته. كذا في المبتغى بالمعجمة . قال في المحيط : تزوج صبية لها أبوان مسلمان فارتدا معاً لم تبن لأنها مسلمة تبعاً للأبوين وتبعاً للدار باعتبار الاتصال والمجاورة، ولهذا اللقيط في دار الإسلام يحكم بإسلامه تبعاً للدار ، ولو أدخلت صغيرة من دار الحرب إلى دار الإسلام وليس معها أبواها فماتت فإنه يصلى عليها وتبعية الدار هنا قائمة فبقيت مسلمة لأن البقاء أسهل من الابتداء، فإن لحقا بها بدار الحرب بانت لانقطاع حكم الدار. ولو مات أحد الأبوين في دارنا مسلماً أو مرتداً ثم ارتد الآخر ولحق بها بدار الحرب لم تبن ويصلى عليها إذا ماتت لأن التبعية حكم تناهى بالموت مسلماً، وكذا بالموت مرتداً لأن أحكام الإسلام قائمة. ولو أن صبية نصرانية تحت مسلم تمجس أبوها وقد ماتت الأم نصرانية لم تبن لأن الولد يتبع خير الوالدين ديناً فبقيت على دين الأم ولو تمجس أبواها بانت ولا مهر لها، ولا يمكن الحكم بالإسلام هنا تبعاً للدار لأن الدار لا تثبت التبعية ابتداء ما دامت تبعية الأبوين قائمة، فإن بلغت عاقلة مسلمة ثم جنت ثم ارتد أبواهالم تبن وإن لحق بها بدار الحرب لأنها مسلمة أصلاً لا تبعاً، وكذلك الصبية العاقلة لو أسلمت ثم جنت لأنها صارت أصلاً في الإسلام اهـ. وهنا مسألتان : الأولى مسألة ما إذا أسلم وتحته أكثر من أربع أو أختان وحكمها عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف إن كان التزوج في عقد واحد فرق بينه وبينهن أو في عقدين فنكاح من يحل سبقه جائز ونكاح من تأخر فوقع الجمع به والزيادة على الأربع باطل . الثانية مسألة ما إذا بلغت المسلمة المنكوحة ولم تصف الإسلام فإنها تبين وهي مذكورة في المحيط وغيره والله تعالى أعلم. قوله: (ولو تمجس أبواها بانت قال في النهر : وفي الفرق بين ما لو تمجسا أو ارتدا تأمل فليتدبر ا هـ . قلت : الفرق ظاهر وهو ما ذكره من أن البنت بارتداد أبويها المسلمين تبقى مسلمة تبعاً للأبوين وللدار، والمرتد في حكم المسلم بجبره على الإسلام بخلاف تمجس أبويها النصرانيين لأنها تصير تبعاً لهما في التمجس ولا يمكن تبعيتها للدار مع بقاء تبعية الأبوين وكأنه ظن أن الضمير في «ارتدا» للأبوين النصرانيين وليس بالراقع قوله : (وهي مذكورة في المحيط وغيره) قال في
Abu Yusuf: the separation occurs. Muhammad said: it does not occur because they both apostatized together, because the woman's becoming a Magian is like apostasy, because she introduced an increase in quality of disbelief, so it is like introducing the origin of disbelief. For Abu Yusuf: apostasy did not occur from her because apostasy is only by changing the original religion, and she did not change the original religion. So apostasy of one spouse occurred, so she is separated. As in al-Muhit. If they both become Jews, the separation occurs by agreement, because she did not introduce an increase in quality of disbelief. His statement: (And they separate if they embrace Islam successively) because the apostasy of the other is incompatible with marriage initially, so also in continuation. And the ruling of separation by one of them embracing Islam alone is known all the more. And she has no mahr before consummation if the Muslim is the husband; if it is she, she gets half. After consummation, nothing is dropped absolutely. She does not inherit from him if he embraces Islam and dies; if she embraces Islam and then he dies as an apostate, she inherits from him. As in al-Muntaba bi al-mujamma. He said in al-Muhit: If a young girl with Muslim parents apostatized together, she does not separate because she is Muslim by following her parents and by following the land due to connection and proximity. Hence a foundling in the land of Islam is judged to be Muslim by following the land. And if a young girl is brought from the land of war to the land of Islam without her parents, and she dies, prayer is performed over her, and the following of the land remains, so she remains Muslim, because continuation is easier than inception. If they (her parents) join her in the land of war, she separates due to the termination of the rule of the land. If one of the parents dies in our land as a Muslim or as an apostate, and then the other apostatizes and joins her in the land of war, she does not separate, and prayer is performed over her if she dies, because the rule of following ended with death as Muslim, and similarly with death as an apostate, because the rulings of Islam remain. If a Christian girl is married to a Muslim and her father becomes a Magian while her mother died Christian, she does not separate because the child follows the better of the two parents in religion, so she remains on the mother's religion. If both parents become Magians, she separates and she has no mahr. And it is not possible to judge Islam here by following the land because the land does not establish following initially as long as the following of the parents exists. If she reaches maturity as a sane Muslim, then becomes insane, then her father apostatizes, she does not separate even if he joins the land of war, because she is Muslim by origin not by following. Similarly, if a sane young girl embraces Islam and then becomes insane, because she became a Muslim by origin. Here are two issues: First: the issue of if he embraces Islam while having more than four wives or two sisters; its ruling according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: if the marriage was in one contract, he is separated from all; if in two contracts, the marriage of the one whose contract came first is valid, and the later contract is invalid due to combination and exceeding four. Second: the issue of if the married Muslim girl reaches maturity and does not embrace Islam, then she is separated. It is mentioned in al-Muhit and others. And Allah knows best. His statement: (And if both her parents become Magians, she separates). He said in al-Nahr: There is a need for reflection on the difference between if they become Magians or apostatize. I say: The difference is clear: it is what he mentioned: that the daughter by the apostasy of her Muslim parents remains Muslim by following the parents and the land, and the apostate is treated as Muslim by being forced to Islam, unlike the case of both her Christian parents becoming Magians because she becomes a follower of them in Magianism, and her following of the land cannot exist while the following of the parents remains. It seems he thought that the pronoun in 'they apostatized' referred to the Christian parents, which is not correct. His statement: (And it is mentioned in al-Muhit and others) he said in...
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage covers several rulings. First, it presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding a Muslim man married to a Christian woman, and both become Magians (tamajjasa). Abu Yusuf holds that the marriage dissolves (taqa‘ al-furqa) because the woman's conversion to Magianism is a new form of disbelief distinct from her original Christianity, and since she changed her religion, it is considered apostasy. Since only she apostatized (the husband was already Muslim), her apostasy ends the marriage. Muhammad argues that both have effectively apostatized together (because the woman's conversion is akin to apostasy from Islam, and the man's conversion to Magianism is also apostasy from Islam), so their mutual apostasy does not dissolve the marriage. The text notes that the same ruling applies if they both become Jews: the marriage is dissolved by agreement, because conversion to Judaism does not introduce a 'new quality' of disbelief for a Christian; it is just another form. The passage then restates the ruling on sequential acceptance of Islam: if one embraces Islam and the other does later sequentially, the marriage dissolves. And if only one embraces Islam (the other remaining non-Muslim), the same applies. The mahr rules are repeated. Then follows a lengthy discussion about a minor girl with Muslim parents: if both parents apostatize together, she remains Muslim due to her following of the land and her parents' original Islam. Various scenarios are discussed: if she is taken to Dar al-Harb, etc. The passage ends with two masail: (1) if a man embraces Islam with more than four wives or two sisters, and (2) if a married Muslim girl reaches puberty and refuses Islam. The commentary then returns to the distinction between tamajjus and apostasy by parents.

Key Terms
تمجس (tamajjasa): Converting to Magianism (Zoroastrianism); for a Muslim it is riddah; for a non-Muslim it is a change within kufr but considered by some as equivalent to apostasy.
فرقة (furqa): Legal separation of the marriage contract due to apostasy or a change of religion.
ردة (riddah): Apostasy from Islam; abandoning the religion of Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of Abu Yusuf on the case where a Muslim husband and his Christian wife both become Magians?
A) The marriage dissolves.
B) The marriage remains valid.
C) It depends on whether they became Magians together.
D) The wife is considered to have apostatized from Islam.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school records an intra-madhhab dispute on whether conversion to Magianism by a Christian spouse triggers separation, reminding us of the importance of understanding the underlying definition of apostasy.

Equality in Division of Nights Among Wives
Opening ruling of the chapter on division of nights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the equality of wives in the division of nights and identify the exception for free and slave wives.

Core Idea
All wives are equal in qasm except a free wife gets twice a slave's share.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq opens the chapter on the division of nights. It lays down the foundational principle that a husband must divide his nights equally among his wives, regardless of their status. However, an important exception is made for slave wives, whose share is half that of a free wife. Understanding this ruling is essential for the detailed rules that follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the division of nights (qasm) among multiple wives. The ruling: it is wajib upon the husband to divide equally, as established in the Hanafi school.
The text does not explicitly state wujub, but it is understood from other sources.
2
List the categories of wives mentioned
The text mentions virgin/non-virgin, new/old, Muslim/Kitabiyya, and free/slave.
3
State the general principle
All categories except free/slave are treated equally: virgin like non-virgin, new like old, Muslim like Kitabiyya.
The phrase 'فيه' refers to the division.
4
Note the exception
A free wife gets twice the share of a slave wife ('وللحرة ضعف الأمة').
This is the only distinction mentioned.

كتاب النكاح باب القسم باب القسم والبكر كالثيب والجديدة كالقديمة والمسلمة كالكتابية فيه وللحرة ضعف الأمة
Book of Nikah, Chapter of Division: Chapter of Division. And the virgin is like the non-virgin, and the new wife is like the old one, and the Muslim woman is like the Kitabiyya in it, and for the free woman is twice the share of the slave woman.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This is the opening passage of the chapter on division of nights (qasm) from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It establishes the general principle that all wives are equal in the division of nights, regardless of their status: virgin or non-virgin, newly married or long married, Muslim or Kitabiyya (Jewish/Christian). However, a free wife is entitled to twice the share of a slave wife. This ruling is a concise statement of the Hanafi position on the basic rights of wives in the division of the husband's time. The phrase 'فيه' refers to the division (القسم). The ruling is straightforward and serves as a foundation for the detailed rules that follow.

Key Terms
القسم (al-qasm): The division of nights among co-wives by the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the division of nights, how does the share of a free wife compare to that of a slave wife?
A) They are equal.
B) The free wife gets twice the share.
C) The slave wife gets twice the share.
D) It depends on the husband's choice.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, all wives are equal in the division of nights except that a free wife receives twice the share of a slave wife.

The Obligation of Division Among Co-Wives: Wajib or Fard?
Commentary on the obligation of division and its degree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school classifies division among co-wives as wajib rather than fard, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on the interpretation of the Quranic text.

Core Idea
The command in the Quran 'fa-wahidah' is conditional and zanni, so division among wives is wajib (obligatory with probable evidence) not fard (certain).

In this passage, the commentator from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into a nuanced fiqh issue: the legal status of dividing time and expenses among co-wives. He navigates between the views of earlier Hanafi authorities and the Shafi'i school, clarifying that while justice in division is mandated by the Quran, the degree of obligation depends on the strength of the evidence. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the Hanafi position that division is wajib, not fard.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is the division of nights and maintenance among multiple wives. The ruling being discussed is whether this division is fard (certain obligation) or wajib (probable obligation).
The act is called al-qasm (division).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? The primary proof is from the Quran: verses 3 and 129 of Surah al-Nisa, particularly the imperative 'fa-wahidah' (marry one).
The dalil is naqli (textual).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How exactly does this dalil prove the ruling? The command 'fa-wahidah' is interpreted by Hanafis as a recommendation (nadb) due to the conditional context ('if you fear...'), not an absolute obligation. The broader command of justice in division is derived, but its evidentiary strength is zanni (probable).
The imperative's meaning is not qat'i because it is conditioned on fear.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? Yes, the Shafi'i school interprets the same verse differently: they consider the command as obligation (wujub) and interpret 'awl as many dependents rather than injustice, leading them to view division as recommended (mustahabb) rather than obligatory.
The ikhtilaf is inter-madhhab.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon and why? The Hanafi position (wajib) is preferred because the evidence is not decisive enough for fard, as the command is conditional and the linguistic interpretation of 'awl supports the Hanafi view. The commentarial tradition (e.g., al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) reaffirms this.
The mufta bihi is the wajib position.

على المراد وهذا إن أخذ من قوله تعالى «فواحدة» كما هو ظاهر كلام الفتح وإن أخذ من قوله تعالى فإن خفتم» على ما يأتي فالأمر أظهر فتدبر قوله : (وظاهره أنه إذا خاف عدم العدل يستحب أن لا يزيد الخ صرح به اندفع ما في شرح المقدسي من حمل الندب في كلام البدائع على اللغوي قوله: (وإنما المراد به التسوية بين المنكوحات لا يخفى أنه إذا وجبت عليه التسوية وتركها كان جوراً وقد قالوا يحرم التزوج عند خوف الجور Chapter of Division: Explanation of a ruling from the rulings of marriage. It is placed at the end because it only becomes necessary when there are multiple wives, and marriage does not necessitate it nor is it predominant in it. Al-qasm, with fatha on the qaf, is the masdar of qasama. In al-Qamus: al-qasm is gift, and it is not pluralized; also opinion, doubt, rain, water, and destiny. It is divided into two: with fatha when the masdar is intended, and with kasra when the portion is intended. End. What is meant here is equality among wives. The basis for it is that the husband is commanded to be just in division among women by the Book. Allah Almighty said, 'And you will never be able to do justice between women even if you are eager, so do not incline completely [to one]' (al-Nisa: 129). Its meaning is: you will not be able to be just and equal in love, so do not incline in division. Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) said that. And He said, 'And live with them honorably' (al-Nisa: 19), and its ultimate aim is division. And He said, 'And if you fear that you will not be just, then [marry] one or what your right hands possess' (al-Nisa: 3). In Fath al-Qadir: So we learn that the permissibility of four is conditional upon not fearing lack of justice, and prohibition of more than one when fear exists. Thus it is known that division is obligatory when there are multiple. End. Its apparent meaning is that if he fears lack of justice, increasing to more than one is prohibited upon him. In al-Bada'i': i.e., if you fear that you will not be just in division and maintenance in two, three, or four, then [marry] one. He is encouraged to marry one when fearing abandonment of justice in increase. And he only fears abandoning that which is obligatory, so this indicates that justice among them in division and maintenance is obligatory. End. Its apparent meaning is that if he fears lack of justice, it is recommended for him not to increase, not that it is prohibited. If it is said: It has already been stated that if he fears injustice, marriage is prohibited, so how can it be recommended? I say: Justice in the sense of avoiding injustice is not meant here because it is obligatory for the single wife. Rather, what is meant is equality among the wives, and abandoning it is only prohibited after it becomes obligatory, not marriage when one fears its absence. There is disagreement in interpreting His statement 'that is more likely that you will not do injustice' (al-Nisa: 3): i.e., restricting to one and slave women is closer to not being unjust. The majority interpreted al-'awl as injustice. It is said: 'ala al-mizan if it tilted, and 'ala al-hakim if he wronged. Al-Shafi'i interpreted it as many dependents and was refuted by the fact that if so, He would have said 'an tu'alu' because it is from a'ala yu'ilu. It was answered that it is linguistic and not objected to by others' speech, and it is established in the language that 'ala al-rajul if his expenses became many. So interpreting it as many dependents is an interpretation by necessity because many dependents necessitate many expenses. And by the hadith reported in al-Bukhari: 'Begin with yourself, then with those you support.' Thus 'marry one' can be interpreted as: the obligatory is one, or the prescribed is one, or the required is one. So it is not explicit about the obligation of marrying one; so from where is the obligation of division derived? And if we say it is a report in the meaning of a command, the command is not explicit about categorical obligation but applies to probable obligation as they clarified. This is based on it being for obligation; otherwise, it could imply recommendation, permission, etc. So it is not categorical in indication of the intended meaning. This is if taken from His statement 'fa-wahidah' as is apparent from the words of al-Fath. But if taken from His statement 'fa-in khiftum' as will come, the matter is clearer. So ponder. His statement: 'And its apparent meaning is that if he fears lack of justice, it is recommended not to increase, etc.' Al-Qahustani clarified this, saying, correcting what is in al-Khulasah and others of impermissibility, but in Sharh al-Ta'wilat, it is permissible for him. Indeed, the command in His statement 'fa-in khiftum alla ta'dilu fa-wahidah' i.e., adhere to it, is carried on recommendation, not requirement. End. And by this is refuted what was in Sharh al-Maqdisi of interpreting 'recommendation' in al-Bada'i' as linguistic. His statement: 'And what is meant is equality among wives' is not hidden: if equality is obligatory and he abandons it, it is injustice. And they said marriage is prohibited when fearing injustice. The specification here that it is prohibited after it becomes obligatory is also said in other cases, otherwise what is the difference between one injustice and another? Ponder. His statement: 'No' marriage when he fears its absence. Look at the position of this speech. Perhaps it is a conjunction.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides the commentary on the obligation of division (qasm) among co-wives. The author begins by defining qasm linguistically and technically, then cites Quranic verses that enjoin justice among wives. The key verse is 'And you will never be able to do justice between women even if you are eager, so do not incline completely [to one]' (al-Nisa: 129). This verse commands the husband to avoid complete inclination, implying that some inequality is unavoidable but that division of time and expenses must be just. The passage then discusses whether the obligation is fard (obligatory in the highest degree) or wajib (obligatory but with some flexibility). The author argues that it is not fard because the evidence is not qat'i in both transmission and meaning. The Quranic command 'marry one' (fa-wahidah) is interpreted by some as a command (amr) indicating obligation, but the Hanafi position is that it indicates recommendation (nadb) due to the context of fear of injustice. The commentary also includes a discussion from various sources (al-Nahr, Fath al-Qadir, al-Bada'i') on the interpretation of the verse 'that is more likely that you will not do injustice'. The author concludes that the division is wajib, and that fearing injustice does not forbid marrying more than one, but rather it is recommended to stick to one. The passage also includes a debate between the Hanafi and Shafi'i interpretations of the word 'awl in the verse, with the Hanafi school interpreting it as injustice (jwr) while al-Shafi'i interpreted it as many dependents. The Hanafi response is based on linguistic evidence. Finally, the author discusses the opinion of al-Qahustani and others that the command in the verse is for recommendation, not requirement, which supports the Hanafi position that division is wajib but not fard.

Key Terms
القسم (al-qasm): The division of nights among co-wives, which is wajib upon the husband.
العدل (al-adl): Justice in division of time and expenses among wives; not required in love.
العول (al-awl): Interpreted here as injustice (al-jawr) in the context of this verse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal status of dividing nights equally among co-wives?
A) Fard (obligatory with certain evidence)
B) Wajib (obligatory with probable evidence)
C) Sunnah (recommended)
D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, division among co-wives is wajib, not fard, due to the zanni nature of the evidence.

Ruling on Polygamy When Injustice is Feared
Analysis of Quranic verse on polygamy and its legal implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on polygamy when fear of injustice exists, identify the evidence from Quran 4:3, and compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i interpretations of 'awl'.

Core Idea
When injustice is feared, it is recommended (mustahabb) to marry one – not forbidden; the command is for recommendation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq examines the fiqh of polygamy in light of Quran 4:3. It addresses whether a man who fears he cannot be just among multiple wives is prohibited or merely advised to limit to one. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the obligatory nature of justice and the recommended nature of monogamy in such cases. The passage also engages a linguistic dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i over the meaning of 'awl', which has direct implications for the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is polygamy (marrying more than one wife). When a man fears inability to be just, the Hanafi ruling is that it is recommended (mustahabb) to limit to one, not haram. The obligation of justice in division and maintenance remains wajib.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The primary dalil is Quran 4:3: 'فإن خفتم ألا تعدلوا فواحدة' (if you fear that you will not be just, then [marry] one).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'فواحدة' is interpreted as a recommendation due to the conditional fear. The word 'تعولوا' is interpreted as 'incline to injustice' based on linguistic usage, not as 'have many dependents'.
The Hanafi reading emphasizes the consequence of injustice.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Fath al-Qadir suggests prohibition when fear is certain, while al-Badai' holds it is only recommended. The author sides with recommendation, citing al-Qahistani.
This is a fatawa-mutakhkhirin tarjih.
5
Analyze the cross-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i interprets 'تعولوا' as 'have many dependents' (kathrat al-iyal). The Hanafi response: the correct verb form would be 'تعيلوا' not 'تعولوا'; the Shafi'i reading is a necessary consequence (lazim), not direct.
The practical difference: Hanafi sees the verse warning against injustice, Shafi'i sees it as financial advice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(۱) رواه البخاري في كتاب الزكاة باب ۱۸ الترمذي في كتاب الزكاة باب ۳۸ النسائي في كتاب الزكاة باب ٥١، ٥٣. الدارمي في كتاب الزكاة باب ۲۱ ۲۲ أحمد في مسنده (١٥٢،٤/٢) (٢٦٢/٥).
Kitab al-Nikah. 'One or what your right hands possess' [Quran 4:3]. And in Fath al-Qadir: We derive that the permissibility of four is conditioned on the absence of fear of injustice, and the prohibition of more than one is established when fear exists, so its obligation is known when they are multiple. End. Its apparent meaning is that if one fears injustice, increasing beyond one becomes forbidden. And in al-Badai': 'If you fear that you will not be just, then one' – it is recommended to marry one when fearing failure of justice in increasing, and one only fears the omission of the obligatory, indicating that justice among them in division and maintenance is obligatory. End. Its apparent meaning is that if one fears injustice, it is recommended not to increase, not that it is forbidden. If you say: It has been stated that if one fears oppression, marriage becomes forbidden, so how can it be recommended? I say: Justice meaning avoidance of oppression is not intended here, as it is obligatory for one wife. What is intended is equality among wives, and its omission is only forbidden after it becomes obligatory, not the marriage itself if one fears its absence. And there is disagreement on the interpretation of His statement 'That is more suitable that you may not incline [to injustice]' [Quran 4:3], i.e., restricting to one and female slaves [concubines] is closer to not being unjust. The majority interpret 'awl' as injustice. It is said 'the scale tilted' meaning deviated, and 'the ruler committed injustice'. Al-Shafi'i interpreted it as many dependents, and it was responded that if so, He would have said 'an tu'elu' because it is from 'a'ala yu'ilu'. And it was answered that it is linguistic, not objected to by the speech of others, and that it is established in language 'the man became burdened' if his expenses increased. So interpreting it as many dependents is an interpretation by necessary consequence because many dependents necessitate many expenses, and by the hadith narrated in Bukhari: 'Start with yourself, then with those you support.' So 'one' may mean the obligatory is one, or the prescribed is one, or the required is one, so it is not explicit about the obligation of marrying one. So from where is the obligation of division derived? Even if we say it is a statement meaning a command, the command is not text for definitive obligation but includes probable obligation, as they stated. This is if it indicates obligation, otherwise it may indicate recommendation, permissibility, etc. So it is not definitive in meaning regarding what is intended. This is if taken from His statement 'one' as is apparent from Fath al-Qadir, but if taken from His statement 'if you fear' as will come, then the matter is clearer. So ponder. His statement: 'And its apparent meaning is that if he fears injustice, it is recommended not to increase, etc.' It was stated by al-Qahistani, correcting what is in al-Khulasah and others of impermissibility, but in Sharh al-Ta'wilat it is permissible for him, because the command in His statement 'if you fear that you will not be just, then one', i.e., adhere to it, is carried on recommendation, not obligation. End. And by this, what is in Sharh al-Maqdisi is refuted, that he carried the 'recommendation' in al-Badai's statement as linguistic. His statement: 'And what is intended is equality among wives.' It is not hidden that if equality is obligatory upon him and he abandons it, it is oppression. And they said it is forbidden to marry when fearing oppression. And the specification here that it is forbidden after it becomes obligatory may be said for others, otherwise what is the difference between one oppression and another? Ponder. His statement: 'no' - marriage if he fears its absence. See what is the position of this speech; perhaps it is a conjunction. (1) Narrated by Bukhari in Kitab al-Zakat, Bab 18; Tirmidhi in Kitab al-Zakat, Bab 38; Nasa'i in Kitab al-Zakat, Bab 51, 53; Darimi in Kitab al-Zakat, Bab 21, 22; Ahmad in his Musnad (2/152, 4/2) (5/262).
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on the ruling of polygamy, specifically on the Quranic verse 4:3. The author begins by referencing Fath al-Qadir, which states that the permissibility of up to four wives is conditional on not fearing injustice. If one fears injustice, it becomes prohibited to marry more than one. In contrast, al-Badai' interprets the same verse as a recommendation (nadb) to marry only one when fearing failure of justice, not a prohibition. The author clarifies that the justice required here is equality in division and maintenance, which is obligatory. The text then addresses an objection: if fearing oppression makes marriage forbidden, how can it be recommended? The response is that justice here means equality among wives, which is obligatory. Fearing its omission does not make the act of marriage itself forbidden; it is the omission of the obligatory that is forbidden after marriage. The author then discusses the interpretation of 'ذلك أدنى أن لا تعولوا' (that is more suitable that you may not incline). The majority of scholars interpret 'العول' as injustice, while al-Shafi'i interprets it as having many dependents. The Hanafi rebuttal is linguistic: 'عال' means to tilt or be unjust, whereas the Shafi'i interpretation requires the form 'أعال' (to have many dependents). The Shafi'i response is that the language also uses 'عال' for burden of dependents, but the Hanafi author argues that interpreting it as many dependents is an inference from consequence, not direct. The author further examines the word 'فواحدة' and concludes that it is not explicit for obligation; it may mean the obligatory is one, or the prescribed is one, or the required is one. Thus, the obligation of division is not directly derived from this verse. The command may be for recommendation. The text supports this with al-Qahistani's statement that the command in the verse is for recommendation, not obligation. Finally, the author warns against confusion between prohibiting marriage before obligation and prohibiting after obligation. The overall lesson is that the Quranic injunction regarding polygamy is primarily a recommendation to limit to one when injustice is feared, not an absolute prohibition or obligation.

Key Terms
العدل (al-`adl): Justice/equality among wives specifically in division (qasm) and maintenance (nafaqah). It is obligatory.
العول (al-`awl): Injustice or deviation from fairness, as opposed to having many dependents.
فواحدة (fa-wahidah): The phrase in Quran 4:3 meaning 'then one', interpreted as a recommendation to limit to one wife when injustice is feared.
التسوية (al-taswiyah): Equality among wives in rights and treatment, specifically in qasm and nafaqah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a man fears he cannot be just among multiple wives, what is the ruling on marrying more than one?
A) It is haram (forbidden) to marry more than one.
B) It is recommended (mustahabb) to marry only one.
C) It is wajib (obligatory) to marry only one.
D) It is makruh (disliked) to marry more than one.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the Quranic command to marry one when injustice is feared is a recommendation, not a prohibition, while justice among wives remains wajib.

Scope of Equality Among Wives (Qasm)
Defines the obligatory equality among wives in division of nights and other matters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on equality among wives, identify the disputed scope, and explain the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Equality among wives is wajib only in staying overnight (al-baytutah); other matters depend on the spouses' financial circumstances.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the scope of wajib equality among wives. While the Quran commands justice, the Sunnah specifies that the obligatory equality is in the division of nights. The Hanafi school further delineates that love and intercourse are not subject to equality, but there is ikhtilaf on whether food, clothing, and housing must be equalized. The author reconciles the differing views and affirms that all wives are equal in division regardless of status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Issue
The passage addresses the extent of wajib equality (taswiyah) among wives. Determine which aspects of marital treatment are obligatory to equalize and which are not.
The Quran commands 'adl' (justice) but leaves it ambiguous, requiring clarification from the Sunnah and scholarly consensus.
2
Locate the Primary Evidence
The Prophet's hadith 'O Allah, this is my division in what I own...' is cited to show that the obligatory equality is limited to matters within his control, i.e., overnight stays (baytutah), not love or desire.
Another hadith from Imam Ahmad threatens punishment for inclining to one wife, but does not specify the scope—hence scholars use the first hadith as the main dalil.
3
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Al-Hidayah restricts wajib equality to baytutah only, while al-Badai' extends it to food, drink, clothing, and housing. Understand the basis of each position.
The disagreement hinges on whether one considers only the husband's ability (al-Hidayah) or both spouses' circumstances (al-Badai').
4
Understand the Author's Reconciliation
The author states that the mufta bihi (relied-upon) view considers both spouses' conditions, so equality in maintenance is not absolutely required; it depends on wealth disparity.
The claimed consensus in al-Ghayah is criticized because it only applies if one considers the husband alone—which is not the preferred view.
5
Apply the Ruling to All Wives Equally
Regardless of a wife's virginity, religion, or health, the division of nights must be equal. The hadith giving a virgin seven nights is interpreted as a one-time preference at the start of marriage, not a permanent right.
This shows that the wajib equality in qasm is uniform and does not vary by the wife's attributes.

Source Text

والحاصل أن العدل في الكتاب مبهم يحتاج إلى البيان لأنه أوجبه، وصرح به بأنه مطلقاً لا يستطاع فعلم أن الواجب منه شيء معين وكذا السنة جاءت مجملة فيه، فإن قوله المروي في السنن الأربعة كان عليه السلام يقسم فيعدل ويقول : اللهم هذا قسمي فيما أملك فلا تلمني فيما تملك ولا أملك. يعني القلب أي زيادة المحبة فظاهره أن ما عداه داخل تحت ملكه وقدرته في التسوية ومنه عدد الوطات والقبلات والتسوية فيها غير لازمة بالإجماع، وكذا ما رواه الإمام أحمد من كان له امرأتان فمال إلى إحداهما جاء يوم القيامة وشقه مائل ) أي مفلوج ولم يبين فيه المراد . قال في فتح القدير : لكن لا نعلم خلافاً في أن العدل الواجب في البيتوته والتأنيس في اليوم والليلة وليس المراد أن يضبط زمان النهار فبقدر ما عاشر فيه إحداهما يعاشر الأخرى بقدره بل ذلك في البيتوتة وأما النهار ففي الجملة اهـ. والحاصل أن التسوية في المحبة لما بين الشارع سقوطها بقي ما أجمعوا عليه مراداً وهو البيتوتة، وظاهر كلامهم أن لا تجب التسوية فيما عداها ولذا قال في الهداية : والتسوية المستحقة في البيتوتة لا في المجامعة لأنه يبتني على النشاط اهـ. وفي البدائع : يجب عليه التسوية بين الحرتين أو الأمتين في المأكول والمشروب والملبوس والسكني والبيتوتة اهـ. وهكذا ذكر الولوالجي، والحق أنه على قول من اعتبر حال الرجل وحده في النفقة فالتسوية فيها واجبة أيضاً، وأما على قول المفتى به من اعتبار حالهما فلا لأن إحداهما قد تكون غنية والأخرى فقيرة فلا يلزمه التسوية بينهما مطلقاً النفقة. وفي الغاية : اتفقوا على التسوية في في الشارح : وفيه نظر فإنه في النفقة يعتبر حالهما على المختار فكيف يدعي الاتفاق فيها على التسوية ولا يتأتى ذلك إلا على قول من يعتبر حال الرجل وحده اهـ.
قال
النفقة
قوله: (والبكر كالثيب والجديدة كالقديمة والمسلمة كالكتابية فيه) أي في القسم لإطلاق ما تلونا. و ما روينا ولأن القسم من حقوق النكاح ولا تفاوت بينهما في ذلك وما روي في الحديث للبكر سبع وللثيب ثلاث وقوله عليه السلام لأم سلمة «إن شئت سبعت لك وسبعت لنسائي، وإن شئت ثلثت لك ودرت فالمراد التفضيل في البداءة بالجديدة دون الزيادة، ولا شك أن الأحاديث محتملة فلم تكن قطعية الدلالة فوجب تقديم الدليل القطعي والأحاديث المطلقة، وحينئذ فلا معنى لتردده في فتح القدير في القطعية، وكما لا فرق بين ما ذكر ومقابليهن لا فرق بين المجنونة التي لا يخاف منها والمريضة والصحيحة والرتقاء على قوله يحرم تركه والمعنى أنه يحرم تركه بعد وجوبه لا يحرم التزوج قبل وجوبه إذا خاف عدمه (۱) رواه أبو داود في كتاب النكاح باب 38 الترمذي في كتاب النكاح باب 42. الدارمي في كتاب النكاح باب 24.
And the summary is that justice in the Book is ambiguous and needs explanation because He obligated it, and He explicitly stated that absolutely it is not possible, so it is known that the obligatory from it is a specific thing. Likewise, the Sunnah came with ambiguity on it. For the Prophet's statement narrated in the four Sunan: 'He used to divide and be just and say: O Allah, this is my division in what I own, so do not blame me for what You own and I do not own.' Meaning the heart, i.e., the increase of love. So its apparent meaning is that what is other than it is within his ownership and ability regarding equality, and from that is the number of intercourses and kisses, and equality in them is not necessary by consensus. Likewise, what Imam Ahmad narrated: 'Whoever has two wives and inclines to one of them will come on the Day of Resurrection with one side leaning (i.e., paralyzed)' and it did not specify the intended. He said in Fath al-Qadir: 'But we do not know any disagreement that the obligatory justice is in staying overnight (al-baytutah) and kind treatment (al-ta'nis) during the day and night. It is not intended that he should control the time of the day so that he treats one as much as he treats the other, rather that is in staying overnight. As for the day, it is in general terms. End.' And the summary is that since the Lawgiver indicated the impossibility of equality in love, what remains that is agreed upon as intended is al-baytutah. And the apparent meaning of their statements is that equality is not obligatory beyond it. Hence, it is said in al-Hidayah: 'The deserved equality is in staying overnight, not in intercourse, because it depends on desire.' End. And in al-Badai': 'He is obligated to equalize between free women or slave women in food, drink, clothing, housing, and staying overnight.' End. And similarly, al-Walwaliji mentioned. And the truth is that according to the one who considers the husband's condition alone in maintenance, equality in it is also obligatory. But according to the relied-upon view that considers the condition of both (husband and wife), then no, because one may be rich and the other poor, so he is not absolutely obligated to equalize in maintenance. And in al-Ghayah: 'They agreed on equality in...' and in al-Sharh: 'In this there is consideration, because in maintenance their situation is considered according to the preferred view, so how can one claim agreement on equality in it? It cannot be except according to those who consider the husband's condition alone.' End.
He said: Maintenance
His statement: 'And the virgin is like the non-virgin, the new wife is like the old, the Muslim is like the Kitabiyyah in it' i.e., in division (al-qasm), due to the generality of what we recited and what we narrated. And because division is among the rights of marriage, and there is no difference between them in that. And what is narrated in the hadith: 'For the virgin, seven (nights); for the non-virgin, three' and his statement to Umm Salamah: 'If you wish, I will give you seven and give my wives seven, and if you wish, I will give you three and rotate' – the intended is preference in starting with the new wife, not an increase. There is no doubt that the hadiths are probable and not definitive in indication, so the definitive evidence and absolute hadiths must take precedence. Hence, there is no meaning for his hesitation in Fath al-Qadir regarding definitiveness. And just as there is no difference between what is mentioned and their counterparts, there is no difference between the insane woman who is not feared from (i.e., harmless), the sick, the healthy, and the one with a vaginal defect (ratqa'), according to the statement that it is forbidden to abandon it. And the meaning is that its abandonment is forbidden after its obligation, not that marriage is forbidden before its obligation if he fears its absence. (1) Narrated by Abu Dawud in Kitab al-Nikah, Bab 38; Tirmidhi in Kitab al-Nikah, Bab 42; Darimi in Kitab al-Nikah, Bab 24.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage clarifies the scope of obligatory equality among wives in the context of division of nights (al-qasm). The author begins by noting that the Quran commanded justice but left it ambiguous. The Sunnah clarifies that the obligatory justice is specifically in staying overnight (al-baytutah) and kind treatment, not in matters beyond human control like love or sexual desire. The Prophet's hadith indicates that he divided his nights equally but asked Allah not to blame him for feelings of the heart. It is agreed that equality in staying overnight is obligatory, while in sexual intercourse it is not required because it depends on desire. The author then presents a disagreement among Hanafi sources: al-Hidayah says equality is only in staying overnight, while al-Badai' extends it to food, drink, clothing, and housing. The author reconciles by stating that the scope of equality in maintenance depends on the criterion used: if we consider only the husband's wealth, then equality in maintenance is required; but the relied-upon view considers both spouses' situations, so equality is not mandatory because one wife may be rich and the other poor. The author then asserts that all wives are equal in division regardless of their status: virgin or non-virgin, new or old, Muslim or Kitabiyya. This is because division is a right of marriage that does not vary. The hadiths that give a virgin seven nights are interpreted as a special treatment for the new bride in the initial days, not a permanent increase in her share. Finally, the author notes that equality should also be observed for wives with disabilities such as insanity, illness, or vaginal defect, as long as the husband does not fear harm.

Key Terms
القسم (al-qasm): The division of nights among wives; the husband's obligation to rotate his overnight stays equally.
البيتوتة (al-baytutah): Staying overnight with a wife; the specific form of division that is obligatory.
التسوية (al-taswiyah): Equality or equal treatment among wives in the matters that are within the husband's control.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which matter is equality among wives obligatory by consensus?
A) Number of acts of sexual intercourse
B) Food and drink
C) Staying overnight (al-baytutah)
D) Love and affection

Key Takeaway
Equality among wives is wajib only in the division of nights (al-baytutah); in other matters, it is either not required or conditional on circumstances.

The Obligatory Justice in Division is Overnight Stay
Explaining the nature of obligatory justice in division among wives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on obligatory justice among co-wives, identify the specific proof from the Sunnah, and explain the intra-Hanafi divergence on maintenance equality.

Core Idea
Justice among wives is wajib only in overnight stay—love and intercourse are beyond obligation.

The Quran commands justice among co-wives but the Prophet acknowledged it is impossible in the heart. The Sunnah clarifies that the obligatory justice pertains to division of time (baytutah). In this passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author pinpoints that overnight stay is the required equality, not love or intercourse, and then examines whether maintenance must also be equal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ambiguity in the Quranic Command
The verse 'You will never be able to be just between wives' (4:129) shows absolute equality is impossible, so the wajib must be something specific. The Quran does not specify what – the Sunnah provides the detail.
2
Analyze the Prophetic Hadith (Dalil)
The hadith narrated in the four Sunan: the Prophet would divide and say, 'O Allah, this is my division in what I possess, so do not blame me in what You possess and I do not possess.' This establishes that love is not under his control, hence not required; only matters under his control (time, nights) are subject to equality.
The dalil is ahad (zanni al-thubut) which is why the ruling is wajib, not fard.
3
Extract the Rulings from Consensus and Earlier Authorities
By consensus, equality in intercourse and kissing is not required because these depend on desire. Al-Marghinani (Fath al-Qadir) says there is no disagreement that the obligatory justice is in baytutah and sociability during day and night – not precise time measurements in the day.
The Hidayah states: 'The required equality is in overnight stay, not intercourse.'
4
Examine the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf on Maintenance
According to the view that considers only the husband's financial condition, equality in maintenance is also wajib. But the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) considers both wives' conditions, so if one is rich and the other poor, unequal maintenance is permissible.
Bahr al-Ra'iq criticizes a claim of consensus on equal maintenance, since that consensus would only hold under the first view.
5
Determine the Operative Position (Mufta Bihi)
The operative ruling: equality in baytutah is wajib; equality in maintenance is not wajib when the wives have different financial circumstances. The tarjih is based on the principle that maintenance follows need.
This is the position adopted by later Hanafi authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحاصل أن العدل في الكتاب مبهم يحتاج إلى البيان لأنه أوجبه، وصرح به بأنه مطلقاً لا يستطاع فعلم أن الواجب منه شيء معين وكذا السنة جاءت مجملة فيه، فإن قوله المروي في السنن الأربعة كان عليه السلام يقسم فيعدل ويقول : اللهم هذا قسمي فيما أملك فلا تلمني فيما تملك ولا أملك. يعني القلب أي زيادة المحبة فظاهره أن ما عداه داخل تحت ملكه وقدرته في التسوية ومنه عدد الوطات والقبلات والتسوية فيها غير لازمة بالإجماع، وكذا ما رواه الإمام أحمد من كان له امرأتان فمال إلى إحداهما جاء يوم القيامة وشقه مائل ) أي مفلوج ولم يبين فيه المراد . قال في فتح القدير : لكن لا نعلم خلافاً في أن العدل الواجب في البيتوته والتأنيس في اليوم والليلة وليس المراد أن يضبط زمان النهار فبقدر ما عاشر فيه إحداهما يعاشر الأخرى بقدره بل ذلك في البيتوتة وأما النهار ففي الجملة اهـ. والحاصل أن التسوية في المحبة لما بين الشارع سقوطها بقي ما أجمعوا عليه مراداً وهو البيتوتة، وظاهر كلامهم أن لا تجب التسوية فيما عداها ولذا قال في الهداية : والتسوية المستحقة في البيتوتة لا في المجامعة لأنه يبتني على النشاط اهـ. وفي البدائع : يجب عليه التسوية بين الحرتين أو الأمتين في المأكول والمشروب والملبوس والسكني والبيتوتة اهـ. وهكذا ذكر الولوالجي، والحق أنه على قول من اعتبر حال الرجل وحده في النفقة فالتسوية فيها واجبة أيضاً، وأما على قول المفتى به من اعتبار حالهما فلا لأن إحداهما قد تكون غنية والأخرى فقيرة فلا يلزمه التسوية بينهما مطلقاً النفقة. وفي الغاية : اتفقوا على التسوية في في الشارح : وفيه نظر فإنه في النفقة يعتبر حالهما على المختار فكيف يدعي الاتفاق فيها على التسوية ولا يتأتى ذلك إلا على قول من يعتبر حال الرجل وحده اهـ.
And the conclusion is that justice (al-'adl) in the Book is ambiguous, needing clarification because He obligated it, and He stated that it is absolutely impossible, so it is known that the obligatory part is something specific. Likewise, the Sunnah came with a general reference to it. For His statement narrated in the four Sunan: 'He (peace be upon him) would divide and be just, saying: O Allah, this is my division in what I possess, so do not blame me in what You possess and I do not possess.' Meaning the heart, i.e., increase of love. So its apparent meaning is that what is beyond that falls under His possession and ability regarding equality, including the number of intercourses and kisses, and equality in them is not binding by consensus. Likewise, what Ahmad narrated: 'Whoever has two wives and inclines to one of them will come on the Day of Resurrection with his side leaning' i.e., paralyzed, and he did not specify what is meant. He said in Fath al-Qadir: But we know of no disagreement that the obligatory justice is in overnight stay and socializing in the day and night. And it is not intended that he precisely measure the daytime so that whatever time he spent with one, he spends equal with the other. Rather, that is regarding the overnight stay. As for the daytime, in general. End. And the conclusion is that since the Lawgiver indicated the impossibility of equality in love, what remains that they have agreed upon is the intended meaning, which is the overnight stay. And the apparent meaning of their statements is that equality is not required in other than that. Hence he said in al-Hidayah: The required equality is in overnight stay, not in intercourse, because it depends on desire. End. And in al-Bada'i': He must establish equality between two free women or two slave women in food, drink, clothing, housing, and overnight stay. End. And similarly, al-Walwālijī mentioned. And the truth is that according to the view that considers only the husband's condition in maintenance, equality in that is also obligatory. However, according to the relied-upon view of considering both conditions, it is not, because one of them may be rich and the other poor, so he is not obligated to establish absolute equality in maintenance. And in al-Ghayah: They agreed on equality in... In al-Sharih: There is consideration in this, because in maintenance, their conditions are considered according to the chosen view, so how can he claim agreement on equality in it? And that cannot be achieved except according to the view that considers only the husband's condition. End.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the nature of the obligatory justice ('adl) in division (qism) among wives. The author begins by noting that the Quranic command to be just is vague—Allah says 'and you will never be able to be just between wives even if you strive' (4:129), indicating that absolute equality in matters of the heart is impossible. Therefore, the obligatory justice must be something specific. The Sunnah confirms this: the Prophet (peace be upon him) would divide his time equally among wives but acknowledged that love is beyond his control. By consensus, equality in intercourse and kissing is not required because these depend on natural desire. Al-Marghinani in Fath al-Qadir states that there is no disagreement that the obligatory justice pertains to overnight stay (baytutah) and general companionship during the day and night—not precise timing of daytime activities. The author then synthesizes: since love is excluded from obligation, what remains is the agreed-upon meaning of baytutah. The ruling from al-Hidayah is that the required equality is in baytutah, not intercourse, because the latter depends on sexual desire. Al-Bada'i' adds that equality is required in food, drink, clothing, housing, and baytutah. A difference arises regarding maintenance (nafaqah): according to the view that considers only the husband's status, equality in maintenance is also obligatory; but the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) considers both wives' financial statuses, so if one is rich and the other poor, he is not obligated to give them equal amounts. The author critiques a claim of consensus on equality in maintenance, noting that such consensus could only exist under the view that looks solely at the husband. This lesson establishes that the core obligation in division is baytutah, not affection or intercourse.

Key Terms
العدل (al-'adl): The required justice/equality between co-wives, specifically in overnight stay and general companionship.
البيتوتة (al-baytutah): Overnight stay at each wife's house according to the rotation schedule.
القسم (al-qism): The division of time and nights among co-wives by the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in what aspect of marital life is the husband required to establish equality among co-wives?
A) Love and affection
B) Intercourse (jima')
C) Overnight stay (baytutah)
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The wajib justice among co-wives is confined to overnight stay; maintenance equality is not required when wives have different financial circumstances.

Equality in Division: No Distinction Between Wives
Ruling that equality in division applies to all wives regardless of status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the Hanafi school requires equal division among wives regardless of virginity, age, religion, or health, and explain why the hadith about seven nights for a virgin is interpreted as a non-obligatory privilege.

Core Idea
All wives are equal in division; the hadith about extra nights is a privilege, not an obligation.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that according to the Hanafi school, a husband must divide his nights equally among his wives, regardless of their status. The text addresses potential objections from hadith that seem to give a virgin wife more nights, and clarifies that those hadiths are open to interpretation and do not override the general principle of equality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling from the matn
The matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) states that a virgin is like a non-virgin, the new like the old, and the Muslim like the Kitabiyya in division. Identify that the ruling is wajib equality.
2
Understand the general evidence
The commentator cites general Quranic and hadith texts ('ما تلونا وما روينا') that imply equality. Note that these are considered absolute and decisive.
3
Analyze the conflicting hadith
The hadith 'للبكر سبع وللثيب ثلاث' appears to give extra nights. Understand that the Hanafi school interprets this as a one-time privilege at the start of marriage, not an ongoing obligation.
The Prophet's offer to Umm Salamah shows flexibility.
4
See how the commentator resolves the conflict
Ibn Nujaym argues that the hadiths are muhtamala (open to interpretation) and thus not qat'iyyat al-dalala (decisive in meaning). The general evidence is qat'i and must take precedence.
5
Note the scope of the ruling
The ruling applies to all wives, including the insane woman, the sick, the healthy, and the ratqa'. The only limitation is that it is not prohibited to marry before the duty arises if one fears zina.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (والبكر كالثيب والجديدة كالقديمة والمسلمة كالكتابية فيه) أي في القسم لإطلاق ما تلونا. و ما روينا ولأن القسم من حقوق النكاح ولا تفاوت بينهما في ذلك وما روي في الحديث للبكر سبع وللثيب ثلاث وقوله عليه السلام لأم سلمة «إن شئت سبعت لك وسبعت لنسائي، وإن شئت ثلثت لك ودرت فالمراد التفضيل في البداءة بالجديدة دون الزيادة، ولا شك أن الأحاديث محتملة فلم تكن قطعية الدلالة فوجب تقديم الدليل القطعي والأحاديث المطلقة، وحينئذ فلا معنى لتردده في فتح القدير في القطعية، وكما لا فرق بين ما ذكر ومقابليهن لا فرق بين المجنونة التي لا يخاف منها والمريضة والصحيحة والرتقاء على قوله يحرم تركه والمعنى أنه يحرم تركه بعد وجوبه لا يحرم التزوج قبل وجوبه إذا خاف عدمه (1) رواه أبو داود في كتاب النكاح باب ٣٨ الترمذي في كتاب النكاح باب ٤٢. الدارمي في كتاب النكاح باب ٢٤.
His statement: (And the virgin is like the non-virgin, the new like the old, the Muslim like the Kitābiyya in it) i.e., in division, due to the generality of what we have recited and what we have narrated. And because division is from the rights of marriage, and there is no disparity between them in that. And what is narrated in the hadith: 'For the virgin, seven nights; for the non-virgin, three,' and his statement (peace be upon him) to Umm Salamah: 'If you wish, I will give you seven and give my other wives seven; if you wish, I will give you three and rotate,' the intended meaning is preference in starting with the new wife, not increase. And there is no doubt that the hadiths are open to interpretation, so they are not decisive in indication (qat'iyyat al-dalala). Therefore, the decisive evidence and the absolute hadiths must take precedence. Hence, there is no meaning to his hesitation in Fath al-Qadir about decisiveness. And just as there is no difference between those mentioned and their counterparts, there is no difference between the insane woman from whom harm is not feared, the sick, the healthy, the ratqā' (with fused vagina), according to his statement: 'abandoning it is prohibited.' And the meaning is that abandoning it is prohibited after its obligation, but it is not prohibited to marry before its obligation if one fears committing it (i.e., zina).
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage comments on a line from Kanz al-Daqa'iq stating that all wives are equal in division (qism) regardless of whether they are virgin or non-virgin, newly married or old, Muslim or Kitabiyya (Jewish/Christian). The commentator (Ibn Nujaym in Bahr al-Ra'iq) provides the proof: general texts from Quran and Hadith that imply equality among all wives in marital rights. The hadith that specifies seven nights for a virgin and three for a non-virgin (reported in Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, etc.) is interpreted as referring to the initial marital gift (mahr) or a special privilege at the beginning of marriage, not to ongoing division. The Prophet's offer to Umm Salamah shows flexibility, and since these hadiths are not decisive in meaning (they are open to interpretation), the general commanding equality must take precedence. Similarly, there is no distinction between an insane wife (who is not feared to cause harm), a sick wife, a healthy one, or a ratqa' (one with a fused vagina preventing intercourse). The ruling 'abandoning it is prohibited' means that once the duty of equal division is established, it cannot be abandoned; however, it is not prohibited to marry a wife before the obligation arises if one fears zina. This lesson reinforces that the obligation of division is a general right of marriage unaffected by the wife's condition.

Key Terms
الثيب (al-thayyib): A woman who has had intercourse previously (non-virgin).
الرتقاء (al-ratqā'): A woman with a fused vagina (congenital) preventing intercourse.
البداءة (al-bidā'ah): The initial start of the marriage, when the husband begins the rotation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Give equal nights to both
C) Give the non-virgin more because she is experienced
D) It is up to the husband's preference

Key Takeaway
Equal division among wives is a wajib right unaffected by the wife's virginity, religion, or health; conflicting hadith are interpreted as non-obligatory privileges.
