Division Obligatory on All Husbands: Impotent, Eunuch, and Minor
Ruling that division applies to all husbands regardless of sexual ability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that division (qism) is wajib on all husbands regardless of sexual ability and apply the Hanafi reasoning that the basis is companionship, not intercourse.

Core Idea
Division is wajib for all husbands because its purpose is companionship, not sexual intercourse.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes a key Hanafi principle: the obligation of dividing one's time among multiple wives rests on the need for companionship (al-mu'anasa), not on the ability to perform intercourse. Therefore, husbands who are impotent, eunuchs, or even minors who have consummated marriage are equally obligated. The text also addresses special cases and the guardian’s role for minor husbands, as well as additional etiquettes of cohabitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle
Read the opening statement: 'وجوب القسم إنما هو للصحة والمؤانسة دون المجامعة'. Understand that the 'illah (effective cause) for division is companionship, not intercourse.
This is key to the whole lesson.
2
Apply the principle to atypical husbands
The text then applies this principle to the majbub (castrated), 'innin (impotent), and khasiy (eunuch), declaring them equal to a normal husband (al-fahl) in obligation.
This is a qiyas: the 'illah (companionship) exists in them, so the ruling applies.
3
Consider the minor husband
The minor (al-sabi) is also obligated if he has consummated marriage (dakhala). The text notes that rights of people (huquq al-'ibad) apply to minors when the cause (sabab) is established.
Consummation here establishes the cause for division.
4
Examine the cross-madhhab note on Malik
The author mentions that Imam Malik holds that the guardian of a minor should rotate him among his wives. The Hanafi author notes that this view does not seem to be based on evidence known to Hanafis.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position stands on its own evidence.
5
Understand the supplementary rules
The passage ends with rules from al-Jawhara: no intercourse on another wife's day, no night visits without a share, but permissible daytime visits, and staying with a severely ill wife until recovery/death.
These regulate the practical implementation of division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحيث علم أن وجوب القسم إنما هو للصحة والمؤانسة دون المجامعة فلا فرق بين زوج وزوج فالمجبوب والعنين والخصي كالفحل، وكذا الصبي إذا دخل بامرأتيه لأن وجوبه لحق النساء وحقوق العباد تتوجه على الصبيان عند تقرر السبب. وفي فتح القدير : وقال مالك ويدور ولي الصبي به على نسائه فظاهره أنه لم يطلع فيه على شيء عندنا، وإذا قلنا بوجوبه على الصبي وتركه فهل يأثم الولي إذا لم يأمره بذلك ولم يدر به أن يأثم. وفي المحيط : وإن لم يدخل الصغير بها فلا فائدة في كونه معها اهـ. وظاهره أن القسم على البالغ لغير المدخول بها لأن في كونه معها فائدة ولذا إنما قيدوا بالدخول في امرأة الصبي. وفي الجوهرة ولا يجامع المرأة في غير يومها ولا يدخل بالليل على التي لا قسم لها، ولا بأس بأن يدخل عليها بالنهار لحاجة ويعودها في مرضها في ليلة غيرها، فإن ثقل مرضها فلا بأس بأن يقيم عندها حتى تشفى أو تموت .اهـ.
And since it is known that the obligation of division is only for companionship and solace, not for intercourse, there is no difference between one husband and another. So the impotent, the impotent (by disease), and the eunuch are like the virile man. Likewise, the minor boy if he has had intercourse with both his wives, because its obligation is for the rights of women, and the rights of people apply to minors when the cause is established. And in Fath al-Qadir: Malik said, and the guardian of the minor should rotate him among his wives. So it appears that he did not come across anything with us. And if we rule that it is obligatory upon the minor and he abandons it, does the guardian sin if he does not order him to do it and does not rotate him? In al-Muhit: If the minor has not had intercourse with her, there is no benefit in his being with her. End. So it appears that division is upon the adult for the non-consummated wife because there is benefit in his being with her. That is why they restricted it by consummation in the case of the minor's wife. And in al-Jawhara: He should not have intercourse with a woman on a day not belonging to her, and he should not enter upon the one who has no share at night. But there is no harm in entering upon her during the day for a need and visiting her in her illness on a night belonging to another. If her illness becomes severe, there is no harm in staying with her until she recovers or dies. End.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage discusses the extent of the obligation of division (qism) in relation to the husband's ability to perform intercourse. Since the purpose of division is companionship (uns) and solace (mu'anasa), not intercourse (mujama'a), the obligation falls on all husbands equally: the majbub (castrated), the 'innin (impotent due to disease), the khasiy (eunuch) are all like a normal man. Similarly, a minor husband who has consummated his marriage with both wives is obligated to divide his time because rights of people are established when the cause is present, even for minors, though enforcement may be through the guardian. The text from Fath al-Qadir mentions that Imam Malik held that the guardian of a minor should rotate him; the Hanafi author notes that Imam Malik's view appears not to be based on evidence known to Hanafis. A detailed discussion follows: if a minor husband abandons division, does his guardian sin for not ordering him? Also, if the minor has not consummated the marriage, there is no benefit in his staying with the wife, so division is not obligatory. For an adult husband, division is required even for a non-consummated wife because companionship is beneficial. Additional rules from al-Jawhara: the husband must not have intercourse with a wife on another's day; he must not visit a wife at night if she has no share, but daytime visits for a need are fine. Visiting a sick wife during her illness on another's night is permissible, and if her illness becomes severe, he may stay with her until recovery or death. This lesson clarifies that the obligation of division is independent of sexual ability and depends on companionship.

Key Terms
المجبوب (al-majbūb): A man who has been castrated (genitals removed).
العنين (al-'innīn): A man impotent due to a chronic condition.
المؤانسة (al-mu'ānasa): Socializing and providing companionship.
الخصي (al-khasiy): A eunuch (testicles removed).
القسم (al-qism): The division of nights among co-wives.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because he must compensate with extra financial support.
B) Because the obligation is for companionship, not intercourse.
C) Because his wives have a right to children.
D) Because impotence does not affect his marital duties in any way.

Key Takeaway
Division among wives is wajib for all husbands, regardless of sexual ability, because its purpose is companionship.

Duration of the Division Cycle: Discretion and Limits
Ruling on the duration of the division cycle with talil proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the duration of the division cycle and apply the maximum limit of four months.

Core Idea
The husband may choose the cycle length, but it cannot exceed four months to avoid harm.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a practical question in polygamy: how long can a husband make his rotation cycle? Al-Hidayah grants the husband full discretion, but later authorities like Fath al-Qadir impose a limit to prevent harm. Understanding this tension between discretion and limitation is key to applying the ruling correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the general rule: the husband may choose the cycle length because what is required is equality, not a specific method.
From al-Hidayah.
2
Examine the proof
The proof is talil (reasoning): the purpose of division is companionship and warding off loneliness; an excessively long cycle defeats this purpose.
Analogy to ila' (four months) is used to set a limit.
3
Analyze the qualification
Fath al-Qadir argues that the cycle cannot be a year; the maximum should be the period of ila' (four months). Even a week may be harmful without consent.
4
Evaluate the dispute
There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: absolute discretion (al-Hidayah) vs. restricted to near periods (Fath al-Qadir). The commentator prefers the absolute view but notes the qualification.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling is that the cycle should not exceed four months unless agreed; a week is a safe recommendation to avoid harm.
Later authorities adopt the restriction as a precaution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الهداية : والاختيار في مقدار الدور إلى الزوج لأن المستحق هو التسوية دون طريقه .اهـ. وفي فتح القدير : واعلم أن هذا الإطلاق لا يمكن اعتباره على صرافته فإنه لو أراد أن يدور سنة سنة ما يظن إطلاق ذلك له بل لا ينبغي له أن يطلق له مقدار مدة الإيلاء وهو أربعة أشهر، وإذا كان وجوبه للتأنيس ودفع الوحشة وجب أن تعتبر المدة القريبة وأظن أكثر من جمعة مضارة إلا أن يرضيا به اهـ . والظاهر الإطلاق لأنه لا مضارة حيث كان على وجه القسم لأنها مطمئنة بمجيء نوبتها والحق له في البداءة بمن شاء. وحيث علم أن الوطء لا يدخل تحت القسم فهل هو واجب للزوجة؟
And in al-Hidayah: The choice in the measure of the cycle is for the husband, because the required is equality, not the method. End. And in Fath al-Qadir: Know that this absolute statement cannot be taken at face value; if he intended to rotate year by year, it is not considered permissible for him. Rather, he should not be given more than the period of ila' (vow of abstinence), which is four months. And since its obligation is for companionship and warding off loneliness, a short period must be considered. I think more than a week is harmful unless they agree to it. End. And the apparent view is that it is absolute because there is no harm when it is done as division, as she is assured of her turn, and he has the right to start with whomever he wishes. And since it is known that intercourse is not included in division, is it obligatory for the wife?
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses the duration of the division cycle (dawr). Al-Hidayah states that the choice of the cycle length is up to the husband, because what is required is equality in turn-taking, not the specific method. However, Fath al-Qadir qualifies this: the husband cannot set an excessively long cycle, like one year; the maximum should be the period of ila' (four months), because longer would defeat the purpose of companionship and cause harm. The author of Fath al-Qadir suggests that even more than a week might be harmful unless the wives agree. The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) then notes that the apparent view is that the husband's choice is unrestricted because there is no harm as long as it is a proper division—wives are content knowing their turn will come. The husband also has the right to start with whichever wife he chooses. At the end, the text transitions to a new question: since intercourse is not included in division, is it nevertheless an obligation upon the husband towards the wife? This lesson shows the tension between the husband's discretion and the need to avoid marital harm.

Key Terms
الدور (al-dawr): The cycle of rotation among wives in division.
الإيلاء (al-īlā'): A vow of abstinence from intercourse for four months or more.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the maximum length of a division cycle according to Fath al-Qadir?
A) One year
B) Four months
C) One week
D) No limit

Key Takeaway
The division cycle must be short enough to preserve the purpose of companionship; the maximum is four months.

Obligation of Sexual Intercourse on the Husband
Ruling on obligation of intercourse with enforceability distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the obligation of sexual intercourse and distinguish between its judicial enforceability and religious obligation.

Core Idea
Intercourse is the wife's right: one instance is judicially enforceable; more is between him and Allah.

This lesson examines a nuanced area of Hanafi marital law: the husband's obligation to have sexual intercourse. While the wife has a right to demand intimacy, the school distinguishes between what a judge can enforce and what is purely a religious duty. The passage clarifies that only one instance can be compelled in court; beyond that, the husband's sexual desire governs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
Intercourse (wat') is not part of division of nights (qism); it is a separate right of the wife.
2
State the hukm level
Upon the wife's demand, intercourse becomes wajib (obligatory) on the husband.
This is the general ruling; enforceability varies.
3
Distinguish enforceability
Judicial enforcement is limited to one instance. Additional instances are obligatory only between the husband and Allah (religiously), but the judge cannot compel them.
The limit is due to dependence on the husband's sexual desire.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars hold that multiple instances are also judicially enforceable, but the mufta bihi is the first view.
Al-Bada'i' presents both views; the author leans toward the limitation to once.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحيث علم أن الوطء لا يدخل تحت القسم فهل هو واجب للزوجة؟ وفي البدائع : وللزوجة أن تطالب زوجها بالوطء لأن حله لها حقها كما أن حلها له حقه. وإذا طلبته يجب على الزوج ويجبر عليه في الحكم مرة واحدة والزيادة على ذلك تجب فيما بينه وبين الله تعالى، ولا تجب عليه في الحكم عند بعض أصحابنا، وعند بعضهم تجب عليه في الحكم اهـ. ولم يبين حد الزيادة على المرة ولا يمكن أن يقال كلما طلبت لأنه موقوف على شهوته .لها. وفي فتح القدير : ويجب عليه وطؤها أحياناً. وفي المعراج : ولو أقام إحداهما شهراً فخاصمته الأخرى في ذلك قضى عليه أن يستقبل العدل بينهما وما مضى هدر غير أنه أثم فيه لأن القسمة تكون فيه بعد الطلب، ولو عاد بعد ما نهاه القاضي أوجعه عقوبة.
And since it is known that intercourse is not included under division, is it obligatory for the wife? In al-Bada'i': The wife may demand intercourse from her husband because his right of access to her is her right, just as her access to him is his right. If she demands it, it becomes obligatory upon the husband and he is compelled to it judicially once. As for more than that, it is obligatory between him and Allah Almighty, but not judicially according to some of our companions; according to others, it is judicially obligatory. End. And the limit beyond once is not specified, nor can it be said that it is whenever she demands because it depends on his desire. In Fath al-Qadir: He must have intercourse with her occasionally. And in al-Mi'raj: If he stays with one wife for a month and the other complains, the judge rules that he should re-establish justice between them from that point onward, and what passed is disregarded, except that he sinned. Because division occurs after demand. If he repeats after the judge forbade him, the judge punishes him.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This final passage addresses a key question: Is sexual intercourse (wat') an obligation on the husband towards his wife? The author first states that intercourse is not part of division (qism), so its obligation is separate. Al-Bada'i' explains that the wife has the right to demand intercourse, because the husband's access to her is also her right. If she demands, the husband must comply and is judicially compelled for one instance. Increase beyond one is obligatory religiously (between him and Allah), but there is a difference of opinion among the Hanafi jurists: some say it is also judicially obligatory (i.e., the judge can enforce), others say not. The text notes that the frequency beyond once cannot be specified because it depends on his sexual desire. Fath al-Qadir states that he must have intercourse with her 'occasionally' (aḥyanan). Al-Mi'raj provides a scenario: if a husband neglects one wife for a month and the other complains, the judge orders him to re-establish equality from that point on; the past is disregarded but he is guilty of sin. If he repeats after the judge's prohibition, the judge may punish him. This lesson shows that while intercourse is not part of the rotation schedule, it remains a conjugal right that may be enforced judicially at least minimally.

Key Terms
الوطء (al-wat'): Sexual intercourse between husband and wife.
الحكم (al-hukm): Judicial enforcement by the qadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many times can a wife judicially compel her husband to have intercourse, according to the Hanafi school?
A) As many times as she demands
B) Only once
C) Four times a month
D) Not at all

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school obligates the husband to have intercourse once upon demand, with judicial enforceability; further instances are a religious duty but not court-compellable due to dependence on the husband's desire.

Categories of Women Not Entitled to Division (Qasm)
Categorizes women not entitled to division and clarifies the basis of qasm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which women are not entitled to division and explain the underlying basis that division is for companionship, not intercourse.

Core Idea
Division is for companionship, not intercourse; thus, physical defects of the husband do not affect the obligation.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author lists various categories of women who lose their right to division (qasm). Understanding these exceptions clarifies the purpose of division: it is meant to provide comfort and companionship, not merely sexual access. This principle also explains why a husband's impotence or castration does not absolve him from dividing his time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories
Scan the list: menstruating, postpartum, minor cohabitable, in ihram, under dhihar, and their counterparts. Note that these women are not entitled to qasm.
2
Understand the exceptions
Explain why each category is excluded (e.g., impurity, incapacity, contractual barrier). For example, a woman in ihram is prohibited from conjugal relations, but division is still for companionship; however, she is excluded because the purpose cannot be fully achieved? Actually, the passage does not give reasons; it just lists. We can infer temporary impediments.
The passage does not elaborate on reasons, but the basis of companionship suggests that these women are not in a state to receive companionship normally.
3
Recognize the rebellious wife
Nashiza loses right due to disobedience. She has no right to division.
4
Apply the basis of division
Since it is for health and companionship (al-sihha wa al-mu'anasa), not cohabitation, physical conditions of the husband (majbub, 'annin, khasi) do not cancel the obligation.
This is a key principle that distinguishes Hanafi view.
5
Consider the minor husband
If he has consummated, division is obligatory because the cause (rights of women) is established. If not consummated, there is no benefit.
The passage from al-Muhit clarifies this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحائض والنفساء والصغيرة التي يمكن وطؤها والمحرمة والمظاهر منها ومقابلاتهن، وأما المطلقة رجعياً فإن قصد رجعتها قسم لها وإلا لا كما في البدائع من باب الرجعة. وأما الناشزة فلا حق لها في القسم. وحيث علم أن وجوب القسم إنما هو للصحة والمؤانسة دون المجامعة فلا فرق بين زوج وزوج فالمجبوب والعنين والخصي كالفحل، وكذا الصبي إذا دخل بامرأتيه لأن وجوبه لحق النساء وحقوق العباد تتوجه على الصبيان عند تقرر السبب. وفي فتح القدير: وقال مالك ويدور ولي الصبي به على نسائه فظاهره أنه لم يطلع فيه على شيء عندنا، وإذا قلنا بوجوبه على الصبي وتركه فهل يأثم الولي إذا لم يأمره بذلك ولم يدر به أن يأثم. وفي المحيط: وإن لم يدخل الصغير بها فلا فائدة في كونه معها اهـ. وظاهره أن القسم على البالغ لغير المدخول بها لأن في كونه معها فائدة ولذا إنما قيدوا بالدخول في امرأة الصبي. وفي الجوهرة ولا يجامع المرأة في غير يومها ولا يدخل بالليل على التي لا قسم لها، ولا بأس بأن يدخل عليها بالنهار لحاجة ويعودها في مرضها في ليلة غيرها، فإن ثقل مرضها فلا بأس بأن يقيم عندها حتى تشفى أو تموت. اهـ. وفي الهداية: والاختيار في مقدار الدور إلى الزوج لأن المستحق هو التسوية دون طريقه. اهـ. وفي فتح القدير: واعلم أن هذا الإطلاق لا يمكن اعتباره على صرافته فإنه لو أراد أن يدور سنة سنة ما يظن إطلاق ذلك له بل لا ينبغي له أن يطلق له مقدار مدة الإيلاء وهو أربعة أشهر، وإذا كان وجوبه للتأنيس ودفع الوحشة وجب أن تعتبر المدة القريبة وأظن أكثر من جمعة مضارة إلا أن يرضيا به. اهـ. والظاهر الإطلاق لأنه لا مضارة حيث كان على وجه القسم لأنها مطمئنة بمجيء نوبتها والحق له في البداءة بمن شاء.
The menstruating woman, the postpartum woman, the minor female who can be cohabited, the woman in ihram, the woman under dhihar, and their counterparts. As for the revocably divorced woman, if he intends to take her back, she gets division, otherwise not, as in al-Bada'i' from the chapter on return. As for the rebellious woman, she has no right to division. Since it is known that the obligation of division is only for health and companionship, not cohabitation, there is no difference between a husband and a husband: the emasculated, the impotent, and the castrated are like the virile. Likewise, the minor if he has consummated with his two wives, because its obligation is for the rights of women, and the rights of servants are directed upon minors when the cause is established. In Fath al-Qadir: Malik said that the guardian of a minor should rotate with him among his wives, apparently he did not see anything definitive according to us. If we say it is obligatory upon the minor and he leaves it, is the guardian sinful if he does not order him to do so and does not rotate with him? In al-Muhit: If the minor has not consummated with her, there is no benefit in his being with her. Apparently, the division is upon the adult for the non-consummated wife because there is benefit in his being with her, and therefore they only restricted to consummation in the case of the minor's wife. In al-Jawhara: He should not cohabit with a woman on other than her day, nor enter at night upon those who have no division, but there is no harm in entering upon her during the day for a need or visiting her in her illness on another's night. If her illness becomes serious, there is no harm in staying with her until she recovers or dies. In al-Hidaya: The choice in the amount of rotation is for the husband, because what is entitled is equality, not the method. In Fath al-Qadir: Know that this absolute application cannot be considered literally, for if he wanted to rotate year by year, it is not thought that such is allowed for him, but rather he should not be given more than the period of ila' which is four months. Since its obligation is for comfort and repelling loneliness, the near period should be considered, and I think more than a week with harm, unless they agree. The apparent is the absolute because there is no harm when it is in the manner of division, for she is reassured by the arrival of her turn, and he has the right to begin with whomever he wishes.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary expanding on the rules of division (qasm) among wives. It first lists categories of women who are not entitled to division: menstruating, postpartum, minor who can be cohabited, woman in ihram, woman under dhihar, and their equivalents. The divorced wife in revocable divorce gets division only if the husband intends to take her back; otherwise, she does not. A rebellious wife (nashiza) loses her right. The basis of division is health and companionship, not intercourse, so physical defects of the husband (such as emasculation, impotence, castration) do not affect the obligation. A minor husband who has consummated his marriage is also obligated because the rights of people are established upon minors when the cause is present. The passage then discusses the duration of division: the choice is with the husband, but it must not be harmful. Some scholars suggest a maximum of four months (like ila) or a week without consent, but the apparent view is that he may choose freely as long as there is no harm, because the wife is assured by the rotation.

Key Terms
القسم (al-qasm): The division of time and companionship among wives equally.
الناشزة (al-nashiza): A wife who is rebellious or disobedient to her husband without legitimate reason.
المجبوب (al-majbub): A man who has been castrated (testicles removed or damaged).
العنين (al-'annin): A man who is impotent (unable to have intercourse).
الخصي (al-khasi): A man who has been castrated (testicles removed).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following women is NOT entitled to division according to the passage?
A) A woman who is menstruating
B) A woman who is in ihram
C) A woman who is rebellious
D) All of the above are not entitled

Key Takeaway
The obligation of division is based on companionship, not sexual access, so physical defects do not exempt the husband, and certain temporary states exclude the wife from the right.

Duration and Discretion in Division Among Wives
Discusses duration of division and husband's discretion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the duration of division and explain the husband's discretion within the limits of no harm.

Core Idea
The husband chooses the rotation period, but prolonged absence without consent may be harmful.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq also addresses how long the husband can delay before rotating to another wife. The Hanafi school gives the husband considerable flexibility, but later scholars cautioned against excessive periods that cause harm. Understanding this balance is key to applying the rule justly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule from al-Hidaya
Al-Hidaya states: 'The choice in the amount of rotation is for the husband, because what is entitled is equality, not the method.' This gives the husband discretion.
2
Apply the limitation from Fath al-Qadir
Fath al-Qadir argues that absolute discretion cannot be taken literally. If he wanted to rotate year by year, that would not be allowed. The maximum should be the period of ila (four months), and a week without consent is harmful unless they agree.
Ila is a vow of abstention from intercourse for four months.
3
Understand the dissenting view of Malik
Malik is cited as saying the guardian of a minor should rotate with him among his wives. The passage notes that Malik did not see anything definitive according to us (Hanafis), implying difference.
4
Synthesize the mufta bihi
The apparent view (al-zahir) is absolute discretion because there is no harm when the wife is assured by her turn. The husband may begin with whomever he wishes.
This is the relied-upon position according to the passage.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the maximum period suggested by Fath al-Qadir for rotation without harm?
A) One year
B) Four months (the period of ila)

The husband has discretion in setting the rotation period, but it must not be so long as to cause harm; the maximum suggested by later scholars is four months without consent.

Obligation of Intercourse (Wat') in Marriage
Ruling on the obligation of intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the obligation of intercourse and distinguish between judicial enforceability and religious duty.

Core Idea
Intercourse is a separate right: once is judicially enforceable; more is between him and God.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies that intercourse (wat') is not part of the division of nights; it is an independent marital right. The Hanafi school holds that the wife may demand intercourse once, and the husband must comply judicially. Additional times are recommended but not enforceable in court, though some Hanafi scholars disagree. Understanding this distinction between legal obligation and religious duty is key to grasping the balance of spousal rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Is it obligatory, recommended, or something else? Determine the hukm level.
Watch for the phrase 'يجب على الزوج ويجبر عليه في الحكم مرة واحدة'.
2
Distinguish between judicial obligation and religious duty
The text states that once is judicially enforceable, but additional times are only obligatory 'between him and God.' Note the ikhtilaf among Hanafi scholars on whether additional times are also enforceable.
Some companions say they are judicially obligatory; others say not.
3
Examine the limit of the obligation
Why can't it be said that the husband must comply every time the wife asks? Because it depends on his desire. This sets a practical limit.
The right is not unlimited; it is tied to the husband's ability.
4
Note the separate ruling from Fath al-Qadir
The citation from Fath al-Qadir adds that he must have intercourse 'from time to time' (أحياناً), which reinforces a regular but not continuous duty.
This is consistent with the once requirement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحيث علم أن الوطء لا يدخل تحت القسم فهل هو واجب للزوجة؟ وفي البدائع: وللزوجة أن تطالب زوجها بالوطء لأن حله لها حقها كما أن حلها له حقه. وإذا طلبته يجب على الزوج ويجبر عليه في الحكم مرة واحدة والزيادة على ذلك تجب فيما بينه وبين الله تعالى، ولا تجب عليه في الحكم عند بعض أصحابنا، وعند بعضهم تجب عليه في الحكم. اهـ. ولم يبين حد الزيادة على المرة ولا يمكن أن يقال كلما طلبت لأنه موقوف على شهوته. لها. وفي فتح القدير: ويجب عليه وطؤها أحياناً. وفي المعراج: ولو أقام إحداهما شهراً فخاصمته الأخرى في ذلك قضى عليه أن يستقبل العدل بينهما وما مضى هدر غير أنه أثم فيه لأن القسمة تكون فيه بعد الطلب، ولو عاد بعد ما نهاه القاضي أوجعه عقوبة وأمره بالعدل لأنه أساء الأدب وارتكب ما هو حرام عليه وهو الجور فيعزر في ذلك. اهـ. وحاصله أنه لا يعزر في المرة الأولى وإذا عزر فتعزيره بالضرب. وفي الجوهرة: لا يعزر بالحبس لأنه لا يستدرك الحق فيه بالحبس لأنه يفوت بمضي الزمان. اهـ. وهذا مستثنى من قولهم إن للقاضي الخيار في التعزير بين الضرب والحبس. قوله: (وللحرة ضعف الأمة يعني إذا كان له زوجتان حرة وأمة فللحرة الثلثان من القسم وللأمة الثلث، بذلك ورد الأثر عن علي رضي الله عنه، ولأن حل الأمة انقص من حل الحرة فلا بد من إظهار النقصان في الحقوق. وأطلقها فشمل المكاتبة والمدبرة وأم الولد والمبعضة لأن الرق فيهن قائم. وفي البدائع: وهذا التفاوت في السكنى والبيتوتة، فأما في المأكول والمشروب والملبوس فإنه يسوي بينهما لأن ذلك من الحاجات اللازمة، وقدمنا أنه مبني على اعتبار حاله، أما على اعتبار حالهما فلا وفي المعراج لو أقام عند امرأته الأمة يوماً ثم أعتقت لم يقم عند الحرة إلا يوماً واحداً لاستوائهما في سبب الاستحقاق، وتجعل حريتها عند انتهاء النوبة بمنزلة حريتها عند ابتداء النوبة، وكذا لو أقام عند حرة يوماً ثم أعتقت الأمة تحول عنها إلى المعتقة لما ذكرنا. اهـ. قوله: (ويسافر بما شاء منهن والقرعة أحب) لأنه قد يثق بإحداهما في السفر وبالأخرى في الحضر والقرار في المنزل لحفظ الأمتعة أو لخوف الفتنة، أو يمنع من سفر إحداهما كثرة سمنها فتعيين من يخاف صحبتها في السفر لخروج قرعتها إلزام للضرر الشديد وهو مندفع بالمنافي للحرج، وأما ما رواه الجماعة من قرعته بينهن إذا أراد سفراً فكان للاستحباب تطييباً لقلوبهن لأن مطلق الفعل لا يقتضي الوجوب فكيف وهو محفوف بما يدل على الاستحباب من عدم وجوب القسم عليه لقوله تعالى: {ترجي من تشاء منهن وتؤوي إليك من تشاء} [الأحزاب: ٥١] وكان ممن أرجاهن سودة وجويرية وأم حبيبة وصفية وميمونة، وممن آوى عائشة والباقيات رضي الله عنهن أجمعين. قال القاضي في تفسيره: ترجي من تشاء منهن تؤخرها وتترك مضاجعتها، وتؤوي من تشاء تضم إليك وتضاجعها، أو تطلق من تشاء وتمسك من تشاء، ومن ابتغيت أي طلبت ممن عزلت طلقت بالرجع فلا جناح عليك في شيء من ذلك. اهـ. قيد بالسفر لأن مرضه لا يسقط القسم عنه وقد صح أنه عليه السلام لما مرض استأذن نساءه أن يمرض في بيت عائشة رضي الله عنها فأذن له، ولم أر كيفية قسمه في مرضه إذا كان لا يستطيع التحول إلى بيت
And since it is known that intercourse does not fall under the division, is it obligatory for the wife? In al-Bada'i': The wife may demand intercourse from her husband because his being lawful for her is her right, just as her being lawful for him is his right. If she demands it, it becomes obligatory upon the husband, and he is compelled judicially once, and additional times are obligatory between him and God Almighty, and are not obligatory upon him judicially according to some of our companions, and according to some they are obligatory judicially. He did not specify the limit of the additional times, and it cannot be said every time she asks because it depends on his desire. In Fath al-Qadir: He must have intercourse with her from time to time. In al-Mi'raj: If he stays with one of them for a month and the other litigates about that, the judge rules that he must start equality between them from then on, and what passed is nullified, but he is sinful in it because the division comes after demand. If he returns after the judge forbids him, the judge may inflict a painful punishment and order him to be just because he has misbehaved and committed what is forbidden to him, i.e., injustice, so he is punished. In al-Jawhara: He is not punished by imprisonment because he cannot recover the right through imprisonment since it is lost with the passage of time. This is excepted from their statement that the judge has the option in punishment between beating and imprisonment. His statement: 'And the free wife has double of the slave wife' means that if he has two wives, a free and a slave, the free has two-thirds of the division and the slave one-third; by this an effect (athar) has been narrated from Ali, and because the status of the slave is less than that of the free, so the deficiency must be shown in rights. It is general and includes the mukataba, mudabbara, umm walad, and partially free because slavery subsists in them. In al-Bada'i': This disparity is for lodging and sleeping; as for food, drink, clothing, he equalizes between them because that is from necessary needs. And we presented that it is based on considering his state; but considering their state, it is not. In al-Mi'raj: If he stays with his slave wife for a day then she is freed, he does not stay with the free wife except for one day, because they are equal in the cause of entitlement, and her freedom at the end of the turn is like her freedom at the beginning of the turn. Similarly, if he stays with a free wife for a day then the slave is freed, he turns from her to the freed one for the reason we mentioned. His statement: 'And he travels with whomever he wishes among them, and drawing lots is more beloved' because he may trust one of them in travel and the other in residence and staying home to guard luggage or for fear of fitna, or the travel of one may be prevented by her excessive fatness, so specifying the one whose companionship is feared in travel by her lot coming out is imposing severe harm, which is repelled by what contradicts hardship. As for what the group narrated about his drawing lots among them when he intended to travel, it was for istihbab (recommendation) to please their hearts, because the mere act does not require obligation, especially since it is accompanied by what indicates recommendation from the absence of obligation of division upon him due to His saying: 'You may delay whom you will of them and take to yourself whom you will' [33:51]. And among those he delayed were Sawda, Juwayriyya, Umm Habiba, Safiyya, and Maymuna, and among those he took were 'Aisha and the rest, may God be pleased with them all. Al-Qadi said in his commentary: 'You may delay whom you will of them—you postpone her and leave off sleeping with her, and take to yourself whom you will—you take to yourself and sleep with her, or you divorce whom you will and you keep whom you will, and whom you seek—whom you desire among those you have set aside—you may take back by revocable divorce, so there is no blame upon you in any of that.' It is restricted to travel because his illness does not drop the division from him, and it is established that when he became ill, he sought permission from his wives to be nursed in 'Aisha's house, and they permitted him. I have not seen how his division was in his illness when he could not move to a house
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on division (qasm) and addresses several related issues. First, it clarifies that intercourse (wat') is not part of the division; it is a separate right of the wife. She can demand it once, and the husband must comply judicially; additional times are between him and God, but some Hanafi scholars say they are also enforceable. If a husband stays with one wife for a month without justification, the judge orders him to start afresh with equality, and the past days are not compensated; he is sinful. If he repeats the offense, the judge may punish him by beating (ta'zir) but not imprisonment because the right cannot be recovered that way. Then the passage addresses the division when one wife is free and the other is a slave: the free wife gets two-thirds of the nights and the slave one-third, based on a tradition from Ali and because the slave's right is weaker. This disparity applies only to lodging and sleeping; food, drink, and clothing are given equally. If a slave wife is freed during the rotation, the rules adjust accordingly. Finally, it discusses traveling: the husband may take any wife he wishes, but drawing lots is recommended (mustahabb) to avoid partiality, as evidenced by the Prophet's practice and the Quranic verse giving him the choice. This is restricted to travel because illness does not suspend the division; the Prophet sought permission from his wives when he was ill.

Key Terms
الوطء (al-wat'): Sexual intercourse; a separate right of the wife not included in the division of nights.
التعزير (al-ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for acts that are sinful but have no fixed penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the judicial consequence if a husband refuses intercourse after his wife demands it once?
A) He is imprisoned until he complies.
B) He is compelled once; additional refusals are not judicially actionable.
C) He must be divorced.
D) He is fined.

Key Takeaway
Intercourse is a separate right: once is judicially enforceable; more is religiously recommended but not court-compelled.

Enforcing Division Equality and Ta'zir for Violation
Ruling on enforcement of equal division and ta'zir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the judge's role in enforcing equal division among wives and state the punishment for violation (ta'zir by beating, not imprisonment).

Core Idea
Equal division among wives is enforced by the judge; a violator is punished by beating, not imprisonment.

This passage discusses what happens when a husband violates the obligation of equal division among his wives. If he stays with one wife for a month without justification, the judge orders him to start fresh with equality, and the past days are forfeit. If he repeats the offense after being warned, the judge may impose a discretionary punishment (ta'zir) by beating, not imprisonment, because the right is time-sensitive and cannot be recovered through detention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the violation
What did the husband do? He stayed with one wife for a month, and the other wife complained.
The act is a violation of equal division (qasm).
2
Determine the judge's ruling on the past
The judge does not compensate the past days; they are lost. He orders the husband to start equality from now. The husband is sinful for the past.
The past is null because division only applies after demand.
3
Consider the second offense and ta'zir
If the husband repeats the violation after being forbidden, the judge may punish him with ta'zir. The text specifies the punishment is beating (ضرب), not imprisonment.
The reason: imprisonment would not recover the lost time.
4
Understand the exception from general rule
The judge normally has discretion between beating and imprisonment for ta'zir, but in this case beating is specified because imprisonment is ineffective.
This is an exception to the general rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

على ذلك تجب فيما بينه وبين الله تعالى، ولا تجب عليه في الحكم عند بعض أصحابنا، وعند بعضهم تجب عليه في الحكم. اهـ. ولم يبين حد الزيادة على المرة ولا يمكن أن يقال كلما طلبت لأنه موقوف على شهوته. لها. وفي فتح القدير: ويجب عليه وطؤها أحياناً. وفي المعراج: ولو أقام إحداهما شهراً فخاصمته الأخرى في ذلك قضى عليه أن يستقبل العدل بينهما وما مضى هدر غير أنه أثم فيه لأن القسمة تكون فيه بعد الطلب، ولو عاد بعد ما نهاه القاضي أوجعه عقوبة وأمره بالعدل لأنه أساء الأدب وارتكب ما هو حرام عليه وهو الجور فيعزر في ذلك. اهـ. وحاصله أنه لا يعزر في المرة الأولى وإذا عزر فتعزيره بالضرب. وفي الجوهرة: لا يعزر بالحبس لأنه لا يستدرك الحق فيه بالحبس لأنه يفوت بمضي الزمان. اهـ. وهذا مستثنى من قولهم إن للقاضي الخيار في التعزير بين الضرب والحبس. قوله: (وللحرة ضعف الأمة يعني إذا كان له زوجتان حرة وأمة فللحرة الثلثان من القسم وللأمة الثلث، بذلك ورد الأثر عن علي رضي الله عنه، ولأن حل الأمة انقص من حل الحرة فلا بد من إظهار النقصان في الحقوق. وأطلقها فشمل المكاتبة والمدبرة وأم الولد والمبعضة لأن الرق فيهن قائم. وفي البدائع: وهذا التفاوت في السكنى والبيتوتة، فأما في المأكول والمشروب والملبوس فإنه يسوي بينهما لأن ذلك من الحاجات اللازمة، وقدمنا أنه مبني على اعتبار حاله، أما على اعتبار حالهما فلا وفي المعراج لو أقام عند امرأته الأمة يوماً ثم أعتقت لم يقم عند الحرة إلا يوماً واحداً لاستوائهما في سبب الاستحقاق، وتجعل حريتها عند انتهاء النوبة بمنزلة حريتها عند ابتداء النوبة، وكذا لو أقام عند حرة يوماً ثم أعتقت الأمة تحول عنها إلى المعتقة لما ذكرنا. اهـ. قوله: (ويسافر بما شاء منهن والقرعة أحب) لأنه قد يثق بإحداهما في السفر وبالأخرى في الحضر والقرار في المنزل لحفظ الأمتعة أو لخوف الفتنة، أو يمنع من سفر إحداهما كثرة سمنها فتعيين من يخاف صحبتها في السفر لخروج قرعتها إلزام للضرر الشديد وهو مندفع بالمنافي للحرج، وأما ما رواه الجماعة من قرعته بينهن إذا أراد سفراً فكان للاستحباب تطييباً لقلوبهن لأن مطلق الفعل لا يقتضي الوجوب فكيف وهو محفوف بما يدل على الاستحباب من عدم وجوب القسم عليه لقوله تعالى: {ترجي من تشاء منهن وتؤوي إليك من تشاء} [الأحزاب: ٥١] وكان ممن أرجاهن سودة وجويرية وأم حبيبة وصفية وميمونة، وممن آوى عائشة والباقيات رضي الله عنهن أجمعين. قال القاضي في تفسيره: ترجي من تشاء منهن تؤخرها وتترك مضاجعتها، وتؤوي من تشاء تضم إليك وتضاجعها، أو تطلق من تشاء وتمسك من تشاء، ومن ابتغيت أي طلبت ممن عزلت طلقت بالرجع فلا جناح عليك في شيء من ذلك. اهـ. قيد بالسفر لأن مرضه لا يسقط القسم عنه وقد صح أنه عليه السلام لما مرض استأذن نساءه أن يمرض في بيت عائشة رضي الله عنها فأذن له، ولم أر كيفية قسمه في مرضه إذا كان لا يستطيع التحول إلى بيت
And since it is known that intercourse does not fall under the division, is it obligatory for the wife? Division Between Free and Slave Wives
Ruling on division between free and slave wives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the division of nights between a free wife and a slave wife according to the Hanafi school and state the exceptions for food, drink, and clothing.

Core Idea
Free wife gets two-thirds of nights; slave wife gets one-third; but they are equal in basic necessities.

The passage now addresses the division when a husband has both a free wife and a slave wife. The free wife receives two-thirds of the nights, the slave wife one-third, based on a tradition from Ali and the principle that the slave's status is lower. However, this disparity only applies to lodging and sleeping; in food, drink, and clothing, they are treated equally because these are essential needs. The passage also discusses scenarios where the slave wife is freed during the rotation.

Guided Path
1
State the ratio
The free wife gets double the slave wife: free gets two-thirds, slave gets one-third.
This is from a tradition of Ali.
2
Identify the underlying principle
The slave's status (hull) is less than the free's, so the deficiency must show in rights.
Slave's lower status reduces her entitlement.
3
Note the scope of the disparity
The disparity applies only to lodging and sleeping (السكنى والبيتوتة). For food, drink, and clothing, they are equal.
Basic necessities are not subject to disparity.
4
Handle the case of emancipation during rotation
If the slave wife is freed during the rotation, her freedom at the end of the turn is treated as if at the beginning. The husband adjusts accordingly.
He does not owe extra days for the freed wife.

In al-Bada'i': This disparity is for lodging and sleeping; as for food, drink, clothing, he equalizes between them because that is from necessary needs. And we presented that it is based on considering his state; but considering their state, it is not. In al-Mi'raj: If he stays with his slave wife for a day then she is freed, he does not stay with the free wife except for one day, because they are equal in the cause of entitlement, and her freedom at the end of the turn is like her freedom at the beginning of the turn. Similarly, if he stays with a free wife for a day then the slave is freed, he turns from her to the freed one for the reason we mentioned. His statement: 'And he travels with whomever he wishes among them, and drawing lots is more beloved' because he may trust one of them in travel and the other in residence and staying home to guard luggage or for fear of fitna, or the travel of one may be prevented by her excessive fatness, so specifying the one whose companionship is feared in travel by her lot coming out is imposing severe harm, which is repelled by what contradicts hardship. As for what the group narrated about his drawing lots among them when he intended to travel, it was for istihbab (recommendation) to please their hearts, because the mere act does not require obligation, especially since it is accompanied by what indicates recommendation from the absence of obligation of division upon him due to His saying: 'You may delay whom you will of them and take to yourself whom you will' [33:51]. And among those he delayed were Sawda, Juwayriyya, Umm Habiba, Safiyya, and Maymuna, and among those he took were 'Aisha and the rest, may God be pleased with them all. Al-Qadi said in his commentary: 'You may delay whom you will of them—you postpone her and leave off sleeping with her, and take to yourself whom you will—you take to yourself and sleep with her, or you divorce whom you will and you keep whom you will, and whom you seek—whom you desire among those you have set aside—you may take back by revocable divorce, so there is no blame upon you in any of that.' It is restricted to travel because his illness does not drop the division from him, and it is established that when he became ill, he sought permission from his wives to be nursed in 'Aisha's house, and they permitted him. I have not seen how his division was in his illness when he could not move to a house
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on division (qasm) and addresses several related issues. First, it clarifies that intercourse (wat') is not part of the division; it is a separate right of the wife. She can demand it once, and the husband must comply judicially; additional times are between him and God, but some Hanafi scholars say they are also enforceable. If a husband stays with one wife for a month without justification, the judge orders him to start afresh with equality, and the past days are not compensated; he is sinful. If he repeats the offense, the judge may punish him by beating (ta'zir) but not imprisonment because the right cannot be recovered that way. Then the passage addresses the division when one wife is free and the other is a slave: the free wife gets two-thirds of the nights and the slave one-third, based on a tradition from Ali and because the slave's right is weaker. This disparity applies only to lodging and sleeping; food, drink, and clothing are given equally. If a slave wife is freed during the rotation, the rules adjust accordingly. Finally, it discusses traveling: the husband may take any wife he wishes, but drawing lots is recommended (mustahabb) to avoid partiality, as evidenced by the Prophet's practice and the Quranic verse giving him the choice. This is restricted to travel because illness does not suspend the division; the Prophet sought permission from his wives when he was ill.

Key Terms
الحرة (al-hurra): A free woman (as opposed to a slave).
الأمة (al-amma): A slave woman.
المكاتبة (al-mukataba): A slave woman who has made a contract of manumission; she remains partially enslaved.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, in what aspect are the free wife and slave wife treated equally despite the division ratio?
A) In lodging
B) In food, drink, and clothing
C) In the number of nights
D) In all aspects

Key Takeaway
Free wife gets 2/3 nights, slave wife 1/3, but both are equal in food, drink, and clothing.

Traveling with a Wife: Choice vs. Lots
Ruling on traveling with a wife and the status of drawing lots

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on traveling with a wife and explain why drawing lots is recommended (mustahabb) but not obligatory.

Core Idea
Husband may travel with any wife; drawing lots is recommended, not required.

The final part of the passage discusses the husband's right to travel with one of his wives. The Hanafi school holds that he may take whichever wife he wishes, but it is recommended (mustahabb) to draw lots to please their hearts. This is based on the Quranic verse granting the Prophet choice, and the Prophet's practice of drawing lots when traveling, which is understood as a recommendation. Illness does not suspend division, unlike travel.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The husband may travel with whomever he wishes among his wives.
The phrase 'ويسافر بما شاء منهن' indicates full choice.
2
Identify the recommendation of lots
Drawing lots is 'أحب' (more beloved) to avoid partiality and please hearts.
It is not obligatory.
3
Analyze the evidence
The Prophet's practice of lots is understood as mustahabb, not wajib, because the Quranic verse (33:51) gave him choice, indicating no obligation of lots.
The absence of obligation is reinforced by the fact that mere action does not imply obligation.
4
Note the distinction from illness
Travel permits discretion; illness does not suspend division, and the Prophet sought permission from his wives to stay in Aisha's house when ill.
This shows the difference in rulings between travel and illness.

Three Rulings on Travel, Lots, and Gift Revocation
Matn listing three distinct rulings under the chapter of division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three rulings on travel, lots, and wife's gift revocation in the Hanafi school, and identify their respective hukm levels.

Core Idea
A husband may choose any wife for travel; lots are recommended; a wife may revoke her gifted night before it is taken.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq opens the chapter on division (qasm) among co-wives. It delivers three independent rulings in concise matn style. Understanding these foundational rules is essential before diving into the detailed proofs that follow in the commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
The matn states three distinct legal rules: (1) the husband may travel with whichever wife he wishes, (2) casting lots is preferable, (3) a wife who gives her portion to another may revoke.
Each rule applies in the context of multiple wives.
2
Determine the hukm level of each
Classify each ruling: the travel choice is mubah (permissible), lots are mustahabb (recommended), and revocation is a right that is valid and revocable.
The matn uses 'أحب' (preferred) indicating mustahabb, not wajib.
3
Note the implied evidence
Although no proof is given here, each ruling rests on known Hanafi proofs: travel freedom from Quranic context, lots from Prophetic practice, revocation from the nature of unfulfilled rights.
The commentary in later texts provides the full dalil.
4
Understand the revocation nuance
The wife's right to revoke applies only before the gifted night is actually taken. Once the other wife has availed the night, revocation is no longer possible.
This is based on the principle that a gift of a future right is not executed until delivered.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب النكاح
باب القسم
ويسافر بمن شاء والقرعة أحب ولها أن ترجع إن وهبت قسمها للأخرى.
Book of Marriage, Chapter of Division. He may travel with whomever he wishes, and casting lots is preferable, and she has the right to revoke if she gifted her portion to another.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It presents three independent rulings: (1) A husband with multiple wives may choose any one to accompany him on a journey; (2) though not obligatory, it is mustahabb (preferred) to cast lots among them to decide whom to take; (3) a wife who voluntarily gives her night to a co-wife may later revoke that gift and reclaim her right. The commentary will later provide proofs and details.

Key Terms
القسم (al-qasm): The division of nights among co-wives by the husband
القرعة (al-qur'a): Casting lots to select which wife accompanies on a journey
وهبت قسمها (wahabat qasmaha): A wife voluntarily giving her right to a night to another co-wife

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Recommended (mustahabb)
C) Permitted (mubah)

Key Takeaway
A husband may travel with any wife, lotting is recommended, and a wife may revoke her gifted night before it is taken.

Ta'zir for Injustice in Marital Division: Beating Not Imprisonment
Commentary on the judge's power to discipline a husband who is unjust in division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on ta'zir for a husband unjust in marital division and explain why imprisonment is excluded in this case.

Core Idea
A husband unjust in division of nights receives ta'zir by beating, not imprisonment; lost nights cannot be recovered with time.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the judge's power to discipline a husband who is unjust in dividing nights among his wives. While ta'zir generally allows a choice between beating and imprisonment, a specific exception is made here: the husband is beaten, not imprisoned, because the lost nights cannot be restored. This ruling is based on the nature of the wronged wife's right.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is injustice (jūr) in dividing nights among wives. The ruling is ta'zir (discretionary punishment). The judge commands justice; upon persistence, ta'zir is applied.
The first occurrence is not punished; only repetition triggers punishment.
2
Trace the conditions
First, no punishment for the first time. Second, if ta'zir is applied, it must be by beating, not imprisonment.
Condition: ta'zir is only after persistence.
3
Understand the dalil (proof)
The proof is the general principle of ta'zir and the specific reasoning that imprisonment cannot recover the lost right because it passes with time. The authority is al-Jawhara.
The dalil is istihsan (juristic preference) based on the nature of the right.
4
Identify the exception
This is an exception to the usual rule that the judge may choose between beating and imprisonment for ta'zir. Here imprisonment is excluded.
The exception prevents further injustice.
5
Evaluate the scope
This ruling applies specifically to injustice in division of nights; other ta'zir offenses still allow imprisonment.
The principle: ta'zir must be proportionate and capable of remedying the wrong.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمره بالعدل لأنه أساء الأدب وارتكب ما هو حرام عليه وهو الجور فيعزر في ذلك اهـ. وحاصله أنه لا يعزر في المرة الأولى وإذا عزر فتعزيره بالضرب. وفي الجوهرة: لا يعزر بالحبس لأنه لا يستدرك الحق فيه بالحبس لأنه يفوت بمضي الزمان اهـ. وهذا مستثنى من قولهم إن للقاضي الخيار في التعزير بين الضرب والحبس.
And he is commanded with justice because he misbehaved and committed what is forbidden for him, which is injustice, so he is subject to discretionary punishment (ta'zir) for that, end. Its summary: he is not punished the first time, and if punished, his punishment is beating. And in al-Jawhara: he is not punished with imprisonment because the right is not recovered by imprisonment as it is lost with the passage of time, end. And this is an exception from their statement that the judge has a choice in discretionary punishment between beating and imprisonment.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage explains the consequence for a husband who is unjust in dividing nights among his wives (jūr). The judge commands him to be just. If he persists, he receives ta'zir (discretionary punishment). The ruling states he is not punished the first time he errs, but if repeated, he is beaten. A distinction from al-Jawhara: imprisonment is not used here because the lost nights cannot be recovered; imprisonment would delay rather than restore the right. This is an exception to the general rule that the judge may choose between beating and imprisonment for ta'zir. Authority weight: This is from the commentary of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq; the underlying ruling appears in mutunkhah works.

Key Terms
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for sinful acts without fixed hadd

Key Takeaway
Ta'zir for a husband unjust in division of nights is limited to beating, not imprisonment, because the lost equitable time cannot be recovered.

Division of Nights Between Free and Slave Wives in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling on the proportion of nights for a free wife vs. a slave wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the proportion of nights for a free wife vs. a slave wife, identify the proof (athar from Ali and logical reasoning), and apply it to scenarios involving change of status.

Core Idea
A free wife gets two-thirds of nights; a slave wife gets one-third – inequality reflects their difference in legal status.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling when a man has both a free and a slave wife. The text from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq states a clear proportion and explains the underlying reasoning. Understanding this rule requires appreciating how the Hanafi school weighs status in marital rights and how the proof is constructed from both textual transmission (athar) and rational deduction (qiyas).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? It is the division of nights among wives when one is free and one is a slave. The ruling: the free wife receives two-thirds, the slave wife one-third.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two proofs: first, an athar (tradition) from Ali ibn Abi Talib (RA) that prescribes this division. Second, a rational argument: the 'hall' (permissibility/status) of a slave is less, so her rights in division must be less.
The athar is a companion tradition; the rational argument is a form of qiyas.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For the athar, the ruling is directly derived from the transmitted report. For the rational argument, the illa (effective cause) is the deficiency in hall, which necessitates a deficiency in the right to lodging.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds equal division between free and slave wives in all aspects. The Hanafi school responds that the difference in status must manifest in the division.
This difference is a genuine ikhtilaf in the fiqh of marriage.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in the Hanafi school, a free wife has a greater right to her husband's company than a slave wife; in the Shafi'i school, they are equal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وللحرة ضعف الأمة) يعني إذا كان له زوجتان حرة وأمة فللحرة الثلثان من القسم وللأمة الثلث، بذلك ورد الأثر عن علي رضي الله عنه، ولأن حل الأمة انقص من حل الحرة فلا بد من إظهار النقصان في الحقوق. وأطلقها فشمل المكاتبة والمدبرة وأم الولد والمبعضة لأن الرق فيهن قائم. وفي البدائع: وهذا التفاوت في السكنى والبيتوتة، فأما في المأكول والمشروب والملبوس فإنه يسوي بينهما لأن ذلك من الحاجات اللازمة، وقدمنا أنه مبني على اعتبار حاله، أما على اعتبار حالهما فلا وفي المعراج لو أقام عند امرأته الأمة يوماً ثم أعتقت لم يقم عند الحرة إلا يوماً واحداً لاستوائهما في سبب الاستحقاق، وتجعل حريتها عند انتهاء النوبة بمنزلة حريتها عند ابتداء النوبة، وكذا لو أقام عند حرة يوماً ثم أعتقت الأمة تحول عنها إلى المعتقة لما ذكرنا اهـ.
His statement: 'And for the free woman is double the slave woman' means if he has two wives, a free woman and a slave woman, then for the free woman is two-thirds of the division and for the slave woman is one-third. That is based on the reported tradition from Ali (RA), and because the permissibility (hall) of the slave woman is less than the permissibility of the free woman, so deficiency must be shown in rights. He made it general so it includes the mukataba, mudabbara, umm walad, and partially free because slavery is established in them. And in al-Bada'i': This disparity is in lodging and sleeping; as for food, drink, and clothing, he equalizes between them because those are necessary needs. We earlier stated that it is based on consideration of his condition; as for considering their condition, no. And in al-Mi'raj: If he stayed with his slave wife for a day then she was freed, he does not stay with the free wife except one day because they become equal in the cause of entitlement, and her freedom at the end of the turn is treated like her freedom at the beginning of the turn. Similarly, if he stayed with a free wife for a day then the slave was freed, he shifts to the freed one, as we mentioned. End.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling when a man has two wives, one free (hurra) and one slave (ama). The free wife has two-thirds of the nights, the slave wife one-third. The proof is the athar (tradition) from Ali ibn Abi Talib and the logical reasoning that the 'hall' (permissibility/status) of a slave is lesser, so her rights in division should reflect that deficiency. This applies to all types of slave women: mukataba, mudabbara, umm walad, and even partially free. The disparity only applies to lodging and cohabitation; in food, drink, and clothing, they must be equalized because these are necessities. If the slave wife is freed mid-cycle, her entitlement becomes equal to that of the free wife from that point, and the husband adjusts accordingly. This is from the commentary of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, referencing al-Bada'i' and al-Mi'raj. Authority weight: The base ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah; the details are from later commentaries.

Key Terms
حل الأمة (hall al-ama): The legal permissibility of a slave woman (in terms of status and rights)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what ratio of nights does a free wife receive when a husband has one free and one slave wife?
A) Half
B) Two-thirds
C) One-third
D) Equal

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school mandates an unequal division of nights (2/3 free, 1/3 slave) based on the difference in status, supported by the athar of Ali and logical reasoning.

Traveling with a Wife: Permission and Recommendation of Lots
Commentary providing proofs for traveling with a wife and use of lots

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on traveling with a wife and explain why casting lots is recommended (mustahabb) and not obligatory.

Core Idea
Traveling with one wife is permitted; the lot is mustahabb, not wajib — because the Prophet's practice was to please hearts, not to fulfill an obligation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the ruling on a husband traveling with one of his wives. The matn allows the husband to choose, and the commentator explains the basis: the Prophet's practice of casting lots was a recommendation, not a duty, as shown by Quranic evidence and the principle of avoiding hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Determine what is permitted (choosing which wife to travel with) and what is recommended (casting lots).
The matn states 'he may travel with whomever he wishes' and 'lots are preferred'.
2
Understand the reason for recommendation
The lot is recommended to avoid hardship for the wife who would not be chosen and to please hearts, not because it is obligatory.
The commentator gives practical reasons: trust, guarding goods, fear of fitna, etc.
3
Analyze the primary evidence
Examine the Quranic verse (33:51) and the Prophet's practice. The verse gives the Prophet choice, so his lot was not obligatory; it was to please hearts.
The verse: 'You can defer whom you wish and take to yourself whom you wish.'
4
Distinguish travel from illness
Note that in illness, the husband must still give each wife her turn (division), unlike travel. Illness does not drop the obligation of division.
The commentator mentions the Prophet's asking for permission to be in Aisha's house when ill.
5
Apply the principle
Conclude that the lot is mustahabb, not wajib, and understand the thamarah (practical consequence): a husband may choose without lots, but following the recommendation is better.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ويسافر بما شاء منهن والقرعة أحب) لأنه قد يثق بإحداهما في السفر وبالأخرى في الحضر والقرار في المنزل لحفظ الأمتعة أو لخوف الفتنة، أو يمنع من سفر إحداهما كثرة سمنها فتعيين من يخاف صحبتها في السفر لخروج قرعتها إلزام للضرر الشديد وهو مندفع بالمنافي للحرج، وأما ما رواه الجماعة من قرعته بينهن إذا أراد سفراً فكان للاستحباب تطييباً لقلوبهن لأن مطلق الفعل لا يقتضي الوجوب فكيف وهو محفوف بما يدل على الاستحباب من عدم وجوب القسم عليه لقوله تعالى: {تُرْجِي مَن تَشَاءُ مِنْهُنَّ وَتُؤْوِي إِلَيْكَ مَن تَشَاءُ} [الأحزاب:51] وكان ممن أرجاهن سودة وجويرية وأم حبيبة وصفية وميمونة، وممن آوى عائشة والباقيات رضي الله عنهن أجمعين. قال القاضي في تفسيره: تُرْجِي مَن تَشَاءُ مِنْهُنَّ تُؤَخِّرُهَا وَتَتْرُكُ مُضَاجَعَتَهَا، وَتُؤْوِي مَن تَشَاءُ تَضُمُّ إِلَيْكَ وَتُضَاجِعُهَا، أَوْ تُطَلِّقُ مَن تَشَاءُ وَتُمْسِكُ مَن تَشَاءُ، وَمَنِ ابْتَغَيْتَ أَيْ طَلَبْتَ مِمَّنْ عَزَلْتَ طَلَّقْتَ بِالرَّجْعَةِ فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكَ فِي شَيْءٍ مِنْ ذَلِكَ اهـ. قيد بالسفر لأن مرضه لا يسقط القسم عنه وقد صح أنه عليه السلام لما مرض استأذن نساءه أن يمرض في بيت عائشة رضي الله عنها فأذن له، ولم أر كيفية قسمه في مرضه إذا كان لا يستطيع التحول إلى بيت أخرى، والظاهر أن المراد بقسمه في مرضه أنه إذا صح ذهب إلى الأخرى بقدر ما أقام عند الأولى بخلاف ما إذا سافر بواحدة فإنه إذا أقام لا يقضي للمقيمة.
His statement: 'And he may travel with whomever he wishes of them, and casting lots is preferred' because he may trust one in travel and another in residence and staying home for guarding goods or fear of temptation, or one may be prevented from travel due to excessive fatness, so specifying the one he fears to accompany in travel by lot imposes severe harm which is repelled by the principle of no hardship. As for the reported tradition of the group (al-jama'a) of him casting lots among them when he wanted to travel, it was for recommendation to please their hearts, because an absolute action does not necessitate obligation; how much more so when it is accompanied by indications of recommendation such as the non-obligation of division upon him due to His statement: 'You can defer whom you wish and take to yourself whom you wish' (33:51). And among those he deferred were Sawda, Juwayriya, Umm Habiba, Safiyya, and Maymuna, and among those he took were Aisha and the rest, may Allah be pleased with them all. Al-Qadi said in his tafsir: 'You defer whom you wish: you delay her and leave her bed; and take to yourself whom you wish: you draw near and lie with her; or you divorce whom you wish and retain whom you wish; and whoever you desire among those you have set aside, you may take back in revocable divorce, so there is no sin upon you in any of that.' He restricted it to travel because his illness does not drop the division from him; it is authentically reported that when the Prophet (SAW) fell ill, he asked his wives for permission to be nursed in Aisha's house and they granted it. I did not see how his division was during his illness if he could not move to another house; the apparent meaning is that his division during illness means that when he recovered he would go to the other wife in proportion to the time he stayed with the first, unlike when he travels with one, then when he returns he does not make up for the one left behind.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This commentary expands on the matn ruling about traveling. The husband's choice is based on practical considerations; the lot is only recommended, as shown by the Prophet's practice. The key evidence is the verse from Surah al-Ahzab (33:51) which grants the Prophet the option to defer or take any wife, implying that division is not obligatory for him; this indicates that for others, division is obligatory, but travel is an exception. The passage also distinguishes illness from travel: in illness, the husband must still give each wife her turn if possible; if he cannot move, he compensates after recovery. This is from the commentary of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. Authority weight: The base ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah; the commentary uses Quran and hadith as proofs.

Key Terms
الاستحباب (al-istihbab): Recommendation, not obligation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the Prophet's casting lots among his wives for travel considered recommended (mustahabb) rather than obligatory according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because it was a specific ruling for the Prophet only
B) Because the Quranic verse grants the option to defer any wife, indicating no obligation
C) Because the lot was only for the first travel
D) Because the wives objected to the lot

Key Takeaway
A husband may travel with any wife he chooses; casting lots is recommended but not obligatory, as proven by the Quranic concession of choice.

Wife's Revocation of Her Gift of a Night
Ruling on wife's gift revocation with proof and cross-madhhab comparison

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a wife's revocation of her gifted night and explain why it is valid, distinguishing the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
A wife may revoke her gift of a night because she dropped a right not yet due.

This lesson examines the ruling that a wife who gifts her night to a co-wife may revoke it. The proof is the action of Sawda bint Zam'a, who gave her day to Aisha. The Hanafi school holds revocation valid unconditionally, unlike the Shafi'i school which imposes detailed conditions. Understanding this difference illuminates the Hanafi approach to rights that have not yet vested.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a wife gifting her day/night from her husband's division to another co-wife. The ruling is that it is permissible to give, and she may later revoke that gift.
The text states 'لها أن ترجع' – she has the right to revoke.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the practice of Sawda bint Zam'a, who gifted her day to Aisha, and the Prophet accepted that. This establishes permissibility of the gift.
This is a Qawl Sahabi / action of a Companion with tacit approval.
3
Analyze the legal reasoning for revocation
The reason revocation is valid is that she dropped a right (the husband's obligation to spend the night with her) before it became due. Since the right had not yet vested, dropping it does not make it final; she can reclaim it.
Hanafi principle: a right that has not yet become due is not relinquished by an earlier waiver.
4
Note the Shafi'i ikhtilaf
The Shafi'is have detailed conditions: e.g., if she gifts a specific night, the husband stays with the donee for two nights, etc. The Hanafis do not adopt these because they view the gift as an assignment of the husband's duty; the right after the gift belongs to the husband, not the donee.
The text says 'لعل مشايخنا إنما لم يعتبروا هذا التفصيل لأن هذه الهبة إنما هي إسقاط عنه فكان الحق له'.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that revocation is valid unconditionally. This is based on Zahir al-Riwaya and the practice of the Companions.
No tarjih needed; the text presents it as ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولها أن ترجع إذا وهبت قسمها لأخرى) فأفاد جواز الهبة والرجوع، أما الأول فلأن سودة بنت زمعة وهبت يومها لعائشة رضي الله عنها، وأما صحة الرجوع في المستقبل فلأنها أسقطت حقاً لم يجب بعد فلا يسقط. وقد فرع الشافعية هنا تفاريع لم أر أحداً من مشايخنا ذكرها منها: أنها إذا وهبت حقها المعينة ورضي بات عند الموهوب ليلتين وإن كرهت ما دامت الواهبة في نكاحه ولو كانا متفرقين لم يوال بينهما. وإن وهبته للجميع جعلها كالمعدومة، ولو وهبته له فخص به واحدة جاز. كذا في الروض ولعل مشايخنا إنما لم يعتبروا هذا التفصيل لأن هذه الهبة إنما هي إسقاط عنه فكان الحق له سواء وهبت له أو لصاحبتها فله أن يجعل حصة الواهبة لمن شاء. تتمة: في حقوق الزوجين: ذكر في البدائع أن من أحكام النكاح المعاشرة بالمعروف للآية. واختلف فيها فقيل التفضل والإحسان إليها قولاً وفعلاً وخلقاً، وقيل أن يعمل معها كما يحب أن يعمل مع نفسه وهي مستحبة من الجانبين. ومنها إذا حصل نشوز أن يبدأها بالوعظ ثم بالهجر ثم بالضرب للآية، لأنها للترتيب على التوزيع واختلف في الهجر فقيل يترك مضاجعتها، وقيل يترك جماعها والأظهر ترك كلامها مع المضاجعة والجماع إن احتاج إليه. وفي المعراج: إذا كان له امرأة واحدة يؤمر أن يبيت معها ولا يعطلها، وفي رواية الحسن لها ليلة من كل أربع إن كان حرة. ومن كل سبع إن كانت أمة، وفي ظاهر الرواية لا يتعين حقها في يوم من أربعة أيام لأن القسم عند المزاحمة فالصحيح أنه يؤمر استحباباً أن يصحبها أحياناً من غير أن يكون في ذلك شيء موقت. ولو كان له مستولدات وإماء فلا يقسم لهن لأنه من خصائص النكاح ولكن يستحب له أن لا يعطلهن وأن يسوي بينهن في المضاجعة. ولو حطت لزوجها جعلاً على أن يزيدها في القسم فهو حرام وهو رشوة وترجع.
His statement: 'And she has the right to revoke when she gifted her portion to another' — this indicates the permissibility of the gift and the revocation. As for the first, because Sawda bint Zam'a gave her day to Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her. As for the validity of future revocation, because she dropped a right that had not yet become due, so it is not relinquished. The Shafi'is have derived subsidiary rulings here that I have not seen any of our scholars mention: for example, if she gifts her specific right and he is content, he stays with the donee for two nights even if she dislikes it, as long as the donor is in his marriage; if they are separate, he does not keep consecutive nights. If she gifts it to all, she is treated as non-existent; if she gifts it to him and he allocates it to one, it is permissible. This is in al-Rawd. Perhaps our scholars did not consider this detail because this gift is a dropping from him, so the right belongs to him; whether gifted to him or to her co-wife, he may allocate the donor's share to whomever he wishes. Appendix: On the rights of the spouses: In al-Bada'i' it is mentioned that among the rulings of marriage is good companionship according to the verse. There is difference: it is said it is kindness and benevolence to her in word, deed, and character; and it is said he should treat her as he would like to be treated himself, and it is recommended from both sides. And among them is that if nushuz (disobedience) occurs, he begins with admonition, then separation in bed, then beating, according to the verse, because it is for sequential order. There is difference on separation: it is said he leaves her bed; it is said he leaves intercourse; the most apparent is leaving speech while still sharing bed and intercourse if needed. In al-Mi'raj: If he has one wife, he is commanded to spend the night with her and not leave her idle. In the narration of al-Hasan, she has a night every four days if free, and every seven if slave. In the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwaya), her right is not fixed to a specific day in every four days because division (qasm) is at the time of competition; the correct view is that he is recommended to keep her company occasionally without a fixed time. If he has concubines (mustawladat) and slave women, he does not divide nights for them because that is specific to marriage, but it is recommended not to leave them idle and to equalize among them in bed-sharing. And if she reduces her husband's burden (ja'al) in exchange for him increasing her share in the division, it is haram and bribery, and she takes it back.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage covers two topics: (1) A wife's right to revoke her gift of a night to a co-wife, proven by the hadith of Sawda gifting her day to Aisha. The Hanafi position is that she may revoke because the right was not yet due; it is an unfulfilled right. The Shafi'is have detailed sub-rulings which the Hanafis generally do not adopt because they consider the right to be the husband's after the gift. (2) An appendix on spousal rights: the husband is commanded to treat his wife kindly (ma'ruf). In case of nushuz, the sequence is admonition, bed-separation, then beating (allowed but only if effective and without excess). The division (qasm) is only for married wives, not for concubines. The husband is recommended to be fair with concubines but not obliged. Finally, any bribery to increase one's share is haram. Authority weight: The base rulings are from the Zahir al-Riwaya; the appendix draws from al-Bada'i' and al-Mi'raj.

Key Terms
هبة (hiba): Gift; here, the wife giving her right to a night to another co-wife.
رجوع (ruju'): Revocation; taking back the gifted right.
قسم (qasm): Division of nights among wives; the wife's right to a turn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on a wife revoking her gift of a night to a co-wife?
A) It is invalid because the gift is binding once accepted.
B) It is valid because she dropped a right not yet due.
C) It is valid only with the husband's approval.
D) It is invalid if the husband has already spent the night.

Key Takeaway
A wife may revoke her gift of a night unconditionally because the right was not yet due at the time of the gift.
