Managing Nushuz and Spousal Rights
Appendix on spousal rights: nushuz and night division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi sequence for managing nushuz and state the rules for division of nights among wives and concubines.

Core Idea
Nushuz is addressed progressively: admonition, bed separation, then light beating; division of nights is a right for free wives, not concubines.

This lesson covers the appendix on spousal rights, focusing on how a husband should handle a wife's nushuz (disobedience) and how nights are divided among wives. The text emphasizes that the husband is commanded to treat his wife kindly, but if nushuz occurs, he must follow a specific sequence. Division of nights is a recommended right for free wives, but concubines have no such right. The lesson also warns against bribery for extra nights.

Guided Path
1
Understand the baseline: good companionship
The husband is commanded to treat his wife with ma'ruf (kindness). This is a general obligation. The text mentions two interpretations: one as kindness in all aspects, the other as treating her as he would like to be treated.
Both are recommended; kindness is mutual.
2
Learn the three-step process for nushuz
When nushuz occurs, the husband begins with admonition (wa'z), then separates in bed (hajr), and finally, if necessary, strikes lightly (darb). This sequence is from the Quran (4:34).
The text emphasizes the order (tartib) is based on the verse.
3
Resolve the ikhtilaf on hajr
There are three opinions: (1) leaving her bed, (2) leaving intercourse, (3) leaving speech while still sharing bed/intercourse if needed. The most apparent (azhar) view is the third.
The Hanafi school prefers the option that maintains some connection.
4
Understand division of nights for wives
If a man has one wife, he is commanded to spend the night with her. For multiple free wives, division (qasm) is recommended but not fixed. The right is one night out of four for a free wife (according to one narration), but the Zahir al-Riwaya says it's not fixed to a specific pattern.
The text says 'he is recommended to keep her company occasionally without a fixed time' – this is the relied-upon view.
5
Note the ruling for concubines and the bribery prohibition
Concubines (including umm walad) have no right to division because it is specific to marriage. However, it is recommended to treat them fairly. Finally, if a wife offers money to increase her share, it is bribery and haram, and she may recover the payment if given.
Bribery (rashwa) is haram, and the wife can take back the payment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولها أن ترجع إذا وهبت قسمها لأخرى) فأفاد جواز الهبة والرجوع، أما الأول فلأن سودة بنت زمعة وهبت يومها لعائشة رضي الله عنها، وأما صحة الرجوع في المستقبل فلأنها أسقطت حقاً لم يجب بعد فلا يسقط. وقد فرع الشافعية هنا تفاريع لم أر أحداً من مشايخنا ذكرها منها: أنها إذا وهبت حقها المعينة ورضي بات عند الموهوب ليلتين وإن كرهت ما دامت الواهبة في نكاحه ولو كانا متفرقين لم يوال بينهما. وإن وهبته للجميع جعلها كالمعدومة، ولو وهبته له فخص به واحدة جاز. كذا في الروض ولعل مشايخنا إنما لم يعتبروا هذا التفصيل لأن هذه الهبة إنما هي إسقاط عنه فكان الحق له سواء وهبت له أو لصاحبتها فله أن يجعل حصة الواهبة لمن شاء. تتمة: في حقوق الزوجين: ذكر في البدائع أن من أحكام النكاح المعاشرة بالمعروف للآية. واختلف فيها فقيل التفضل والإحسان إليها قولاً وفعلاً وخلقاً، وقيل أن يعمل معها كما يحب أن يعمل مع نفسه وهي مستحبة من الجانبين. ومنها إذا حصل نشوز أن يبدأها بالوعظ ثم بالهجر ثم بالضرب للآية، لأنها للترتيب على التوزيع واختلف في الهجر فقيل يترك مضاجعتها، وقيل يترك جماعها والأظهر ترك كلامها مع المضاجعة والجماع إن احتاج إليه. وفي المعراج: إذا كان له امرأة واحدة يؤمر أن يبيت معها ولا يعطلها، وفي رواية الحسن لها ليلة من كل أربع إن كان حرة. ومن كل سبع إن كانت أمة، وفي ظاهر الرواية لا يتعين حقها في يوم من أربعة أيام لأن القسم عند المزاحمة فالصحيح أنه يؤمر استحباباً أن يصحبها أحياناً من غير أن يكون في ذلك شيء موقت. ولو كان له مستولدات وإماء فلا يقسم لهن لأنه من خصائص النكاح ولكن يستحب له أن لا يعطلهن وأن يسوي بينهن في المضاجعة. ولو حطت لزوجها جعلاً على أن يزيدها في القسم فهو حرام وهو رشوة وترجع.
His statement: 'And she has the right to revoke when she gifted her portion to another' — this indicates the permissibility of the gift and the revocation. As for the first, because Sawda bint Zam'a gave her day to Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her. As for the validity of future revocation, because she dropped a right that had not yet become due, so it is not relinquished. The Shafi'is have derived subsidiary rulings here that I have not seen any of our scholars mention: for example, if she gifts her specific right and he is content, he stays with the donee for two nights even if she dislikes it, as long as the donor is in his marriage; if they are separate, he does not keep consecutive nights. If she gifts it to all, she is treated as non-existent; if she gifts it to him and he allocates it to one, it is permissible. This is in al-Rawd. Perhaps our scholars did not consider this detail because this gift is a dropping from him, so the right belongs to him; whether gifted to him or to her co-wife, he may allocate the donor's share to whomever he wishes. Appendix: On the rights of the spouses: In al-Bada'i' it is mentioned that among the rulings of marriage is good companionship according to the verse. There is difference: it is said it is kindness and benevolence to her in word, deed, and character; and it is said he should treat her as he would like to be treated himself, and it is recommended from both sides. And among them is that if nushuz (disobedience) occurs, he begins with admonition, then separation in bed, then beating, according to the verse, because it is for sequential order. There is difference on separation: it is said he leaves her bed; it is said he leaves intercourse; the most apparent is leaving speech while still sharing bed and intercourse if needed. In al-Mi'raj: If he has one wife, he is commanded to spend the night with her and not leave her idle. In the narration of al-Hasan, she has a night every four days if free, and every seven if slave. In the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwaya), her right is not fixed to a specific day in every four days because division (qasm) is at the time of competition; the correct view is that he is recommended to keep her company occasionally without a fixed time. If he has concubines (mustawladat) and slave women, he does not divide nights for them because that is specific to marriage, but it is recommended not to leave them idle and to equalize among them in bed-sharing. And if she reduces her husband's burden (ja'al) in exchange for him increasing her share in the division, it is haram and bribery, and she takes it back.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage covers two topics: (1) A wife's right to revoke her gift of a night to a co-wife, proven by the hadith of Sawda gifting her day to Aisha. The Hanafi position is that she may revoke because the right was not yet due; it is an unfulfilled right. The Shafi'is have detailed sub-rulings which the Hanafis generally do not adopt because they consider the right to be the husband's after the gift. (2) An appendix on spousal rights: the husband is commanded to treat his wife kindly (ma'ruf). In case of nushuz, the sequence is admonition, bed-separation, then beating (allowed but only if effective and without excess). The division (qasm) is only for married wives, not for concubines. The husband is recommended to be fair with concubines but not obliged. Finally, any bribery to increase one's share is haram. Authority weight: The base rulings are from the Zahir al-Riwaya; the appendix draws from al-Bada'i' and al-Mi'raj.

Key Terms
نشوز (nushuz): Disobedience of the wife towards the husband's legitimate rights.
وعظ (wa'z): Admonition; verbal advice to correct behavior.
هجر (hajr): Separation; in this context, separation in bed or conversation.
ضرب (darb): Light beating that does not cause injury, as a last resort.
رشوة (rashwa): Bribery; here, wife paying husband for extra nights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the first step a husband should take when his wife is guilty of nushuz?
A) Separate beds immediately.
B) Stop talking to her.
C) Advise her verbally.
D) Strike her lightly.

Key Takeaway
The husband must address nushuz progressively: advise, then separate in bed (preferred: leave speech), then lightly beat if needed; division of nights is a recommendation for free wives, not concubines.

Ruling on a Wife Giving Her Share of Nights to Another Wife
Ruling with proof from the Sunnah and comparison with Shafi'i details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a wife giving her turn to a co-wife and retracting it, and identify the evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
A wife may give her turn to another and retract before it is due—her right is not absolute.

Marriage in Islam establishes mutual rights and responsibilities, and in a polygynous marriage, the husband must divide his time equally among co-wives. But what about the wife's own right to her share? Can she voluntarily give her turn to another wife, and can she change her mind? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling, based on the practice of the Mother of the Believers, Sawdah bint Zam'ah, and the legal principle that a right not yet due can be relinquished.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the wife is doing: giving her turn (hibah) and potentially retracting (ruju'). The ruling is mubah (permissible) for both actions.
The text explicitly says 'permissibility of gift and retraction'.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the action of Sawdah bint Zam'ah giving her day to Aisha, implicitly approved by the Prophet (taqrir).
This is a sunnah ahad, but sufficient for a zanni ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's silence and approval indicate that the action is permissible. For retraction, the text argues that since the right had not yet become obligatory, dropping it does not eliminate it; thus retraction is valid.
Key principle: a right that is not yet due can be waived and then reinstated.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i position
The author notes that Shafi'is elaborate on scenarios like gifting to the husband or to all co-wives. Hanafis ignore these details because they view the gift as a relinquishment, giving the husband discretion.
This highlights the Hanafi usul focus on the nature of the right.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, a wife may give her turn to a co-wife. If she retracts before the turn begins, the husband must restore her share.
The retraction must be before the specific night arrives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولها أن ترجع إذا وهبت قسمها لأخرى فأفاد جواز الهبة والرجوع، أما الأول فلأن سودة بنت زمعة وهبت يومها لعائشة رضي الله عنها، وأما صحة الرجوع في المستقبل فلأنها أسقطت حقاً لم يجب بعد فلا يسقط. وقد فرع الشافعية هنا تفاريع لم أر أحداً من مشايخنا ذكرها منها : أنها إذا وهبت حقها المعينة ورضي بات عند الموهوب ليلتين وإن كرهت ما دامت الواهبة في نكاحه ولو كانا متفرقين لم يوال بينهما. وإن وهبته للجميع جعلها كالمعدومة، ولو وهبته له فخص به واحدة جاز. كذا في الروض ولعل مشايخنا إنما لم يعتبروا هذا التفصيل لأن هذه الهبة إنما هي إسقاط عنه فكان الحق له سواء وهبت له أو لصاحبتها فله أن يجعل حصة الواهبة لمن شاء.
And she has the right to retract if she gives away her share to another, so this indicates the permissibility of gift and retraction. As for the first, because Sawdah bint Zam'ah gave her day to Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her. And as for the validity of retraction in the future, because she dropped a right that had not become obligatory yet, so it cannot be eliminated. The Shafi'is have derived subsidiary rulings here that I have not seen any of our scholars mention, including: that if she gives her specific right and he is pleased, he may stay with the donee for two nights even if she dislikes it, as long as the donor is in his marriage; and if they are separated he does not alternate between them; and if she gives it to all, he treats her as nonexistent; and if she gives it to him and he allocates it to one, it is permissible. Thus in al-Rawd. Perhaps our scholars did not consider this detail because this gift is only a relinquishment by him, so the right belongs to him, whether she gives it to him or to her co-wife, and he may allocate the donor's portion to whomever he wishes.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Kanz al-Daqa'iq is a ruling with proof. It establishes that a wife may give her share (turn) of nights to another co-wife, and she may retract that gift before the turn becomes due. The proof is the action of Sawdah bint Zam'ah, who gave her day to Aisha (may Allah be pleased with them). The Hanafi position is that such a gift is a relinquishment of a right that has not yet accrued, hence retraction is possible. The author notes that Shafi'i scholars have elaborated various scenarios for when the gift is made to the husband or to a specific co-wife, but Hanafi scholars generally ignore these details because according to Hanafi usul, the wife's right is not absolute ownership; it is a right that can be waived, and when waived, the husband has discretion over how to allocate the shared time. Thus the Hanafi position simplifies the ruling.

Key Terms
قسم (qism): The allocation of nights among co-wives in a polygynous marriage.
الهبة (al-hibah): A wife giving her share of time to another co-wife as a gift.
الرجوع (al-ruju'): The wife's retraction of her gift before the share becomes due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal status of a wife retracting her gift of a night to a co-wife?
A) She cannot retract it under any circumstances.
B) She may retract it as long as the turn has not yet become due (i.e., the night has not arrived).
C) She may retract only if the husband agrees.
D) She may retract only if the co-wife consents.

Key Takeaway
A wife may gift her turn to a co-wife and retract before it becomes due—the Hanafi school prioritises the wife's revisability based on the nature of her right as a personal claim.

Kind Companionship and Nushuz Treatment
Rulings on marital kindness and nushuz discipline

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequential steps for treating nushuz in the Hanafi school, explain the three interpretations of hajr, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A husband must admonish, then abandon in bed (with varying interpretations), and only lightly beat as a last resort.

The Quran commands kind companionship between spouses. When a wife becomes nashiz (disobedient), the Hanafi school prescribes a specific three-step process before any escalation. This lesson unpacks the obligation of kindness and the disciplined approach to nushuz, including an intra-madhhab debate on the meaning of 'abandonment in bed'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation of kind companionship
Locate the first ruling: 'companionship with kindness' (mu'ashara bi'l-ma'ruf) is wajib, derived from the Qur'anic verse. Note the two interpretations: some say it is favor and kindness, others say treat her as you would yourself.
Both views agree it is obligatory in principle, but differ on scope.
2
Recognize the three-step process for nushuz
The text states: first admonition (wa'z), then hajr (abandonment in bed), then beating (darb). This follows Quran 4:34, which is interpreted as sequential obligation (tartib).
The beating is restricted to light, non-injurious forms.
3
Distinguish the three interpretations of hajr
Three views: (1) avoid sharing the bed, (2) avoid intercourse while still sharing the bed, (3) avoid speaking while maintaining physical relations. The author declares the third as al-azhar (most evident).
The mufta bihi is the third view: avoid talk, but do not withhold bed or intercourse.
4
Evaluate the mufta bihi position
Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and other later authorities prefer the third view. This balances discipline with the husband's own needs and avoids complete estrangement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تتمة: في حقوق الزوجين : ذكر في البدائع أن من أحكام النكاح المعاشرة بالمعروف للآية. واختلف فيها فقيل التفضل والإحسان إليها قولاً وفعلاً وخلقاً، وقيل أن يعمل معها كما يحب أن يعمل مع نفسه وهي مستحبة من الجانبين. ومنها إذا حصل نشوز أن يبدأها بالوعظ ثم بالهجر ثم بالضرب للآية، لأنها للترتيب على التوزيع واختلف في الهجر فقيل يترك مضاجعتها، وقيل يترك جماعها والأظهر ترك كلامها مع المضاجعة والجماع إن احتاج إليه. وفي المعراج : إذا كان له امرأة واحدة يؤمر أن يبيت معها ولا يعطلها، وفي رواية الحسن لها ليلة من كل أربع إن كان حرة. ومن كل سبع إن كانت أمة، وفي ظاهر الرواية لا يتعين حقها في يوم من أربعة أيام لأن القسم عند المزاحمة فالصحيح أنه يؤمر استحباباً أن يصحبها أحياناً من غير أن يكون في ذلك شيء موقت. ولو كان له مستولدات وإماء فلا يقسم لهن لأنه من خصائص النكاح ولكن يستحب له أن لا يعطلهن وأن يسوي بينهن في المضاجعة. ولو حطت لزوجها جعلاً على أن يزيدها في القسم فهو حرام وهو رشوة وترجع بمالها.
Addendum: On the rights of the spouses: It is mentioned in al-Bada'i' that among the rulings of marriage is companionship with kindness according to the verse. There is disagreement: it is said it is favor and benevolence towards her in word, deed, and character; and it is said that he should act with her as he would like to be treated with his own self, and it is recommended from both sides. Among them: if nushuz (disobedience) occurs, he should start with admonition, then with abandonment (in bed), then with beating according to the verse, because it is for sequence and distribution. There is disagreement about abandonment: some say avoid sleeping with her, others say avoid intercourse, and the most evident is to avoid speaking with her while sleeping with her and having intercourse if needed. In al-Mi'raj: If he has only one wife, he is ordered to spend the night with her and not leave her without a turn. According to the transmission of al-Hasan, she has one night out of every four if free, and one out of every seven if a slave. In the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwaya), her right is not fixed to a specific day out of four days because division applies when there is competition. So the correct view is that he is recommended to accompany her sometimes without a fixed time. And if he has concubines (mustawladaat) and female slaves, he does not divide nights among them because it is a characteristic of marriage, but it is recommended not to neglect them and to equalize between them in bed-sharing. And if she reduces (some of her mahr) to her husband as a fee to increase her share, it is forbidden (haram) and it is bribery, and she takes back her money.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This is an addendum (تتمة) from the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, collecting various rulings on spousal rights. The first ruling: kind companionship (mu'ashara bi'l-ma'ruf) is an obligation (fard) from the verse, but its nature is debated: some say it includes favor and kindness, others say the golden rule. The second ruling: treatment of nushuz follows a sequential order: admonition, separation from bed, and finally light beating as a last resort per Qur'an 4:34. The author notes ikhtilaf on the meaning of hajr (abandonment): the strongest view is to cease talking to her while continuing physical relations. The third ruling: a husband with one wife should spend nights with her, though the time is not fixed; it is recommended to keep company. Different transmissions on exact frequency are mentioned, but the relied-upon position in Zahir al-Riwaya is that it is recommended without a fixed schedule. For concubines, there is no legal obligation of division, but it is recommended to treat them fairly in bed-sharing. The final point: a wife cannot pay her husband to get extra qism; it constitutes bribery (rishwah) and is invalid; she can reclaim the money.

Key Terms
نشوز (nushuz): A wife's disobedience to her husband's legitimate rights or a husband's mistreatment.
هجر (hajr): Abandonment in bed or separation as a disciplinary measure against nushuz.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mufta bihi, what does 'hajr' (abandonment) involve?
A) The husband refuses to sleep in the same bed
B) The husband avoids intercourse
C) The husband avoids speaking while still sharing bed and intercourse if needed
D) The husband separates entirely

Key Takeaway
Kind companionship is wajib, and nushuz must be treated in a strict sequential order: admonition, then hajr (avoiding speech while maintaining intimacy), then light beating as a last resort.

Division of Nights (Qism) and Prohibition of Bribery for It
Rulings on division of nights for wives and concubines

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain when qism is wajib versus recommended, identify the ruling for concubines, and state the prohibition of paying for extra qism.

Core Idea
Qism is wajib only with multiple wives; for one wife it is recommended without fixed time, and concubines have no right to division.

The Hanafi school addresses how a husband should allocate his nights. For a single wife, it is recommended to keep her company but not obligatory to set a schedule. For concubines, there is no legal division, but fairness is encouraged. A wife paying her husband to increase her share is considered bribery and invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for a single wife
Read the passage: 'if he has only one wife, he is ordered to spend the night with her.' But note the disagreement: some transmissions fix specific nights, but the relied-upon view (Zahir al-Riwaya) is that it is recommended (mandub) without fixed time.
The 'order' here is istihbab (recommendation), not wujub.
2
Recognize the ruling for concubines
The text explicitly states that the husband does not need to divide nights among concubines (mustawladaat and imaa') because division is a characteristic of marriage. However, it is recommended to treat them equally in bed-sharing.
This distinguishes marriage from concubinage in terms of rights.
3
Understand the prohibition of bribery for extra qism
If a wife gives her husband a fee to increase her nights, it is haram (forbidden) and constitutes bribery (rishwah). She can take back her money because the transaction is invalid.
This protects wives from exploitation and maintains the integrity of qism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a wife gives her husband money to increase her share of nights?
A) Permissible as a mutual gift
B) Makruh but valid
C) Haram, considered bribery; she can take back the money
D) Wajib for the husband to accept if the wife wishes

Key Takeaway
For a single wife, qism is recommended without fixed time; for concubines, no obligation; paying for extra qism is haram bribery.

Travel Division and Disposition of a Wife's Gifted Share in Polygamy
Rulings on division of time when husband travels, and whether husband can reallocate a wife's gifted share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on a husband's choice of stay duration while traveling, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a husband may reallocate a wife's gifted share.

Core Idea
A husband may choose his stay pattern; a wife's gifted share raises a dispute on his disposal.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two interrelated questions of qism (division of time) in polygamous marriages. First, when a husband travels and stays with one wife, how must he compensate the others? The Hanafi view gives him flexibility to set the duration of each round. Second, if a wife voluntarily gives her share to a co-wife, does the husband gain the right to allocate that share further? An intra-Hanafi dispute reveals deeper principles about the nature of a wife's right to qism and the effect of isqat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first ruling: husband's choice of dawr when traveling
The text states that the husband may choose the amount of each round (dawr) both in health and illness. When he stays with one wife, he must compensate the others equally for that period.
The duration is at his discretion, but if he stays with one for more than three days, the second wife only gets three days maximum.
2
Understand the limitation: maximum three days
The text limits compensation to three days even if the first stay was longer, based on al-Khulasa. This prevents excessive favoritism.
3
Recognize the dispute: husband's disposal after a wife gifts her share
When a wife gives her share to a co-wife, some Hanafi scholars hold that the right reverts to the husband, who may then allocate it to another co-wife. Others hold that the right remains with the donor wife, so only she may retract.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the text does not give a clear tarjih.
4
Analyze the two positions and their proofs
One position: the wife's relinquishment (isqat) frees the husband from an obligation, so the share becomes his to assign. The other: the right was established for the wife, so after relinquishment, the husband cannot reassign it to a third party.
The text mentions that some later scholars considered the relinquishment as isqat 'anhu (relinquishment by him), reverting the matter to him.
5
Apply the analogy to nuzul 'an al-waza'if and custom
The passage likens taking money for waiving qism to resigning from a position for compensation. Those who permit it rely on custom, but here there is no custom, so the stronger view is prohibition.
The commentary concludes that the discussion parallels the issue of nuzul 'an al-waza'if; the fatwa depends on custom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذكره الحديث بعد التثليث أن له التسبيع ولم يذكر زيادة عليه قوله : بقدر ما أقام عند الأولى) قال في النهر : ولا يخفى أنه إذا كان الاختيار في مقدار الدور إليه حال صحته ففي مرضه أولى فإذا مكث عند الأولى مدة أقام عند الثانية بقدرها ا.هـ. وهذا إذا أراد أن يجعل مدة إقامته دوراً لما مر أن الاختيار في مقدار الدور إليه، وبه اندفع ما ذكره المقدسي حيث قال: وما ذكر من أنه لو أقام عند واحدة فطلبت مثلها الأخرى لا يفعل ويستأنف القسم يقتضي أنه لا يستأنف هنا بالأولى ا هـ . نعم ينبغي تقييده بثلاثة أيام على ما مر عن الخلاصة. فلو أقام أكثر منها أقام عند الأخرى ثلاثة فقط تأمل قوله: (فكان الحق له الخ قال في النهر كون الحق له فيما إذا وهبت لصاحبتها ممنوع ففي البدائع في توجيه المسألة بأنه حق يثبت لها فلها أن تستوفي ولها أن تترك ا هـ. قال بعض الفضلاء: كون الحق لها إنما هو قبل الإسقاط أما بعده فاعتبره المشايخ اسقاطاً عنه فرجع الأمر إليه فيه. وقد يقال : إن الحق حيث كان لها وأسقطته المعينة لا يجوز أن يجعله لغيرها قوله : (أو زادها في مهرها (الخ قال الباقاني في شرح الملتقى فيه نظر إذ هو حقها فإذا رضيت بإسقاطه في مقابلة الزيادة فما المانع من الجواز فتأمل ا.هـ. وجوابه ما مر من تعليل صحة رجوعها لو وهبته لضرتها بأنها أسقطت حقاً لم يجب بعد فتدبر والظاهر أنه يأتي فيه الكلام الذي قالوه في النزول عن الوظائف، ومن أفتى بجواز أخذ المال بمقابلته إنما بناه على العرف ولا يخفى أنه لا عرف هنا، وأما من منعه مطلقاً يقول بالمنع هنا بالأولى تدبر .
He mentioned the hadith after the triple that he has the right of seven (nights) and did not mention an increase upon it. His statement: 'to the extent of what he stayed with the first'. He said in al-Nahr: It is not hidden that if the choice of the amount of the round (duration) is his (the husband) in health, then in illness it is even more so. If he stayed with the first for a period, he stays with the second for its equivalent. End. This is if he intends to make his stay a round because the choice of the amount of the round is his. By this is repelled what al-Maqdisi mentioned: 'What is mentioned that if he stays with one and the other demands the like, he does not do so and starts the division anew, implies that he does not start anew here a fortiori.' End. Yes, it should be limited to three days as mentioned from al-Khulasa. If he stays more than that, he stays with the other for only three days. Consider his statement: 'So the right belongs to him.' He said in al-Nahr: That the right belongs to him when she gives to her co-wife is disputable. For in al-Bada'i' in explaining the issue, it is a right established for her, so she may take it or leave it. End. Some scholars said: The right was hers before relinquishment; after relinquishment, the scholars considered it as a relinquishment by him, so the matter reverts to him. It may be said: Since the right was hers and she specifically relinquished it, he may not assign it to someone else. His statement: 'Or he increases her mahr...' al-Baqani said in Sharh al-Multaqa: There is consideration; it is her right, so if she agrees to relinquish it in exchange for an increase, what prevents permissibility? Consider. End. The answer is what passed about the reasoning of the validity of her retraction if she gave it to her co-wife, because she relinquished a right that had not become obligatory. So consider. It seems that the same discussion about relinquishment of positions (nuzul 'an al-waza'if) applies here. And whoever gave a fatwa of permissibility of taking money in exchange for it built it on custom (urf), and it is not hidden that there is no custom here. As for the one who forbids absolutely, he would say forbiddance here is a fortiori. Consider.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage continues the Sharh on the topic of qism. It addresses three issues: (1) When a husband travels and stays with one wife, what is the rule regarding division upon return? The Hanafi view is that the husband may choose the duration of his stay with each wife; in illness it is even more so. He can set his own pattern. The ruling from al-Nahr states that if he stays with one for a period, he must compensate the other equally. This is limited to three days maximum for the second wife. (2) If a wife gives her share to a co-wife, does the husband gain the right to allocate it? There is ikhtilaf among Hanafi scholars: some say the right remains with the wife and she may retract, so after relinquishment, the husband does not have the right to give it to another; others say that after the wife drops her right, it reverts to the husband as a relinquishment of his obligation, so he may assign it as he wishes. (3) The issue of a wife accepting increased mahr in exchange for giving up her turn or for a higher share in division. Al-Baqani questions the prohibition, reasoning that it is her right. The answer given is that the wife's right is not yet obligatory, so the contract is invalid. The commentary concludes that this matter parallels the issue of 'nuzul 'an al-waza'if' (resigning from positions for compensation); those who permit it rely on custom, but there is no custom here, so prohibition stands. This demonstrates the Hanafi tendency to uphold the wife's freedom and reject commodification of marital rights.

Key Terms
دور (dawr): A cycle or round of the husband's stay among wives; he may choose its duration.
إسقاط (isqat): Relinquishment of a right that has not yet become obligatory; used here for the wife dropping her share.
النزول عن الوظائف (al-nuzul 'an al-waza'if): Resigning from a position or waiving a right in exchange for compensation; the validity depends on custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi dispute discussed, what is the position of some scholars regarding a husband's ability to reallocate a co-wife's turn after the donor wife has relinquished it?
A) He may not reallocate it because the right belongs to the wife who gave it.
B) He may reallocate it to any other co-wife because the relinquishment frees him to use his discretion.
C) He must give it to the co-wife who was originally intended by the donor.
D) He must ask the donor wife's permission again.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school gives the husband flexibility in qism timing, but the disposition of a wife's gifted share remains an unresolved intra-school dispute hinging on the nature of isqat and the role of custom.

Void Agreements Between Spouses on Division and Mahr
Ruling on void spousal agreements involving mahr and division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which agreements between spouses regarding division and mahr are void (batil) and explain the Hanafi rationale.

Core Idea
Any agreement exchanging spousal rights for consideration is batil if it involves unlawful gain or exploitation.

The first part of the source passage lists several agreements where a wife gives something from her mahr to increase her rights in division, or where she gives her day to a co-wife. The authors rule them all void. In this lesson, we unpack the reasoning behind these rulings and learn to distinguish between void agreements and valid waivers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Agreements
Look at the text: what specific agreements are mentioned? (e.g., wife gives from mahr to increase her qasm, husband increases mahr in exchange for something, wife gives something to give her day to another co-wife).
The text mentions three distinct scenarios.
2
Note the Ruling
The text declares them all 'batil' (void). Understand the legal consequence: the agreement has no legal effect from the beginning.
Batil is stronger than fasid; it cannot be rectified.
3
Understand the Rationale
Why are they batil? The commentary indicates it involves riba or exploitation. The wife's right to her share (qasm) is a personal right; trading it for money or mahr increase is not allowed because it resembles unfair gain (al-akl bil-batil).
The Hanafi school prohibits any financial transaction involving spousal rights that is not sanctioned by shari'ah.
4
Distinguish from Valid Waivers
The later discussion (Nahy al-Fudala) shows that a simple waiver without consideration is valid. This lesson focuses on the void agreements that involve a quid pro quo.
If a wife simply forgives her right without any exchange, it is valid.
5
Apply to Similar Cases
Consider a hypothetical: a wife offers to give up her night in exchange for a gift from her husband. The ruling is batil because it involves trading a right for material gain.
Even if both consent, the transaction is void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب النكاح باب
بمالها، وكذا لو جعلت من مهرها شيئاً ليزيدها في القسم أو زادها في مهرها أو جعل لها شيئاً لتجعل يومها لصاحبتها فالكل باطل ولا يجوز أن يجمع بين الضرتين أو الضرائر في مسكن واحد إلا برضاهن للزوم الوحشة ولو اجتمعت الضرائر في مسكن واحد بالرضا يكره أن يطأ إحداهما بحضرة الأخرى حتى لو طلب وطأها لم تلزمها الإجابة ولا تصير بالامتناع ناشزة، ولا خلاف في هذه المسائل. وله أن يجبرها على الغسل من الجنابة والحيض والنفاس إلا أن تكون ذمية وله جبرها على التنظيف والاستحداد وله أن يمنعها من كل ما يتأذى من رائحته وله أن يمنعها من الغزل .اهـ. وفي فتح القدير : وعلى هذا له أن يمنعها من التزين بما يتأذى بريحه كأن يتأذى برائحة الحناء المخضب .اهـ. وسيأتي في فصل التعزير المواضع التي يضربها فيها، وفي باب النفقات ما يجوز لها من الخروج وما لا يجوز. قالوا: ولو كان أبوها زمناً وليس له من يقوم عليه مؤمناً كان أو كافراً فإن عليها أن تعصي الزوج في المنع. وفي البزازية من الحظر والإباحة : وحق الزوج على الزوجة أن تطيعه في كل مباح يأمرها به اهـ وفيها من أخر الجنايات: ادعت على زوجها ضرباً فاحشاً وثبت ذلك عليه يعزر الزوج اهـ. وظاهره أنه لو لم يكن فاحشاً وهو غير المبرح فإنه لا يعزر فيه. وذكر البقاعي في المناسبات حديثاً «لا يسأل الرجل فيم ضرب زوجته وحديثاً آخر أنه المرأة أن تشكو زوجها والله تعالى أعلم.
نهي الفضلاء: كون الحق لها إنما هو قبل الإسقاط أما بعده فاعتبره المشايخ اسقاطاً عنه فرجع الأمر إليه فيه. وقد يقال : إن الحق حيث كان لها وأسقطته المعينة لا يجوز أن يجعله لغيرها قوله : (أو زادها في مهرها) الخ قال الباقاني في شرح الملتقى فيه نظر إذ هو حقها فإذا رضيت بإسقاطه في مقابلة الزيادة فما المانع من الجواز فتأمل ا.هـ. وجوابه ما مر من تعليل صحة رجوعها لو وهبته لضرتها بأنها أسقطت حقاً لم يجب بعد فتدبر والظاهر أنه يأتي فيه الكلام الذي قالوه في النزول عن الوظائف، ومن أفتى بجواز أخذ المال بمقابلته إنما بناه على العرف ولا يخفى أنه لا عرف هنا، وأما من منعه مطلقاً يقول بالمنع هنا بالأولى تدبر .
Book of Nikah, chapter: With her wealth, and likewise if she makes something from her mahr to increase her division, or he increases her in her mahr, or he makes something for her to give her day to her co-wife, then all is void. It is not permissible to combine the two co-wives or the co-wives in one dwelling except with their consent due to aversion. If co-wives gather in one dwelling with consent, it is disliked for him to have intercourse with one in the presence of another; even if he requests intercourse, she is not obliged to respond, and she does not become nashiz (rebellious) by refusing. There is no disagreement on these issues. He can compel her to bathe from janabah, menstruation, and postpartum bleeding, unless she is a dhimmi. He can compel her to clean and remove pubic hair. He can prevent her from anything whose smell is offensive, and he can prevent her from spinning. End quote. In Fath al-Qadir: Accordingly, he can prevent her from adornment whose smell is offensive, such as the smell of henna dye. End quote. It will come in the chapter of ta'zir the places he may strike her, and in the chapter of nafaqat what she is allowed to go out for and what not. They said: If her father is disabled and has no one to care for him, whether Muslim or disbeliever, then she must disobey her husband in prevention. In al-Bazzaziyya, from al-Hazr wa al-Ibaha: The husband's right over his wife is that she obeys him in every permissible act he commands her. End quote. And in it, from the chapter of injurie: if a wife claims that her husband struck her excessively and it is proven, the husband is punished (ta'zir). End quote. Its apparent meaning is that if the beating was not excessive (i.e., not severe), then he is not punished. Al-Buqa'i mentioned in al-Munasabat a hadith: 'Do not ask a man why he beats his wife' and another hadith that the woman may complain of her husband. And Allah knows best. The admonition of the scholars: The right belongs to her only before waiver; after waiver, the shaykhs consider it a waiver from him, so the matter returns to him. It may be said: Since the right was hers and she explicitly waived it, it is not permissible to give it to another. His statement: (or he increases her in her mahr) etc. Al-Baqqani said in Sharh al-Multaqa: There is consideration in this, for it is her right; if she consents to waive it in exchange for an increase, what prevents permissibility? So reflect. End quote. Its answer is what has passed of the reasoning for the validity of her returning it if she gave it to her co-wife, that she waived a right that was not incumbent after it. So reflect. Apparently, the discussion here is like what they said about relinquishing offices. Those who gave fatwa allowing taking money in exchange for it rely on custom. It is not hidden that there is no custom here. As for those who prohibit it absolutely, they say prohibition here is all the more reason to reflect.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings from the chapter on marriage, specifically dealing with the rights and obligations between spouses. The author begins by stating that any agreement where a wife gives something from her mahr to increase her rights in division, or the husband increases her mahr, or she gives something to give her day to a co-wife, is batil (void). This is because such transactions involve either riba or unfair exploitation. Next, it is ruled that co-wives should not be forced to share a single dwelling without their consent, as this causes aversion (wahshah). If they do consent, it is makruh (disliked) for the husband to have intercourse with one in the presence of the other; she is not obliged to respond, and refusal does not make her nashiz. The author notes that there is no ikhtilaf on these issues. The husband has the right to compel his wife to perform ghusl after janabah, menstruation, and postpartum bleeding, unless she is a dhimmi (non-Muslim under protection). He can also compel her to clean and remove pubic hair (istihdad). He can prevent her from doing anything that produces an offensive smell, including spinning (if it makes her hands sweaty) or wearing henna if the smell bothers him. References are made to Fath al-Qadir and later sections on ta'zir and nafaqat. A special case: if the wife's father is disabled and has no one to care for him, the wife must disobey her husband if he prevents her from caring for her father, regardless of the father's faith. From al-Bazzaziyya, the general rule is that the wife must obey her husband in every permissible act he commands. If a wife proves that her husband beat her excessively (fahish), the husband is punished with ta'zir; non-excessive beating does not incur punishment. Two hadiths are cited: one about not asking a man why he beats his wife, and another about the woman's right to complain. The passage ends with a discussion (Nahy al-Fudala) on the nature of the wife's right to her share: it is hers only before she waives it; after waiver, the matter returns to the husband. There is a subtle point about exchanging the waiver for an increase in mahr—some scholars see no harm, others prohibit it by analogy to relinquishing offices, especially in the absence of custom.

Key Terms
قسم (qasm): Division of nights among co-wives, a right of the wife.
باطل (bāṭil): Void and of no legal effect, as opposed to fasid (voidable) in Hanafi terminology.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling if a husband increases his wife's mahr in exchange for her giving up her right to one night with him?
A) Valid because she consented
B) Batil (void) because it involves exchange of a right for consideration
C) Makruh but valid
D) Valid only if witnessed

Key Takeaway
Agreements to trade spousal rights (like qasm) for money or property are void (batil) in Hanafi fiqh.

Co-Wife Dwelling and Intercourse Etiquette
Rulings on co-wife dwelling and intercourse etiquette

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on co-wives sharing a dwelling and the etiquette of intercourse in their presence.

Core Idea
Co-wives cannot be forced to share a dwelling; if they consent, intercourse in presence of another is disliked and refusal does not make her nashiz.

The source passage next addresses the living arrangements of co-wives. It rules that co-wives must not be forced into a single dwelling without their consent due to the aversion this causes. Even if they consent, certain etiquette must be observed regarding intercourse. This lesson explains these rulings and their basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling on Dwelling
The text says: 'It is not permissible to combine the two co-wives or the co-wives in one dwelling except with their consent due to aversion (al-uzm al-wahshah).' Understand that the default is separate dwellings; forcing them together is not allowed.
This is a protective measure for the wives' psychological well-being.
2
Note the Exception
If they consent, they may share. But even then, certain rules apply.
Consent overcomes the prohibition.
3
Understand the Etiquette of Intercourse
If co-wives share a dwelling with consent, it is makruh (disliked) for the husband to have intercourse with one in the presence of the other. The wife present is not obliged to respond and refusal does not make her nashiz (rebellious).
This preserves modesty (haya) and avoids offending the other wife.
4
Recognize the Absence of Disagreement
The author notes: 'There is no disagreement on these issues.' This indicates the rulings are settled within the Hanafi school.
Ijmah or consensus among Hanafi scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب النكاح باب
بمالها، وكذا لو جعلت من مهرها شيئاً ليزيدها في القسم أو زادها في مهرها أو جعل لها شيئاً لتجعل يومها لصاحبتها فالكل باطل ولا يجوز أن يجمع بين الضرتين أو الضرائر في مسكن واحد إلا برضاهن للزوم الوحشة ولو اجتمعت الضرائر في مسكن واحد بالرضا يكره أن يطأ إحداهما بحضرة الأخرى حتى لو طلب وطأها لم تلزمها الإجابة ولا تصير بالامتناع ناشزة، ولا خلاف في هذه المسائل. وله أن يجبرها على الغسل من الجنابة والحيض والنفاس إلا أن تكون ذمية وله جبرها على التنظيف والاستحداد وله أن يمنعها من كل ما يتأذى من رائحته وله أن يمنعها من الغزل .اهـ. وفي فتح القدير : وعلى هذا له أن يمنعها من التزين بما يتأذى بريحه كأن يتأذى برائحة الحناء المخضب .اهـ. وسيأتي في فصل التعزير المواضع التي يضربها فيها، وفي باب النفقات ما يجوز لها من الخروج وما لا يجوز. قالوا: ولو كان أبوها زمناً وليس له من يقوم عليه مؤمناً كان أو كافراً فإن عليها أن تعصي الزوج في المنع. وفي البزازية من الحظر والإباحة : وحق الزوج على الزوجة أن تطيعه في كل مباح يأمرها به اهـ وفيها من أخر الجنايات: ادعت على زوجها ضرباً فاحشاً وثبت ذلك عليه يعزر الزوج اهـ. وظاهره أنه لو لم يكن فاحشاً وهو غير المبرح فإنه لا يعزر فيه. وذكر البقاعي في المناسبات حديثاً «لا يسأل الرجل فيم ضرب زوجته وحديثاً آخر أنه المرأة أن تشكو زوجها والله تعالى أعلم.
نهي الفضلاء: كون الحق لها إنما هو قبل الإسقاط أما بعده فاعتبره المشايخ اسقاطاً عنه فرجع الأمر إليه فيه. وقد يقال : إن الحق حيث كان لها وأسقطته المعينة لا يجوز أن يجعله لغيرها قوله : (أو زادها في مهرها) الخ قال الباقاني في شرح الملتقى فيه نظر إذ هو حقها فإذا رضيت بإسقاطه في مقابلة الزيادة فما المانع من الجواز فتأمل ا.هـ. وجوابه ما مر من تعليل صحة رجوعها لو وهبته لضرتها بأنها أسقطت حقاً لم يجب بعد فتدبر والظاهر أنه يأتي فيه الكلام الذي قالوه في النزول عن الوظائف، ومن أفتى بجواز أخذ المال بمقابلته إنما بناه على العرف ولا يخفى أنه لا عرف هنا، وأما من منعه مطلقاً يقول بالمنع هنا بالأولى تدبر .
Book of Nikah, chapter: With her wealth, and likewise if she makes something from her mahr to increase her division, or he increases her in her mahr, or he makes something for her to give her day to her co-wife, then all is void. It is not permissible to combine the two co-wives or the co-wives in one dwelling except with their consent due to aversion. If co-wives gather in one dwelling with consent, it is disliked for him to have intercourse with one in the presence of another; even if he requests intercourse, she is not obliged to respond, and she does not become nashiz (rebellious) by refusing. There is no disagreement on these issues. He can compel her to bathe from janabah, menstruation, and postpartum bleeding, unless she is a dhimmi. He can compel her to clean and remove pubic hair. He can prevent her from anything whose smell is offensive, and he can prevent her from spinning. End quote. In Fath al-Qadir: Accordingly, he can prevent her from adornment whose smell is offensive, such as the smell of henna dye. End quote. It will come in the chapter of ta'zir the places he may strike her, and in the chapter of nafaqat what she is allowed to go out for and what not. They said: If her father is disabled and has no one to care for him, whether Muslim or disbeliever, then she must disobey her husband in prevention. In al-Bazzaziyya, from al-Hazr wa al-Ibaha: The husband's right over his wife is that she obeys him in every permissible act he commands her. End quote. And in it, from the chapter of injurie: if a wife claims that her husband struck her excessively and it is proven, the husband is punished (ta'zir). End quote. Its apparent meaning is that if the beating was not excessive (i.e., not severe), then he is not punished. Al-Buqa'i mentioned in al-Munasabat a hadith: 'Do not ask a man why he beats his wife' and another hadith that the woman may complain of her husband. And Allah knows best. The admonition of the scholars: The right belongs to her only before waiver; after waiver, the shaykhs consider it a waiver from him, so the matter returns to him. It may be said: Since the right was hers and she explicitly waived it, it is not permissible to give it to another. His statement: (or he increases her in her mahr) etc. Al-Baqqani said in Sharh al-Multaqa: There is consideration in this, for it is her right; if she consents to waive it in exchange for an increase, what prevents permissibility? So reflect. End quote. Its answer is what has passed of the reasoning for the validity of her returning it if she gave it to her co-wife, that she waived a right that was not incumbent after it. So reflect. Apparently, the discussion here is like what they said about relinquishing offices. Those who gave fatwa allowing taking money in exchange for it rely on custom. It is not hidden that there is no custom here. As for those who prohibit it absolutely, they say prohibition here is all the more reason to reflect.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings from the chapter on marriage, specifically dealing with the rights and obligations between spouses. The author begins by stating that any agreement where a wife gives something from her mahr to increase her rights in division, or the husband increases her mahr, or she gives something to give her day to a co-wife, is batil (void). This is because such transactions involve either riba or unfair exploitation. Next, it is ruled that co-wives should not be forced to share a single dwelling without their consent, as this causes aversion (wahshah). If they do consent, it is makruh (disliked) for the husband to have intercourse with one in the presence of the other; she is not obliged to respond, and refusal does not make her nashiz. The author notes that there is no ikhtilaf on these issues. The husband has the right to compel his wife to perform ghusl after janabah, menstruation, and postpartum bleeding, unless she is a dhimmi (non-Muslim under protection). He can also compel her to clean and remove pubic hair (istihdad). He can prevent her from doing anything that produces an offensive smell, including spinning (if it makes her hands sweaty) or wearing henna if the smell bothers him. References are made to Fath al-Qadir and later sections on ta'zir and nafaqat. A special case: if the wife's father is disabled and has no one to care for him, the wife must disobey her husband if he prevents her from caring for her father, regardless of the father's faith. From al-Bazzaziyya, the general rule is that the wife must obey her husband in every permissible act he commands. If a wife proves that her husband beat her excessively (fahish), the husband is punished with ta'zir; non-excessive beating does not incur punishment. Two hadiths are cited: one about not asking a man why he beats his wife, and another about the woman's right to complain. The passage ends with a discussion (Nahy al-Fudala) on the nature of the wife's right to her share: it is hers only before she waives it; after waiver, the matter returns to the husband. There is a subtle point about exchanging the waiver for an increase in mahr—some scholars see no harm, others prohibit it by analogy to relinquishing offices, especially in the absence of custom.

Key Terms
ناشزة (nāshizah): A wife who rebels against her husband's lawful rights without legitimate excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If co-wives share a dwelling with consent, and the husband requests intercourse with one in the presence of the other, what is the obligation of the requested wife?
A) She must obey her husband
B) She is not obliged to respond, and refusal does not make her nashiz
C) She must respond if the other wife also agrees
D) She is obliged to respond but may avoid it tactfully

Key Takeaway
Co-wives cannot be forced to share a dwelling; consent is required, and even then, intimacy in front of another is disliked and refusal is not rebellion.

Nikah — Marriage
beginner

Husband's Right to Compel Cleanliness and Prohibit Offensive Smells
Rulings on husband's right to compel cleanliness and prohibit offensive smells

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the husband's rights to compel his wife to perform ghusl, clean herself, and avoid offensive smells, and state the exceptions.

Core Idea
A husband can compel his wife to be clean and avoid offensive smells; this includes ghusl, hair removal, and forbidding strong odors like henna.

The source passage lists several rights the husband has over his wife regarding personal hygiene and appearance. He can compel her to bathe from janabah, menstruation, and postpartum bleeding, and to clean and remove pubic hair. He can also prevent her from doing anything that produces an offensive odor, including wearing henna. This lesson explains these rights and their limits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Husband's Rights over Cleanliness
The text gives three rights: he can compel her to bathe from janabah (impurity after intercourse), menstrual and postpartum bleeding; he can compel her to clean herself and remove pubic hair (istihdad); he can prevent her from anything that causes offensive odor.
These are based on the husband's right to enjoy marital intimacy without discomfort.
2
Note the Exception for Non-Muslim Wife
The right to compel ghusl from janabah does not apply if the wife is a dhimmi (non-Muslim living under Islamic rule). Why? Because ghusl from janabah is a purificatory act that is not required from her in her faith.
Other cleanliness rights likely still apply.
3
Understand the Scope of 'Offensive Smell'
The text includes spinning (ghazl) as something he can prevent because it may cause sweat odor. Fath al-Qadir adds that he can prevent henna if the smell bothers him. This is based on his right to enjoy her without being annoyed.
The ruling is specific to offensive odors; pleasant scents are not included.
4
Apply to Similar Cases
Consider a case where a wife uses a perfume that the husband dislikes (but not offensive). He cannot force her to stop because it is not harmful or offensive.
The criterion is 'yuta'adha min ra'ihati' (whose smell is harmful/annoying).

Source Text

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings from the chapter on marriage, specifically dealing with the rights and obligations between spouses. The author begins by stating that any agreement where a wife gives something from her mahr to increase her rights in division, or the husband increases her mahr, or she gives something to give her day to a co-wife, is batil (void). He can prevent her from doing anything that produces an offensive smell, including spinning (if it makes her hands sweaty) or wearing henna if the smell bothers him. Key Terms
استحداد (istihdad): Removal of pubic hair; one of the acts of personal hygiene a husband can compel his wife to do.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, can a husband compel his Muslim wife to perform ghusl after intercourse?
A) Yes, he can compel her
B) No, it is only recommended
C) Only if she has an offensive smell
D) Yes, but only if she is a virgin

Key Takeaway
A husband can compel his wife to maintain hygiene and avoid offensive smells, but not beyond what causes discomfort.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
7 min
Wife's Obedience, Ta'zir for Excessive Beating, and Caring for Disabled Parent
Rulings on wife's obedience, caring for disabled parent, and ta'zir for excessive beating

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the limits of a wife's obedience, when a husband is punished for beating, and the exception for caring for a disabled parent.

Core Idea
A wife must obey her husband in lawful matters, but she may disobey to care for a disabled parent; excessive beating incurs ta'zir.

The source passage continues with several important rulings: a general rule that the wife must obey her husband in every permissible act; a specific case where she must disobey him to care for her disabled father; and the rule that a husband who beats his wife excessively is subject to ta'zir (discretionary punishment). This lesson covers these points and their practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the General Rule of Obedience
From al-Bazzaziyya: 'The husband's right over his wife is that she obeys him in every permissible act he commands her.' This is the default – she must obey in matters that are halal and within his authority.
The key word is 'mubah' (permissible); she is not obliged to obey if he commands something haram or makruh tahrimi.
2
Identify the Exception for Caring for a Disabled Parent
If the wife's father is disabled (zamin) and has no one to care for him, she must disobey her husband if he prevents her from caring for her father. This applies whether the father is Muslim or disbeliever.
This overrides the general rule because caring for a needy parent is a higher obligation.
3
Understand the Ruling on Beating
If a wife proves that her husband beat her excessively (fahish), the husband is punished with ta'zir. Non-excessive beating (ghayr al-mubarrah) does not incur punishment.
This aligns with Quranic permission for light disciplining (daraba ghayr mubarrah) but prohibits abuse.
4
Recognize the Principles Behind These Rulings
These rulings balance the husband's authority with the wife's rights and higher duties. Obedience is required only in lawful matters; filial piety takes precedence over marital obedience when the parent is in need; and physical discipline is strictly limited to non-abusive forms.
The hadith cited about not questioning a man why he beats his wife is interpreted in context of permissible disciplining.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب النكاح باب

Book of Nikah, chapter: With her wealth, and likewise if she makes something from her mahr to increase her division, or he increases her in her mahr, or he makes something for her to give her day to her co-wife, then all is void. It is not permissible to combine the two co-wives or the co-wives in one dwelling except with their consent due to aversion. If co-wives gather in one dwelling with consent, it is disliked for him to have intercourse with one in the presence of another; even if he requests intercourse, she is not obliged to respond, and she does not become nashiz (rebellious) by refusing. There is no disagreement on these issues. He can compel her to bathe from janabah, menstruation, and postpartum bleeding, unless she is a dhimmi. He can compel her to clean and remove pubic hair. He can prevent her from anything whose smell is offensive, and he can prevent her from spinning. End quote. In Fath al-Qadir: Accordingly, he can prevent her from adornment whose smell is offensive, such as the smell of henna dye. End quote. It will come in the chapter of ta'zir the places he may strike her, and in the chapter of nafaqat what she is allowed to go out for and what not. They said: If her father is disabled and has no one to care for him, whether Muslim or disbeliever, then she must disobey her husband in prevention. In al-Bazzaziyya, from al-Hazr wa al-Ibaha: The husband's right over his wife is that she obeys him in every permissible act he commands her. End quote. And in it, from the chapter of injurie: if a wife claims that her husband struck her excessively and it is proven, the husband is punished (ta'zir). End quote. Its apparent meaning is that if the beating was not excessive (i.e., not severe), then he is not punished. Al-Buqa'i mentioned in al-Munasabat a hadith: 'Do not ask a man why he beats his wife' and another hadith that the woman may complain of her husband. And Allah knows best. The admonition of the scholars: The right belongs to her only before waiver; after waiver, the shaykhs consider it a waiver from him, so the matter returns to him. It may be said: Since the right was hers and she explicitly waived it, it is not permissible to give it to another. His statement: (or he increases her in her mahr) etc. Al-Baqqani said in Sharh al-Multaqa: There is consideration in this, for it is her right; if she consents to waive it in exchange for an increase, what prevents permissibility? So reflect. End quote. Its answer is what has passed of the reasoning for the validity of her returning it if she gave it to her co-wife, that she waived a right that was not incumbent after it. So reflect. Apparently, the discussion here is like what they said about relinquishing offices. Those who gave fatwa allowing taking money in exchange for it rely on custom. It is not hidden that there is no custom here. As for those who prohibit it absolutely, they say prohibition here is all the more reason to reflect.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings from the chapter on marriage, specifically dealing with the rights and obligations between spouses. The author begins by stating that any agreement where a wife gives something from her mahr to increase her rights in division, or the husband increases her mahr, or she gives something to give her day to a co-wife, is batil (void). This is because such transactions involve either riba or unfair exploitation. Next, it is ruled that co-wives should not be forced to share a single dwelling without their consent, as this causes aversion (wahshah). If they do consent, it is makruh (disliked) for the husband to have intercourse with one in the presence of the other; she is not obliged to respond, and refusal does not make her nashiz. The author notes that there is no ikhtilaf on these issues. The husband has the right to compel his wife to perform ghusl after janabah, menstruation, and postpartum bleeding, unless she is a dhimmi (non-Muslim under protection). He can also compel her to clean and remove pubic hair (istihdad). He can prevent her from doing anything that produces an offensive smell, including spinning (if it makes her hands sweaty) or wearing henna if the smell bothers him. References are made to Fath al-Qadir and later sections on ta'zir and nafaqat. A special case: if the wife's father is disabled and has no one to care for him, the wife must disobey her husband if he prevents her from caring for her father, regardless of the father's faith. From al-Bazzaziyya, the general rule is that the wife must obey her husband in every permissible act he commands. If a wife proves that her husband beat her excessively (fahish), the husband is punished with ta'zir; non-excessive beating does not incur punishment. Two hadiths are cited: one about not asking a man why he beats his wife, and another about the woman's right to complain. The passage ends with a discussion (Nahy al-Fudala) on the nature of the wife's right to her share: it is hers only before she waives it; after waiver, the matter returns to the husband. There is a subtle point about exchanging the waiver for an increase in mahr—some scholars see no harm, others prohibit it by analogy to relinquishing offices, especially in the absence of custom.

Key Terms
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for offenses not covered by fixed hadd penalties, often imposed by the judge.
مباح (mubah): Permissible, legally neutral. The wife must obey her husband in commands that are mubah (lawful).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a husband beats his wife excessively (fahish) and it is proven, what is the consequence?
A) The wife must forgive him
B) The husband is punished with ta'zir
C) The marriage is annulled
D) The wife becomes nashiz

Key Takeaway
A wife's obedience to her husband is limited to permissible acts and can be overridden by filial duties; excessive beating incurs ta'zir.

Definition of Rada' and Its Legal Conditions
Defining rada' and its legal conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of rada' and identify the conditions that establish mahramiyyah.

Core Idea
Rada' is established when human milk reaches the infant's stomach via mouth or nose—method irrelevant.

This lesson examines the precise definition of rada' (fosterage) as the cause of mahramiyyah. The passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that the mere act of sucking is not required; what matters is the milk reaching the stomach through specific passages. We will explore the conditions, exceptions, and practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sabab (cause)
Determine what triggers the legal prohibition of marriage due to fosterage. The passage defines it as the milk of a human female reaching the infant's stomach.
This is the core of the definition.
2
Specify the shurut (conditions)
List the conditions: milk must be from a human female, reach the stomach via mouth or nose, within the prescribed period (discussed later).
Condition of 'human female' excludes animals, and 'mouth or nose' excludes other passages.
3
Distinguish methods of milk delivery
Understand that any method (sucking, pouring, snuffing, etc.) is effective as long as milk reaches the stomach. The source explicitly includes wajur and sa'ut.
This expands the common understanding that only direct suckling counts.
4
Handle cases of doubt
If there is doubt whether milk reached the stomach, rada' is not established. For example, if a woman inserts her nipple but it is unknown if milk entered, marriage is not prohibited.
Certainty is required for prohibition.
5
Note related rulings
Consider the ruling on breastfeeding without husband's permission (disliked unless necessity) and employing a foolish wet nurse (disliked due to potential harm).
These are practical applications of the definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سبب ثدي المرأة إلى جوف الصغير من فمه أو أنفه في مدة الرضاع الآتية، فشمل ما إذا حلبت لبنها في قارورة فإن الحرمة تثبت بإيجار هذا اللبن صبياً وإن لم يوجد المص، وإنما ذكره لأنه للوصول، فأطلق السبب وأرد المسبب فلا فرق بين المص والصب والسعوط والوجور كما في الخانية. وخرج بالآدمية الرجل والبهيمة، وأطلقها فشمل البكر والثيب والحية والميتة. وقيدنا بالفم والأنف ليخرج ما إذا وصل بالإقطار في الأذن والإحليل والجائفة والآمة بالحقنة في ظاهر الرواية كما في الخانية وسيأتي وخرج بالوصول لو أدخلت امرأة حلمة ثديها في فم رضيع ولا يدري أدخل اللبن في حلقه أم لا لا يحرم النكاح لأن في المانع شكاً. كذا في الولوالجية وفي القنية : امرأة كانت تعطي ثديها صبية واشتهر ذلك بينهم ثم تقول لم يكن في ثدي لبن حين ألقمتها ثدين ولا يعلم ذلك الأمر إلا من جهتها جاز لابنها أن يتزوج بهذه الصبية ا هـ . وفي الخانية صبية أرضعها قوم النساء أن لا يرضعن كل صبي من غير ضرورة فإذا فعلن فليحفظن أو ليكتبن ا هـ . وفي الخانية من الحظر والإباحة : امرأة ترضع صبياً من غير إذن زوجها يكره لها ذلك إلا إذا خافت هلاك الرضيع فحينئذ لا بأس به ا.هـ. وينبغي أن يكون واجباً عليها عند خوف الهلاك إحياء للنفس. وفي المحيط : ولا ينبغي للرجل أن يدخل ولده إلى الحمقاء لترضعه لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى عن لبن الحمقاء وقال «اللبن يعدي» وإنما نهى لأن الدفع إلى الحمقاء يعرض ولده للهلاك بسبب حفظها له وتعهدها أو لسوء الأدب فإنها لا تحسن تأديبه فينشأ الولد سيء الأدب. وقوله اللبن يعدي» يحتمل أن الحمقاء لا تحتمي من الأشياء الضارة للولد فيؤثر في لبنها فيضر بالصبي، وهذا موافق لما تقوله الأطباء فإنهم يأمرون المرضعة بالاحتماء عن أشياء تورث علة، ويحتمل أنه إنما نهى عن ذلك حتى إذا اتفق اتفاق لا يضاف إلى العدوى كما روي عن علي رضي الله عنه لا تسافروا والقمر في العقرب فهذا «إن صح عنه لئلا يتفق اتفاق فينسب إلى كون القمر في العقرب فيكون إيماناً بالنجوم وتكذيباً للأخبار المروية في النهي في هذا الباب ا هـ . وبما قررناه ظهر أن تعريف المصنف منتقض طرداً بالصبي قلة عنه فإنما نهى المراد بالمص الوصول إلى الجوف من المنفذين من إطلاق السبب وإرادة المسبب فلا نقض لكن قال في النهر : لقائل أن يقول لا نسلم وجود مص اللبن فيما إذا لم يعلم أو صل أم لا للتلازم وعكساً لو بقي على ظاهره فإنه يوجد المص ولا رضاع إن لم يصل إلى الجوف وينتفي المصى في الوجور والسعوط ولم ينتف الرضاع والثدي مذكر كما في المغرب. وفي المصباح : الثدي للمرأة وقد يقال في الرجل أيضاً قاله ابن السكيت ويذكر ويؤنث فيقال هو الثدي وهي الثدي والجمع أثد وثدي وأصلها أفعل وفعول مثل أفلس وفلوس وربما جمع على ثداء مثل سهم وسهام ا هـ .
The cause is the milk of a woman reaching the stomach of an infant through his mouth or nose within the coming period of breastfeeding. So it includes if she expressed her milk into a bottle, for the prohibition is established by giving this milk to an infant to drink even if sucking does not occur. He only mentioned sucking because it is the means of reaching. So he mentioned the cause and intended the result, so there is no difference between sucking, pouring, snuffing, and dripping as in al-Khaniyya. What is excluded by 'human' is the male and animal. And he made it absolute, so it includes virgin, non-virgin, living, and dead. We restricted to mouth and nose to exclude what reaches by instilling in the ear, urethra, deep wound, and head wound by enema in the apparent narration as in al-Khaniyya and it will come. And what is excluded by 'reaching' is if a woman inserted the nipple of her breast into the mouth of an infant and it is not known whether the milk entered his throat or not, marriage is not prohibited because there is doubt in the preventer. This is in al-Walwaljiyya. And in al-Qunyah: A woman used to give her breast to a girl and this became known among them, then she said there was no milk in her breast when she gave her the breast, and no one knows that except from her, her son is permitted to marry this girl, end. And in al-Khaniyya: A girl was breastfed by many people of a village, few or many, and it is not known who breastfed her, and one of the villagers wanted to marry her. Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar said: If no sign appears to him and no one testifies to that, it is permissible to marry her, end. And in al-Walwaljiyya: It is obligatory upon women not to breastfeed every boy without necessity, but if they do, they should memorize or write down, end. And in al-Khaniyya from the section of prohibition and permissibility: A woman breastfeeds a boy without the permission of her husband, it is disliked for her unless she fears the infant's destruction, then it is not objectionable. It should be obligatory upon her when destruction is feared, to preserve life. And in al-Muhit: A man should not give his child to a foolish woman to breastfeed, because the Prophet, peace be upon him, forbade the milk of a foolish woman and said 'Milk transmits'. He only forbade because giving to a foolish woman subjects his child to destruction due to her preservation and care or bad manners, for she does not train him well, so the child grows up ill-mannered. His saying 'milk transmits' possibly means that the foolish woman does not avoid things harmful to the child, so it affects her milk and harms the boy. This agrees with what doctors say, for they command the wet nurse to avoid things that cause illness. And possibly he forbade that so that if something happens coincidentally, it is not attributed to contagion, as narrated from Ali, may Allah be pleased with him: 'Do not travel when the moon is in Scorpio.' So this, if authentic, is so that if a coincidence occurs, it is not attributed to the moon being in Scorpio, thus being belief in stars and denial of reports, end. By what we have established, it appears that the author's definition is defective in inclusion by the infant's little sucking about which he forbade. What is meant by sucking is reaching the stomach through the two passages, by using the cause and intending the result, so there is no defect. But al-Nahr said: An objector may say we do not accept the existence of the sucking of milk when we do not know whether it reached or not, due to the customary correlation between sucking and reaching linguistically. Al-Qamus said: 'I sucked it' etc. His claim that from the breast of a human, and as for wajur and sa'ut, they are annexed like amassahu, end. How can it be correct with the sucking? At most, he specified it following the usual. And conversely, if it remained on its apparent meaning, then there is sucking but no rada' if it does not reach the stomach, and sucking is negated in wajur and sa'ut but rada' is not negated. And al-thady (breast) is masculine as in al-Mughrib. In al-Misbah: The breast is for women, and it is also said for men, said by Ibn al-Sikkit, and it is masculine and feminine: 'huwa al-thady' and 'hiya al-thady', plural 'athdun' and 'thidiyyun', originally 'af'ul' and 'fu'ul' like 'aflus' and 'fulus', and sometimes pluralized as 'thidaa' like 'sahmun' and 'sihaam', end.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the definition of rada' (fosterage). The author clarifies that the cause of rada' is the milk of a human woman reaching the stomach of a child through the mouth or nose during the prescribed period. The method of delivery does not matter: whether the child sucks directly, drinks expressed milk, or it is poured or instilled. The key is that the milk reaches the stomach. The passage also discusses various scenarios: doubt about the milk reaching, the ruling on breastfeeding without husband's permission (disliked unless necessity), and the undesirability of employing a foolish wet nurse. It defends the matn's definition against a criticism, explaining that 'sucking' in the definition is meant broadly as the means, not the literal act. The commentary is rich with references to Hanafi fiqh works such as al-Khaniyya, al-Walwaljiyya, al-Qunyah, and al-Muhit.

Key Terms
رضاع (rada'): The milk of a human female reaching the stomach of a child through mouth or nose within the prescribed period.
مص (massa): Literal sucking; in the definition it is used broadly to mean any means of milk reaching the stomach.
وجور (wajur): Pouring milk into the mouth of the child.
سعوط (sa'ut): Instilling milk into the nose.
سبب (sabab): The cause that triggers the legal ruling of prohibition (mahramiyyah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following methods of feeding does NOT establish rada'?
A) Suckling directly from the breast
B) Drinking milk from a bottle
C) Instilling milk into the ear
D) Snuffing milk into the nose

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, rada' is established by human milk reaching the infant's stomach via mouth or nose, regardless of the method of feeding.
