Rada' Prohibition: Quantity and Time Limit in Hanafi Fiqh
Explaining rada' prohibition and time limit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the quantity and time limit of rada' that establishes marriage prohibition, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the duration.

Core Idea
Any amount of breastfeeding within thirty months creates the same marriage prohibitions as lineage.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the rules of rada' (breastfeeding) that establish mahramiyyah. The matn states that even a little breastfeeding within thirty months prohibits. The author provides evidence from the famous hadith 'yuharramu min al-rada'i ma yuharramu min al-nasab' and addresses the abrogation of the hadith that one or two sucklings do not prohibit. He also discusses the time limit dispute within the Hanafi school between the relied-upon narration (thirty months) and the opinion of the Sahibayn (two years).

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn statement
The matn says: 'وحرم به وإن قل في ثلاثين شهر' meaning 'And it prohibits, even if little, in thirty months.' This is the core ruling.
2
Recognize the primary dalil
The author cites the hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim: 'يَحْرُمُ مِنَ الرَّضَاعِ مَا يَحْرُمُ مِنَ النَّسَبِ'. This is a mutawatir hadith with qati' thubut and dalala.
Also support from Quran 4:23 'wa akhawatukum min al-rada'ah'.
3
Understand the abrogation (naskh)
The hadith 'La tuharrimu al-massatu wa al-massataan' (no prohibition by one or two sucklings) is abrogated, as stated by Ibn Abbas. This removes any specific number requirement.
Hanafi accepts naskh of hadith by hadith.
4
Distinguish the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Zahir al-riwayah (Abu Hanifa) holds the limit is thirty months, even after weaning. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) restrict it to two years (the period of breastfeeding before weaning).
The difference hinges on interpretation of Quranic 'around two years' (2:233) and the growth effect.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Despite some scholars favoring the two-year limit, the fatwa is on the thirty-month limit because zahir al-riwayah has precedence in fatwa.
See al-Walwalijiyya and Fath al-Qadir: الفتوى على ظاهر الرواية.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وحرم به وإن قل في ثلاثين شهر إما حرم ما حرم به النسب قرابة وصهرية في هذه المدة ولو كان الرضاع قليلاً لحديث الصحيحين المشهور يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب ومعناه أن الحرمة بسبب الرضاع تعتبر بحرمة النسب فشمل حليلة الابن والأب من الرضاع لأنها حرام بسبب النسب فكذا الرضاع وهو قول أكثر أهل العلم كذا في المبسوط وفي القنية : زنى بامرأة يحرم عليه بنتها من الرضاع ا . اهـ. ولإطلاق قوله تعالى وأخواتكم من الرضاعة ﴾ [النساء: ٢٣] قلنا : لا فرق بين القليل والكثير وأما حديث لا تحرم المصة ولا المصتان»(۲) وما دل على التقدير فمنسوخ صرح بنسخه ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما حين قيل له إن الناس يقولون إن الرضعة لا تحرم فقال : كان ذلك ثم نسخ والرضاع وإن قل يحصل به نشو بقدره فكان الرضاع مطلقاً مظنة بالنسبة إلى الصغير وفسر القليل في الينابيع بما يعلم أنه وصل إلى الجوف، وقيد بالثلاثين لأن الرضاع بعدها لا يوجب التحريم، وأفاد بإطلاقه أنها ثابتة بعد الفطام والاستغناء بالطعام وهو ظاهر الرواية كما في الخانية، وعليه الفتوى كما في الولوالجية. وفي فتح القدير معزياً إلى واقعات الناطفي : الفتوى على ظاهر الرواية، فما ذكره الشارح من أن الفتوى على رواية الحسن من عدم ثبوتها بعده فخلاف المعتمد لما علم من أن الفتوى إذا اختلف كان الترجيح لظاهر الرواية. وأشار بجعل المدة ظرفاً للمحرمة أنها ليست مدة استحقاق الأجر على الأب بل اتفقوا أنه لا تجب أجرة الإرضاع بعد الحولين وكذا لا يجب عليها الإرضاع ديانة بعدهما كما في المجتبى وهما محمل ذكر الحولين في التنزيل وفي فتح القدير : الأصح قولهما من الاقتصار على الحولين في حق التحريم أيضاً وبه أخذ الطحاوي. ومراده بالنظر إلى الدليل .
(۱) رواه البخاري في كتاب النكاح باب ۲۰، ۲۷ مسلم في كتاب الرضاع حديث ١، ٢، ٩، ١٢. أبو داود في كتاب النكاح باب .٦ ابن ماجه في كتاب النكاح باب .٣٤ الموطأ في كتاب الرضاع حديث ١، ٢، ١٦. أحمد في مسنده (٢٧٥/١) (٤/٤، ٥).
(۲) رواه مسلم في كتاب الرضاع حدیث ،۱۷ ، ۲۰ ، ۲۳. أبو داود في كتاب النكاح باب ١٠. الترمذي في كتاب الرضاع باب . النسائي في كتاب النكاح باب .٥١ ابن ماجه في كتاب النكاح باب ٣٥. أحمد في مسنده (٤/٤، ٥) (٣١/٦، ٩٦).
His saying: (And it prohibits, even if little, in thirty months) meaning that it prohibits what lineage prohibits of kinship and in-law relationship in this period, even if the breastfeeding was little, due to the famous hadith in the Sahihayn: 'What is prohibited through breastfeeding is what is prohibited through lineage.' Its meaning is that the prohibition due to breastfeeding is considered like the prohibition of lineage. So it includes the wife of the son and the father from breastfeeding, because they are prohibited due to lineage, and similarly breastfeeding. This is the saying of most scholars as in al-Mabsut. And in al-Qunyah: If one commits adultery with a woman, his daughter from breastfeeding is prohibited to him, end. And due to the absolute nature of His saying: 'And your sisters from breastfeeding' [al-Nisa 23]. We say: There is no difference between little and much. As for the hadith 'One suckling or two do not make prohibited' and what indicates a number, it is abrogated. Ibn Abbas explicitly stated its abrogation when it was said to him that people say one suckling does not prohibit, he said: That was then abrogated. And breastfeeding, even if little, produces growth according to its extent, so breastfeeding absolutely is a cause for prohibition in relation to the infant. And 'little' is explained in al-Yanabi' as what is known to have reached the stomach. And it is restricted to thirty because breastfeeding after it does not necessitate prohibition. And his absolute wording indicates that it is established after weaning and independence from food, and this is the apparent narration as in al-Khaniyya, and upon it is the fatwa as in al-Walwaljiyya. In Fath al-Qadir attributing to Waqi'at al-Natafi: The fatwa is upon the apparent narration. So what the sharh mentioned that the fatwa is upon the narration of al-Hasan of non-establishment after it is against the relied upon, because it is known that when the fatwa differs, preference is given to the apparent narration. And by making the period a container for the prohibited, he indicated that it is not a period for deserving wages from the father; rather they agreed that the wage for breastfeeding is not obligatory after two years, and similarly it is not obligatory upon her to breastfeed religiously after them as in al-Mujtaba. And these two are the interpretation of the mention of two years in the Revelation. In Fath al-Qadir: The most correct is their saying (i.e., Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) of restricting to two years regarding prohibition also, and al-Tahawi adopted it. And he meant by it looking at the evidence.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's statement that breastfeeding, even in small amounts, within thirty months establishes the same marriage prohibitions as lineage. The author cites the well-known hadith 'What is prohibited through breastfeeding is what is prohibited through lineage' as evidence. He then discusses the abrogation of the hadith that one or two sucklings do not prohibit, relying on the explicit statement of Ibn Abbas. The passage then addresses the time limit: the relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah) is that breastfeeding after thirty months does not create prohibition, and this is the fatwa. However, there is a difference within the Hanafi school: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the prohibition is limited to the first two years (the period of breastfeeding before weaning). The author notes that the more correct opinion according to some is the two-year limit, but the fatwa remains on the apparent narration (thirty months). The passage clarifies that the two-year mention in the Quran is about the mother's right to wages, not about the period for prohibition.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted ruling from the six core books of Imam Muhammad; here it refers to the thirty-month limit.
قولهما (qawlahuma): The opinion of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two companions).
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a prior ruling by a later one; here the hadith about one or two sucklings is abrogated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon fatwa (mufta bihi), how long after birth can breastfeeding create marriage prohibition?
A) Two years
B) Thirty months
C) Until weaning
D) Any time

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, any amount of rada' within thirty months creates the same marriage prohibitions as blood lineage, and the fatwa is on the thirty-month limit.

Nikah — Marriage

The Core Ruling: Fosterage Creates Lineage-Like Prohibitions
Opening ruling with proof from hadith and abrogation discussion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that breastfeeding within thirty months creates the same marriage prohibitions as blood lineage and identify the primary proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Breastfeeding, even a little, within thirty months makes the same relatives forbidden as your own blood relatives.

The Book of Fosterage opens with a powerful analogy: what is forbidden by lineage is also forbidden by fosterage. This lesson unpacks the core ruling and its foundational proof from the Prophet's hadith, establishing the general principle that shapes the entire chapter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Locate the phrase 'وحرم به وإن قل في ثلاثين شهر ما حرم به النسب'. Note that the ruling covers any amount of milk, even a drop, provided it is within thirty months.
The ruling is general: all lineage prohibitions apply.
2
Find the primary proof (dalil)
Read the commentary's citation of the hadith 'يَحْرُمُ مِنَ الرَّضَاعِ مَا يَحْرُمُ مِنَ النَّسَبِ' from Bukhari and Muslim. Understand that this is the key textual evidence.
The hadith is mutawatir in meaning, though ahad in transmission.
3
Understand the abrogation issue
The commentary mentions that the hadith specifying 'one or two sucks do not forbid' is abrogated by this general hadith, as declared by Ibn Abbas.
This removes any quantity requirement.
4
Confirm the duration
The ruling is restricted to thirty months. The commentary uses Quran 46:15 to derive this period: six months minimum pregnancy + twenty-four months weaning.
After thirty months, fosterage does not create prohibitions.

كتاب الرضاع
قوله : (وحرم به وإن قل في ثلاثين شهر ما حرم به النسب) إلا أم أخته وأخت ابنه زوج مرضعة لبنها منه أب وعكساً لو بقي على ظاهره فإنه يوجد المص ولا رضاع إن لم يصل إلى الجوف وينتفي المصى في الوجور والسعوط ولم ينتف الرضاع والثدي مذكر كما في المغرب. وفي المصباح : الثدي للمرأة وقد يقال في الرجل أيضاً قاله ابن السكيت ويذكر ويؤنث فيقال هو الثدي وهي الثدي والجمع أثد وثدي وأصلها أفعل وفعول مثل أفلس وفلوس وربما جمع على ثداء مثل سهم وسهام ا هـ .
قوله : (وحرم به وإن قل في ثلاثين شهر) أي حرم بسبب الرضاع ما حرم بسبب النسب قرابة وصهرية في هذه المدة ولو كان الرضاع قليلاً لحديث الصحيحين المشهور يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب ومعناه أن الحرمة بسبب الرضاع تعتبر بحرمة النسب فشمل حليلة الابن والأب من الرضاع لأنها حرام بسبب النسب فكذا الرضاع وهو قول أكثر أهل العلم كذا في المبسوط وفي القنية : زنى بامرأة يحرم عليه بنتها من الرضاع ا . اهـ. ولإطلاق قوله تعالى وأخواتكم من الرضاعة ﴾ [النساء: ٢٣] قلنا : لا فرق بين القليل والكثير وأما حديث لا تحرم المصة ولا المصتان»(۲) وما دل على التقدير فمنسوخ صرح بنسخه ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما حين قيل له إن الناس يقولون إن الرضعة لا تحرم فقال : كان ذلك ثم نسخ والرضاع وإن قل يحصل به نشو بقدره فكان الرضاع مطلقاً مظنة بالنسبة إلى الصغير وفسر القليل في الينابيع بما يعلم أنه وصل إلى الجوف، وقيد بالثلاثين لأن الرضاع بعدها لا يوجب التحريم، وأفاد بإطلاقه أنها ثابتة بعد الفطام والاستغناء بالطعام وهو ظاهر الرواية كما في الخانية، وعليه الفتوى كما في الولوالجية. وفي فتح القدير معزياً إلى واقعات الناطفي : الفتوى على ظاهر الرواية، فما ذكره الشارح من أن الفتوى على رواية الحسن من عدم ثبوتها بعده فخلاف المعتمد لما علم من أن الفتوى إذا اختلف كان الترجيح لظاهر الرواية. وأشار بجعل المدة ظرفاً للمحرمة أنها ليست مدة استحقاق الأجر على الأب بل اتفقوا أنه لا تجب أجرة الإرضاع بعد الحولين وكذا لا يجب عليها الإرضاع ديانة بعدهما كما في المجتبى وهما محمل ذكر الحولين في التنزيل وفي فتح القدير : الأصح قولهما من الاقتصار على الحولين في حق التحريم أيضاً وبه أخذ الطحاوي. ومراده بالنظر إلى الدليل حسب ظنه وإلا فالمذهب للإمام الأعظم وإن لم يظهر دليله لوجوب العمل على المقلد بقول المجتهد من غير نظر في الدليل كما أشار إليه في أول الخانية ولكن قال في آخر الحاوي القدسي: فإن خالفاه قال بعضهم يؤخذ بقوله، وقال بعضهم يؤخذ بقولهما، وقيل يخير المفتي، والأصح أن العبرة لقوة الدليل ا هـ . ولا يخفى قوة دليلهما فإن قوله تعالى والوالدات يرضعن أولادهن حولين كاملين لمن أراد أن يتم الرضاعة [البقرة: ٢٣٣] يدل على أنه لا رضاع بعد التمام، وأما قوله تعالى فإن أراد فصالاً عن تراض منهما وتشاور فلا جناح عليهما ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۳۳] فإنما هو قبل الحولين بدليل تقييده بالتراضي والتشاور أنه وبعدهما لا يحتاج إليهما، وبه يضعف ما في معراج الدراية معزياً إلى المبسوط والمحيط من بعد الحولين فيكون دليلاً له لما علمت من ضياع القيدين حينئذ، وأما استدلال صاحب الهداية للإمام بقوله تعالى وحمله وفصاله ثلاثون شهرا [الأحقاف : ١٥] بناء على أن المدة لكل منهما وقد قام المنقص في الحمل فبقى الفصال على حاله فقد رجع إلى الحق في باب ثبوت النسب من الثلاثين لهما للحمل ستة أشهر والعامان للفصال واختلفوا في إباحته بعد المدة واقتصر الشارح على المنع وهو الصحيح كما في شرح المنظومة، وعلى هذا لا يجوز الانتفاع به للتداوي قال في فتح القدير وأهل الطب يثبتون للبن البنت أي الذي نزل بسبب بنت مرضعة نفعاً لوجع العين. واختلف المشايخ فيه قيل لا يجوز، وقيل يجوز إذا علم أنه يزول به الرمد، ولا يخفى أن حقيقة العلم متعذر فالمراد إذا غلب على الظن وإلا فهو معنى المنع ا هـ . ولا يخفى أن التداوي بالمحرم لا يجوز في ظاهر المذهب أصله بول ما يؤكل لحمه فإنه لا يشرب أصلاً. وفي الجوهرة وللأب إجبار أمته على فطام ولدها منه قبل الحولين إذا لم يضره الفطام كما له أن يجبرها على الإرضاع وليس له أن يأمر زوجته الحرة على الفطام قبلهما لأن لها حق التربية إلى تمام مدة الإرضاع إلا أن تختار ذلك كما أنه ليس له إجبارها على الإرضاع ا هـ. وفي البزازية : والرضاع في دار الإسلام ودار الحرب سواء حتى إذا رضع في دار الحرب أسلموا وخرجوا إلى دارنا ثبتت أحكام الرضاع فيما بينهم ا هـ . قوله : (إلا) أم أخته وأخت ابنه يعني فإنهما يحلان من الرضاع دون النسب. أطلق المضاف والمضاف إليه ففي أم أخته ثلاث صور الأولى الأم رضاعاً والأخت نسباً بأن أرضعت أجنبية أخته نسباً ولم ترضعه الثانية عكسه أن يكون لأخته رضاعاً أم من النسب. الثالثة أن يكونا رضاعاً بأن أرضعت امرأة صبياً وصبية ولهذه الصبية أم أخرى من الرضاع لم ترضع الصبي. وفي أخت ابنه ثلاث أيضاً فالأولى أن تكون الأخت رضاعاً فقط بأن كان له ابن من النسب ولهذا الابن أخت من الرضاعة ارتضعا على غير امرأة أبيه . والثانية أن يكون الابن رضاعاً فقط وله أخت من النسب. الثالثة أن يكونا رضاعاً. ومراده من الابن الولد فيشمل البنت وفي شرح الوقاية فإن قيل : قوله إلا أم أخته إن أريد بالأم الأم رضاعاً
Book of Fosterage. His statement: (And what is forbidden by it, even if little, within thirty months, is what is forbidden by lineage) except the mother of his sister and the sister of his son. The husband of a wet nurse, her milk from him is father and vice versa if it remains apparent. Then the sucking exists, and there is no fosterage if it does not reach the stomach. Sucking is negated in the case of [drink injected into the throat] and snuff, but fosterage is not negated. The breast is masculine as in al-Mughrib, and in al-Misbah: the breast is for a woman and may be said for a man as well, said by Ibn al-Sikkit, and it is masculine and feminine, so it is said 'al-thady' and 'al-thadya', plural 'athd' and 'thudiyy', and their original is af'al and fu'ul like aflas and fulus, and sometimes pluralized as 'thida' like sahm and siham. End. His statement: (And what is forbidden by it, even if little, within thirty months) meaning that what is forbidden by lineage of kinship and marriage affinity is forbidden due to fosterage within this period, even if the fosterage was little, due to the well-known hadith of the two Sahihs: 'What is forbidden by fosterage is what is forbidden by lineage' and its meaning is that prohibition due to fosterage is considered by the prohibition of lineage, so it includes the wife of the son and the father from fosterage because she is forbidden due to lineage, so likewise fosterage. And this is the saying of most scholars. As in al-Mabsut. And in al-Qunyah: He committed adultery with a woman; her daughter from fosterage becomes forbidden to him. End. And due to the generality of His statement: 'And your sisters from fosterage' [Quran 4:23]. We said: There is no difference between little and much. As for the hadith: 'One suck or two sucks do not make forbidden' and what indicates specification, it is abrogated. Its abrogation was declared by Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, when it was said to him that people say that one suck does not forbid, so he said: That was the case, then it was abrogated. And fosterage, even if little, achieves growth to its extent, so fosterage absolutely is a presumption relative to the small child. And 'little' was interpreted in al-Yanabi' as what is known to have reached the stomach. And it was restricted to thirty because fosterage after it does not cause prohibition. And by its absolute [mention] it indicates that it is established after weaning and independence from food, and this is the apparent narration as in al-Khaniyyah, and upon it is the fatwa as in al-Walwaljiyyah. In Fath al-Qadir attributed to Waqi'at al-Natifi: The fatwa is on the apparent narration. So what the commentator mentioned that the fatwa is on the narration of al-Hasan regarding its non-establishment after it is contrary to the relied-upon, because it is known that when the fatwa differs, preference is given to the apparent narration. And by making the period a container for the prohibition, he indicated that it is not a period for deserving compensation from the father; rather they agreed that the wages for suckling are not obligatory after two years, and likewise it is not obligatory for her to suckle religiously after them as in al-Mujtaba. And they are the focus of the mention of two years in the revelation. And in Fath al-Qadir: The sounder view is the saying of them both (Sahibayn) of limiting to two years regarding prohibition as well, and al-Tahawi adopted it. And his intention is according to the evidence in his estimation; otherwise the madhhab is of the Greatest Imam even if its evidence is not apparent, because it is obligatory for the layperson to act upon the statement of the mujtahid without looking into the evidence, as alluded to in the beginning of al-Khaniyyah. But in the end of al-Hawi al-Qudsi, it is said: If they both oppose him, some say his saying is taken, some say both of their sayings are taken, and it is said the mufti is given choice, and the correct is that consideration is given to the strength of evidence. End. And the strength of their evidence is not hidden: His statement: 'And mothers shall suckle their children for two complete years for whoever desires to complete the suckling' [Quran 2:233] indicates that there is no fosterage after completion. As for His statement: 'But if they desire to wean by mutual consent and consultation, then no sin upon them' [Quran 2:233] it is only before two years, as indicated by its restriction to mutual consent and consultation; after them there is no need for them, and by this what is in Miraj al-Dirayah attributed to al-Mabsut and al-Muhit is weakened: that after two years there is fosterage, so it would be evidence for him because of what you know of the loss of the two conditions then. As for the argument of the author of al-Hidayah for the Imam by His statement: 'And his gestation and his weaning are thirty months' [Quran 46:15] based on the fact that the period is for each of them, and the deficiency has occurred in gestation, so weaning remains as it is, then he has returned to the truth in the chapter of establishing lineage from the thirty: for them pregnancy is six months and two years for weaning. And they differed about its permissibility after the period, and the commentator restricted to prohibition, and it is the correct view as in Sharh al-Manzumah. And on this, it is not permissible to benefit from it for medication. He said in Fath al-Qadir: And the physicians affirm for the milk of the girl, i.e., that which descended due to a nursing daughter, benefit for eye pain. And the mashayikh differed: it is said not permissible, and it is said it is permissible if it is known that the inflammation will be removed by it. And it is not hidden that true knowledge is unattainable; so the meaning is when it is strongly presumed, otherwise it is the meaning of prohibition. End. And it is not hidden that medication with what is forbidden is not permissible in the apparent madhhab, its origin is the urine of what is eaten for its meat, for it is not drunk at all. In al-Jawharah: And the father has the right to compel his slave woman to wean his child before two years if weaning does not harm it, just as he has the right to compel her to suckle. But he does not have the right to order his free wife to wean before them because she has the right of upbringing until the completion of the period of suckling, unless she chooses that, just as he does not have the right to compel her to suckle. End. In al-Bazzaziyyah: And fosterage in the abode of Islam and the abode of war are equal, such that if they suckle in the abode of war and then become Muslim and come out to our abode, the rulings of fosterage are established among them. End. His statement: (except the mother of his sister and the sister of his son) means that they become permissible from fosterage unlike lineage. The mudaf and mudaf ilayh are unrestricted; so concerning the mother of his sister there are three forms: first: the mother by fosterage and the sister by lineage, i.e., a stranger suckled his sister by lineage and did not suckle him. Second: the opposite, that his sister is by fosterage and the mother by lineage. Third: that both are by fosterage, i.e., a woman suckled a boy and a girl, and this girl has another mother by fosterage who did not suckle the boy. Concerning the sister of his son there are also three: first: the sister is only by fosterage, i.e., he has a son by lineage and this son has a sister by fosterage who suckled from other than his father's wife. Second: the son is only by fosterage and he has a sister by lineage. Third: both are by fosterage. And by 'son' he means child, so it includes the daughter. In Sharh al-Wiqayah: For if it is said: His statement 'except the mother of his sister' if by 'mother' is meant mother by fosterage, she is...
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq in the Book of Fosterage (Kitab al-Rada'). The passage type is a ruling with proof, combined with an intra-Hanafi dispute. The main ruling is that breastfeeding, even if little, within thirty months establishes the same marriage prohibitions as blood relations, with the exception of the mother of one's sister and the sister of one's son. The commentator explains the rationale: the famous hadith 'What is forbidden by fosterage is what is forbidden by lineage' from Bukhari and Muslim is the primary proof. The Quranic verse 'And your sisters from fosterage' (4:23) is also cited to show the generality. The hadith specifying one or two sucks is considered abrogated by the companion Ibn Abbas. The duration of thirty months is based on the verse in Surah al-Ahqaf (46:15) combining pregnancy and weaning, with pregnancy being six months minimum. However, the two disciples (Sahibayn) limit the prohibition to two years based on Quran 2:233. The commentator sides with the Zahir al-Riwayah position (Imam Abu Hanifa's view of thirty months) and states that the fatwa is on the apparent narration. There is a discussion about using breast milk for medicine; the relied-upon view is that it is not permissible because it is a forbidden substance (since it establishes kinship). The passage then details the exception: 'except the mother of his sister and the sister of his son.' These two relations are not prohibited by fosterage. The commentator exhaustively enumerates the possible scenarios for each exception, showing when the mother or sister is by fosterage versus lineage, and concludes that in all cases they remain halal from the fosterage perspective. This is a key nuance: not every relation forbidden by lineage is forbidden by fosterage; only those specifically covered by the hadith's analogy. The mother of a sister is not covered because the prohibition of a mother is through being the wife of the father or through the daughter's lineage, which is not replicated by fosterage. Similarly for the sister of a son.

Key Terms
رضاع (radā'): Fosterage or breastfeeding; the act of a child suckling milk from a woman (foster mother), which establishes legal kinship.
نسب (nasab): Blood lineage or descent, which establishes marriage prohibitions and inheritance rights.
ثلاثون شهرا (thalāthūna shahran): Thirty months, the maximum period within which breastfeeding can establish marriage prohibitions according to Imam Abu Hanifa.
مص (mass): Sucking or directly drinking milk from the breast, which is required for the establishment of fosterage.
ظاهر الرواية (zāhir al-riwāyah): The apparent or well-known narration from the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, considered the most authoritative source of rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) duration for fosterage to create marriage prohibitions in the Hanafi school?
A) Two years (twenty-four months)
B) Thirty months
C) Until weaning regardless of age
D) Only during the first year

Key Takeaway
Breastfeeding, even a little, within thirty months from birth creates the same marriage prohibitions as blood relations, based on the hadith 'يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب'.

Exceptions in Fosterage: Mother of Sister and Sister of Son
Analyzing exceptions to prohibition by fosterage and their rationale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi exceptions to fosterage prohibition for the mother of one's sister and sister of one's son, explain the rationale based on the absence of the effective cause ('illa), and apply the principle to additional cases.

Core Idea
Fosterage prohibits only when the same prohibited meaning as lineage exists—absent that, marriage is halal.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses exceptions to the general rule that fosterage creates marital prohibitions similar to lineage. The author highlights two specific cases—the mother of one's sister and the sister of one's son—that remain permissible despite a fosterage link. The reasoning is grounded in the Hanafi usul principle that rulings depend on the presence of the effective cause ('illa). By understanding this, you will be able to identify and derive other exceptions.

Guided Path
1
State the two exceptions
Locate in the text the two named exceptions: 'mother of one's sister' (umm akhih) and 'sister of one's son' (ukht ibnih). Note that they are permissible (halal) by fosterage but prohibited by lineage.
2
Analyze the three scenarios for each exception
For each exception, the text gives three possibilities: the relative (mother/sister) is from fosterage only, from lineage only, or both. Understand why each scenario yields permissibility or prohibition accordingly.
The key is that the exception applies when the fosterage link does not create the same prohibited relation.
3
Identify the effective cause (al-'illa)
The reason for prohibition in lineage is being one's mother or daughter (etc.). In fosterage, the rule is that the same prohibited meaning must exist. In these exceptions, the 'illa is absent: the mother of one's sister is not one's own mother, and the sister of one's son is not one's own daughter.
This is the basis for extending the ruling to other similar cases.
4
Apply the 'illa to additional cases
The text lists further cases where the same reasoning applies: mother of one's uncle/aunt, etc. Generalize the principle: any relation that is prohibited by lineage solely because of a link that does not hold in fosterage becomes permissible.
The commentator notes these can multiply to over 60 images when considering permutations.
5
Note the dispute on breastfeeding after two years
The passage begins with a discussion on whether breastfeeding after two years counts for fosterage prohibitions. Abu Hanifa says yes, the Sahibayn say no. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is the Sahibayn's, which affects the scope of fosterage.
This is the general rule; the exceptions are independent of this dispute but rely on the same effective cause reasoning.

كتاب الرضاع
حسب
ظنه وإلا فالمذهب للإمام الأعظم وإن لم يظهر دليله لوجوب العمل على المقلد بقول المجتهد من غير نظر في الدليل كما أشار إليه في أول الخانية ولكن قال في آخر الحاوي القدسي: فإن خالفاه قال بعضهم يؤخذ بقوله، وقال بعضهم يؤخذ بقولهما، وقيل يخير المفتي، والأصح أن العبرة لقوة الدليل ا هـ . ولا يخفى قوة دليلهما فإن قوله تعالى والوالدات يرضعن أولادهن حولين كاملين لمن أراد أن يتم الرضاعة [البقرة: ٢٣٣] يدل على أنه لا رضاع بعد التمام، وأما قوله تعالى فإن أراد فصالاً عن تراض منهما وتشاور فلا جناح عليهما ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۳۳] فإنما هو قبل الحولين بدليل تقييده بالتراضي والتشاور أنه وبعدهما لا يحتاج إليهما، وبه يضعف ما في معراج الدراية معزياً إلى المبسوط والمحيط من بعد الحولين فيكون دليلاً له لما علمت من ضياع القيدين حينئذ، وأما استدلال صاحب الهداية للإمام بقوله تعالى وحمله وفصاله ثلاثون شهرا [الأحقاف : ١٥] بناء على أن المدة لكل منهما وقد قام المنقص في الحمل فبقى الفصال على حاله فقد رجع إلى الحق في باب ثبوت النسب من الثلاثين لهما للحمل ستة أشهر والعامان للفصال واختلفوا في إباحته بعد المدة واقتصر الشارح على المنع وهو الصحيح كما في شرح المنظومة، وعلى هذا لا يجوز الانتفاع به للتداوي قال في فتح القدير وأهل الطب يثبتون للبن البنت أي الذي نزل بسبب بنت مرضعة نفعاً لوجع العين. واختلف المشايخ فيه قيل لا يجوز، وقيل يجوز إذا علم أنه يزول به الرمد، ولا يخفى أن حقيقة العلم متعذر فالمراد إذا غلب على الظن وإلا فهو معنى المنع ا هـ . ولا يخفى أن التداوي بالمحرم لا يجوز في ظاهر المذهب أصله بول ما يؤكل لحمه فإنه لا يشرب أصلاً. وفي الجوهرة وللأب إجبار أمته على فطام ولدها منه قبل الحولين إذا لم يضره الفطام كما له أن يجبرها على الإرضاع وليس له أن يأمر زوجته الحرة على الفطام قبلهما لأن لها حق التربية إلى تمام مدة الإرضاع إلا أن تختار ذلك كما أنه ليس له إجبارها على الإرضاع ا هـ. وفي البزازية : والرضاع في دار الإسلام ودار الحرب سواء حتى إذا رضع في دار الحرب أسلموا وخرجوا إلى دارنا ثبتت أحكام الرضاع فيما بينهم ا هـ . قوله : (إلا) أم أخته وأخت ابنه يعني فإنهما يحلان من الرضاع دون النسب. أطلق المضاف والمضاف إليه ففي أم أخته ثلاث صور الأولى الأم رضاعاً والأخت نسباً بأن أرضعت أجنبية أخته نسباً ولم ترضعه الثانية عكسه أن يكون لأخته رضاعاً أم من النسب. الثالثة أن يكونا رضاعاً بأن أرضعت امرأة صبياً وصبية ولهذه الصبية أم أخرى من الرضاع لم ترضع الصبي. وفي أخت ابنه ثلاث أيضاً فالأولى أن تكون الأخت رضاعاً فقط بأن كان له ابن من النسب ولهذا الابن أخت من الرضاعة ارتضعا على غير امرأة أبيه . والثانية أن يكون الابن رضاعاً فقط وله أخت من النسب. والثالثة أن يكونا رضاعاً. ومراده من الابن الولد فيشمل البنت وفي شرح الوقاية فإن قيل : قوله إلا أم أخته إن أريد بالأم الأم رضاعاً
هي

٣٩٠
كتاب الرضاع
وبالأخت الأخت رضاعاً لا يشمل ما إذا كانت إحداهما فقط بطريق الرضاع، وإن أريد بالأم الأم نسباً وبالأخت الأخت رضاعاً أو بالعكس لا يشمل الصورتين الأخريين. قلنا : المراد ما إذا كانت إحداهما بطريق الرضاع أعم من أن تكون إحداهما فقط أو كل منهما ا هـ. ولا شك أن السبب في استثناء هذين عدم وجود العلة فإنها في التحريم من الرضاع وجود المعنى المحرم في النسب ولم توجد في هذين، أما في الأولى فلان أم أخته من النسب إنما حرمت لكونها أمه أو موطوءة أبيه وهو مفقود في الرضاع. أما في الثانية فلأن أخت ابنه نسباً إنما حرمت لكونها بنته أو بنت امرأته ولم يوجد في الرضاع، فعلم أنه لا حصر في كلامه وقد ثبت ذلك الانتفاء في صور أخرى فزاد على الصورتين في الوقاية أربعة : أم عمه وعمته وأم خاله وخالته لأن أم هؤلاء موطوءة الجد الصحيح أو الفاسد ولا كذلك من الرضاع، وفي شرحها ولا تنس الصور الثلاث في جميع ما ذكرنا ا.هـ. يعني من اعتبار الرضاع في المضاف فقط أو المضاف إليه فقط أو فيهما، وزاد الشارحون صوراً أخرى : الأولى أم حفدته رضاعاً بأن أرضعت أجنبية ولد ولده فله أن يتزوج بهذه المرأة بخلافه من النسب لأنها حليلة ابنه أو بنته ولم يوجد هذا المعنى في الرضاع، وفي المصباح حفد حفداً . خدم فهو حافد والجمع حفدة مثل كافر وكفرة ومنه قيل للأعوان حفدة، وقيل لأولاد الأولاد حفدة لأنهم كالخدام في الصغر ا هـ . والمراد هنا أولاد الأولاد والثانية جدة ولده من الرضاع بأن أرضعت أجنبية ولده ولها أم فإنه يجوز له التزوج بهذه الأم بخلافه من النسب لأنها أمه أو أم امرأته. الثالثة عمة الولد من الرضاع بأن كان لزوج المرضعة أخت فلأب الرضيع أن يتزوجها بخلافه من النسب لأنها أخته ولم يذكروا خالة ولده لأنها حلال من النسب أيضاً لأنها أخت زوجته . الرابعة يحل للمرأة التزوج بأبي أخيها من الرضاع أو بأخي ولدها من الرضاع وبأبي حفدتها من الرضاع وبجد ولدها من الرضاع وبخال ولدها من الرضاع، ولا يجوز ذلك كله من النسب لما قلنا في حق الرجل. ثم اعلم أن ما ذكرناه من صحة اعتبار الرضاع في المضاف فقط أو في المضاف إليه فقط أو فيهما يطرد في جميع الصور كما ذكره ابن وهبان في شرح المنظومة، وأفاد أنها تبلغ ستين مسألة ونيفاً ليس هذا المختصر موضع ذكرها، وأحال إلى الذهن في حل بعضها وتبعه في الإضراب عن حلها العلامة عبد البر الشحنة . بن
وأقول في بيان حلها : إن مسألتي الكتاب أربع وعشرون صورة لأن لأم أخيه بتذكير الأخ وبتأنيث الأخت صورتين لجواز إضافة الأم إلى الأخ والأخت، وكل منهما بالاعتبارات الثلاثة فهي ستة ولأخت ابنه بتذكير الابن وتأنيث البنت صورتين لجواز إضافة الأخت إلى الابن والبنت وبالاعتبارات ستة، ولكل من الاثني عشر صورتان إما باعتبار ما يحل للرجل أو ما يحل للمرأة فإنه كما يجوز له التزوج بأم أخيه يجوز لها التزوج بأبي أخيها فهي أربع وعشرون. وأما الأربعة الثاني أعني أم : عمه وعمته وأم خاله وخالته فهي أربع وعشرون
Book of Fosterage. ... (The text discusses: The madhhab of the Great Imam is followed even if his evidence is not apparent for the muqallid must act upon the mujtahid's statement without examining the evidence. But in Al-Hawi Al-Qudsi: if the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, some say his (Abu Hanifa's) statement is taken, some say theirs, and it is said the mufti is given choice. The correct is that consideration is given to strength of evidence. The strength of their evidence is clear: Allah's saying 'Mothers shall suckle their children for two whole years' indicates no suckling after completion. His saying 'if they desire to wean by mutual consent and consultation, there is no sin upon them' applies before two years as indicated by the condition of mutual consent and consultation; after two years these are not needed. This weakens what is in Miraj al-Dirayah from Al-Mabsut and Al-Muhit about after two years being permissible. ... And on this, using it for medicine is not permissible. ... The author says: (Except) the mother of one's sister and the sister of one's son: they are permissible from fosterage unlike from lineage. He used the mudaf and mudaf ilayh generally. In 'mother of one's sister' there are three scenarios: first: the mother is by fosterage and the sister by lineage; second: the opposite; third: both by fosterage. In 'sister of one's son' also three scenarios. ... The reason for these two exceptions is the absence of the effective cause: the prohibition in fosterage exists when the same prohibited meaning as in lineage is present, and it is absent in these two. ... Additional exceptions: mother of one's paternal uncle, paternal aunt, mother of maternal uncle and maternal aunt (because their mothers are the grandmother's husband, but this is not the case in fosterage). Other images added by commentators: mother of one's grandson (child of one's child) by fosterage... etc. The total number of such images is said to reach over sixty. The author then explains that the two issues of the text yield twenty-four images: for 'mother of his brother' (with brother or sister) and 'sister of his son' (with son or daughter) each with three considerations, and each of those twelve is considered from the man's perspective and the woman's perspective, totalling twenty-four. And the additional four (mother of uncle, aunt, etc.) also yield twenty-four.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of exceptions to the general rule that fosterage creates the same prohibitions as lineage. The author begins with a discussion of the fatwa method when Abu Hanifa and his two students differ: the preferred view is to give weight to the stronger evidence. Then he argues that the evidence of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is stronger for prohibiting breastfeeding after two years, based on Quran 2:233 which sets two years as the complete term. The verse about weaning by mutual consent implies it is before two years; after two years, weaning is automatic. The exception clause 'except the mother of one's sister and sister of one's son' is then explained: these two relations are prohibited by lineage but not by fosterage because the effective cause (being one's mother or daughter) is absent. The author elaborates the three scenarios for each: where the mother/sister relation is from fosterage, from lineage, or both. Then additional exceptions are listed: mother of one's uncle/aunt, etc. The commentator notes that these scenarios multiply into many images (over 60 when considering all permutations of mudaf and mudaf ilayh and gender of the person). The analysis follows the Hanafi method of identifying the effective cause ('illa) and applying it consistently.

Key Terms
الرضاع (al-rida'): The act of a woman suckling a child not her own, which creates certain legal prohibitions similar to those of lineage.
أم الأخ (umm al-akh): Mother of one's brother or sister—specifically here, the mother of one's sister (either by fosterage or lineage) who is exempted from the general prohibition of fosterage.
أخت الابن (ukht al-ibn): Sister of one's son—similarly exempted from prohibition by fosterage if the relation is only through fosterage.
العلة (al-'illa): The effective cause or ratio legis that brings about the legal ruling; here, the reason for prohibition by fosterage is the existence of the same essential prohibited meaning as in lineage (being a mother/daughter, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following women is it permissible for a man to marry according to the Hanafi school, if the relationship is only through fosterage?
A) His foster mother (the woman who breastfed him).
B) The mother of his foster sister (who breastfed his sister but not him).
C) His foster sister.
D) The daughter of his foster brother.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits marriage to the mother of one's sister and sister of one's son when the relationship is through fosterage alone, because the effective cause of prohibition from lineage is absent.

Nikah — Marriage
advanced
12 min
Exceptions to Prohibition by Fosterage and Their Enumeration
Enumerates exceptions to marriage prohibition by fosterage, explaining the underlying cause and counting all possible cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that the cause ('illa) of prohibition from fosterage is the existence of a prohibited relationship from lineage, and identify which fosterage relations are exceptions where marriage is permissible.

Core Idea
Fosterage prohibits marriage only where the same relationship in lineage would be prohibited; when the cause is absent, marriage is permitted.

The Hanafi school holds that fosterage (rada'ah) creates the same marriage prohibitions as lineage (nasab), but this principle is not absolute. There are numerous exceptions where the specific cause of prohibition present in lineage is absent in fosterage, making marriage permissible. In this passage, the author of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq enumerates these excepted cases, building on earlier works and adding his own derived cases, demonstrating the Hanafi methodology of extrapolation by cause ('illa).

Guided Path
1
Identify the basis of prohibition in lineage
Determine the specific cause ('illa) that makes a marriage prohibited in nasab. For example, the mother of one's brother is prohibited because she is one's own mother or a woman one's father had intercourse with. The sister of one's son is prohibited because she is one's daughter or stepdaughter.
This cause is derived from the Quran and Sunnah.
2
Recognize the absence of this cause in fosterage
For each excepted case, verify that the same cause does not exist in the fosterage relationship. For instance, the mother of one's brother from fosterage is not one's biological mother or a woman one's father had intercourse with.
This absence of cause is the basis for permissibility.
3
Follow the enumeration from base text to later additions
Start with the two exceptions from the original matn (mother of one's brother, sister of one's son), then the four cases from Al-Wiqaya (mother of paternal uncle/aunt, mother of maternal uncle/aunt), then the three from commentators (mother of grandson, grandmother of child, paternal aunt of child), and finally the author's two (daughter of child's sister, daughter of child's paternal aunt).
Each addition is based on the same principle of cause absence.
4
Understand the three considerations (i'tibarat) of adding 'min al-rada'a'
The phrase 'from fosterage' can grammatically attach to the mudaf (first term) alone, the mudaf ilayh (second term) alone, or to both. Each attachment yields a different ruling, multiplying the number of cases.
This grammatical analysis is crucial for exhaustive enumeration.
5
Complete the counting to reach the total 81
Work through the arithmetic: 24 cases from the first two exceptions (12 forms × 2 genders), 24 from the four Wiqaya cases, 18 from the three commentator cases, and 15 from the author's two new cases, summing to 81.
The author credits Allah for this enumeration and notes it is a unique contribution of this book.

كتاب الرضاع وبالأخت الأخت رضاعاً لا يشمل ما إذا كانت إحداهما فقط بطريق الرضاع، وإن أريد بالأم الأم نسباً وبالأخت الأخت رضاعاً أو بالعكس لا يشمل الصورتين الأخريين. قلنا : المراد ما إذا كانت إحداهما بطريق الرضاع أعم من أن تكون إحداهما فقط أو كل منهما ا هـ. ولا شك أن السبب في استثناء هذين عدم وجود العلة فإنها في التحريم من الرضاع وجود المعنى المحرم في النسب ولم توجد في هذين، أما في الأولى فلان أم أخته من النسب إنما حرمت لكونها أمه أو موطوءة أبيه وهو مفقود في الرضاع. وأما في الثانية فلأن أخت ابنه نسباً إنما حرمت لكونها بنته أو بنت امرأته ولم يوجد في الرضاع، فعلم أنه لا حصر في كلامه وقد ثبت ذلك الانتفاء في صور أخرى فزاد على الصورتين في الوقاية أربعة : أم عمه وعمته وأم خاله وخالته لأن أم هؤلاء موطوءة الجد الصحيح أو الفاسد ولا كذلك من الرضاع، وفي شرحها ولا تنس الصور الثلاث في جميع ما ذكرنا ا.هـ. يعني من اعتبار الرضاع في المضاف فقط أو المضاف إليه فقط أو فيهما، وزاد الشارحون صوراً أخرى : الأولى أم حفدته رضاعاً بأن أرضعت أجنبية ولد ولده فله أن يتزوج بهذه المرأة بخلافه من النسب لأنها حليلة ابنه أو بنته ولم يوجد هذا المعنى في الرضاع، وفي المصباح حفد حفداً . خدم فهو حافد والجمع حفدة مثل كافر وكفرة ومنه قيل للأعوان حفدة، وقيل لأولاد الأولاد حفدة لأنهم كالخدام في الصغر ا هـ . والمراد هنا أولاد الأولاد والثانية جدة ولده من الرضاع بأن أرضعت أجنبية ولده ولها أم فإنه يجوز له التزوج بهذه الأم بخلافه من النسب لأنها أمه أو أم امرأته. الثالثة عمة الولد من الرضاع بأن كان لزوج المرضعة أخت فلأب الرضيع أن يتزوجها بخلافه من النسب لأنها أخته ولم يذكروا خالة ولده لأنها حلال من النسب أيضاً لأنها أخت زوجته . الرابعة يحل للمرأة التزوج بأبي أخيها من الرضاع أو بأخي ولدها من الرضاع وبأبي حفدتها من الرضاع وبجد ولدها من الرضاع وبخال ولدها من الرضاع، ولا يجوز ذلك كله من النسب لما قلنا في حق الرجل. ثم اعلم أن ما ذكرناه من صحة اعتبار الرضاع في المضاف فقط أو في المضاف إليه فقط أو فيهما يطرد في جميع الصور كما ذكره ابن وهبان في شرح المنظومة، وأفاد أنها تبلغ ستين مسألة ونيفاً ليس هذا المختصر موضع ذكرها، وأحال إلى الذهن في حل بعضها وتبعه في الإضراب عن حلها العلامة عبد البر الشحنة . بن وأقول في بيان حلها : إن مسألتي الكتاب أربع وعشرون صورة لأن لأم أخيه بتذكير الأخ وبتأنيث الأخت صورتين لجواز إضافة الأم إلى الأخ والأخت، وكل منهما بالاعتبارات الثلاثة فهي ستة ولأخت ابنه بتذكير الابن وتأنيث البنت صورتين لجواز إضافة الأخت إلى الابن والبنت وبالاعتبارات ستة، ولكل من الاثني عشر صورتان إما باعتبار ما يحل للرجل أو ما يحل للمرأة فإنه كما يجوز له التزوج بأم أخيه يجوز لها التزوج بأبي أخيها فهي أربع وعشرون. وأما الأربعة الثاني أعني أم : عمه وعمته وأم خاله وخالته فهي أربع وعشرون صورة أيضاً لأن الأربعة بالاعتبارات الثلاث اثنا عشر ولكل منها صورتان : إما باعتبار ما يحل له أو لها فإنه كما يجوز للرجل التزوج بأم عم ولده رضاعاً يجوز لها التزوج بأبي عم ولدها رضاعاً إلى آخر الأقسام. وأما الثلاثة الأخيرة أعني أم حفدته وجدة ولده وعمة ولده فهي بالاعتبارات الثلاث تسعة ولكل منهما صورتان باعتبار ما يحل له : أو لها فإنه كما يجوز للرجل التزوج بأم حفدته يجوز للمرأة التزوج بأبي حفدتها من الرضاع كما قدمناه لكن يتصور في حقها عم ولدها لأنه حلال من النسب أيضاً لها لأنه أخو زوجها، ولكن العدد المذكور لا ينتقص به لأن بدله خال ولدها فإنه كما قدمناه جائز لها من الرضاع دون النسب لأنه أخوها فصارت الثلاثة ثمانية عشر فصار الكل ستاً وستين صورة، فالمراد بالنيف في كلام ابن وهبان ست، وهذا البيان من خواص هذا الكتاب بحول الله وقوته. ثم تأملت بعد قول ابن الهمام إذا عرفت مناط الإخراج أمكنك تسمية صورة أخرى ففتح الله تعالى بتسمية صورتين : الأولى بنت أخت ولده حلال من الرضاع حرام من النسب لأنها إما بنت بنته أو بنت ربيبته ويصح فيه الأوجه الثلاثة، وكل منها إما أن تكون الأخت مضافة إلى الابن أو البنت فهي ستة، وكل منها إما باعتبار ما يحل للرجل أولها فإنه كما يجوز له التزوج ببنت أخت ولده رضاعاً يجوز لها التزوج بابن أخت ولدها رضاعاً فصارت اثني عشر. الثانية بنت عمة ولده جائزة من الرضاع حرام من النسب لأنها بنت أخته وفيها الوجوه الثلاثة فقط باعتبار ما يحل له ولا يتأتى هنا باعتبار المرأة فإنه يحل لها التزوج بابن عمة Book of Fosterage: And by 'sister's sister from fosterage' it does not include the case when only one of them is through fosterage. And if 'mother' is meant by lineage and 'sister' by fosterage, or vice versa, it does not include the other two forms. We said: the intended meaning is when one of them is through fosterage, whether only one or both. There is no doubt that the reason for excluding these two is the absence of the cause (illa), for the prohibition from fosterage depends on the existence of the prohibited meaning in lineage, and it is absent in these two. As for the first, because the mother of his sister from lineage is prohibited only because she is his mother or the one his father had intercourse with, and this is absent in fosterage. As for the second, because the sister of his son from lineage is prohibited only because she is his daughter or the daughter of his wife, and this is not found in fosterage. So it is understood that there is no limitation in his statement, and that negation has been established in other cases. Thus, the Wiqaya added four to the two cases: the mother of his paternal uncle, his paternal aunt, the mother of his maternal uncle, and his maternal aunt, because the mother of these is the one with whom the true or false grandfather had intercourse, and not so in fosterage. And in its commentary: 'Do not forget the three forms in all that we have mentioned,' meaning considering fosterage in the mudaf alone, or the mudaf ilayh alone, or in both. The commentators added other cases: first, the mother of his grandson (hafad) by fosterage, i.e., if a foreign woman nursed the child of his child, he may marry this woman, unlike with lineage because she is the wife of his son or his daughter, and this meaning is not found in fosterage. In al-Misbah: 'hafada, hafdan, khaddama, so he is hafid, plural hafada like kafir and kafara, from which helpers are called hafada, and the children of children are called hafada because they are like servants in childhood.' Here it means grandchildren. Second, the grandmother of his child by fosterage, i.e., if a foreign woman nursed his child and she has a mother, he may marry this mother, unlike with lineage because she is his mother or his wife's mother. Third, the paternal aunt of the child by fosterage, i.e., if the foster-husband has a sister, the foster-father may marry her, unlike with lineage because she is his sister. They did not mention the maternal aunt of his child because she is also permissible in lineage, as she is his wife's sister. Fourth, it is permissible for a woman to marry the father of her brother by fosterage, or the brother of her child by fosterage, or the father of her grandson by fosterage, or the grandfather of her child by fosterage, or the maternal uncle of her child by fosterage, and all of that is not permissible in lineage for the reason we stated regarding the man. Then know that what we mentioned about the validity of considering fosterage in the mudaf alone, or the mudaf ilayh alone, or in both, applies uniformly to all cases, as mentioned by Ibn Wahban in his commentary on the Manzuma. He indicated that they amount to sixty-some cases, and this concise work is not the place to list them, and he referred to the mind for solving some of them, and 'Abd al-Barr al-Shihna followed him in refraining from solving them. Ibn 'Abd al-Barr? I said in explaining their solution: The two cases of the book are twenty-four forms, because 'mother of his brother' with the masculine 'brother' and feminine 'sister' gives two forms due to the possibility of adding 'mother' to 'brother' or 'sister', and each with the three considerations, so that makes six. And 'sister of his son' with the masculine 'son' and feminine 'daughter' gives two forms due to the possibility of adding 'sister' to 'son' or 'daughter', and with the considerations six. And each of the twelve has two forms, either considering what is permissible for the man or what is permissible for the woman, for just as he may marry the mother of his brother, she may marry the father of her brother, so that makes twenty-four. As for the second four, namely the mother of his paternal uncle, his paternal aunt, the mother of his maternal uncle, and his maternal aunt, they are also twenty-four forms, because the four with the three considerations are twelve, and each has two forms, either considering what is permissible for him or for her, for just as it is permissible for a man to marry the mother of his child's paternal uncle by fosterage, it is permissible for her to marry the father of her child's paternal uncle by fosterage, etc. As for the last three, namely the mother of his grandson, the grandmother of his child, and the paternal aunt of his child, they are with the three considerations nine, and each has two forms considering what is permissible for him or for her, for just as it is permissible for a man to marry the mother of his grandson, it is permissible for a woman to marry the father of her grandson by fosterage as we mentioned, but for her, the paternal uncle of her child is also permissible in lineage because he is her husband's brother, but the aforementioned number is not reduced because its alternative is the maternal uncle of her child, as we mentioned, it is permissible for her by fosterage but not from lineage because he is her brother, so the three become eighteen, so the total becomes sixty-six forms. So the meaning of 'some' (nayf) in the statement of Ibn Wahban is six. This explanation is unique to this book by the power and might of Allah. Then after that, I pondered the statement of Ibn al-Humam: 'If you know the criterion for extraction, you can name another form.' So Allah opened up for me to name two forms: First, the daughter of his child's sister is permissible by fosterage, prohibited by lineage because she is either the daughter of his daughter or the daughter of his stepdaughter, and the three aspects are valid in it. Each of them, whether the sister is added to the son or the daughter, makes six, and each of them either considering what is permissible for the man or for her, so it becomes twelve. Second, the daughter of his child's paternal aunt is permissible by fosterage, prohibited by lineage because she is the daughter of his sister, and in it are only the three aspects considering what is permissible for him, and it does not apply here considering the woman, because it is permissible for her to marry the son of her child's paternal aunt both by lineage and fosterage, unlike the first case, where it is not permissible for her to marry the son of her child's sister from lineage because he is either the son of her daughter or the son of her husband's daughter, and he is prohibited from marrying the wife of his grandfather. So the total of these two forms amounts to fifteen ways, so the excepted cases become eighty-one. But the correctness of the attachment of 'min al-rada'a' in their saying 'except the mother of his brother from fosterage' and similar to each of the mudaf alone, the mudaf ilayh alone, and both, is only from the perspective of meaning. As for from the perspective of grammar, it is attached to 'the mother' as a hal from it, because 'the mother' is definite, so the prepositional phrase comes as a hal from it, not as a related to an omitted element. It is not a na't because it is definite? I mean 'the mother of his brother'. Unlike 'his sister' because it is mudaf ilayh, and there is no condition permitting it to have a hal. And similar comes in 'the sister of his son', as stated in Fath al-Qadir. And al-Muradi narrated in al-Alfiyya from some Basrans the permissibility of the hal coming from the mudaf ilayh without any condition. 'The coming of...' explanation of 'that the three like 'I struck the slave girl of Hind sitting' and Ibn Malik objected in his commentary on al-Tashil regarding the claim of its permissibility without dispute, and in al-Mughni it is mentioned that the jar and majrur and zarf when they occur after a pure indefinite... His saying: 'And it does not apply here considering the woman' it would be appropriate to assume its alternative is the son of her child's maternal uncle so that the number is not reduced, as he assumed in the previous case, namely her child's paternal uncle, where he assumed its alternative is her child's maternal uncle. His saying: 'and his statement is attached'
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a Hanafi commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, continues the discussion of exceptions to the general rule that fosterage (rada'ah) creates the same marriage prohibitions as lineage (nasab). The author explains that the basis of prohibition in nasab is a specific cause (illa): in the case of the mother of one's brother (from lineage), she is one's own mother or a woman one's father had intercourse with; in the case of the sister of one's son (from lineage), she is one's daughter or stepdaughter. These causes are absent in corresponding fosterage relations, making marriage permissible. The passage then lists additional cases where the cause is absent: the mother of one's paternal uncle/aunt and maternal uncle/aunt (because their mother would have been the grandfather's wife), the mother of one's grandson (because she would be the wife of one's son or daughter in lineage), the grandmother of one's child (because she would be one's own mother or wife's mother), and the paternal aunt of one's child (because she would be one's sister). For women, parallel permissibility applies. The author then provides a detailed enumeration of all possible cases, taking into account three ways of adding the fosterage attribute (to the first term, the second term, or both) and the gender of the reference (whether the ruling is for a man or a woman). He counts 24 cases from the book's two original exceptions, then 24 from the four extra cases in Al-Wiqaya, then 18 from the three further cases added by commentators, totaling 66. Then he adds two more cases from his own ijtihad: the daughter of one's child's sister and the daughter of one's child's paternal aunt, which add 15 more forms, bringing the total to 81 excepted cases. The passage ends with a grammatical note about the construction of phrases like "mother of his brother from fosterage," explaining that the prepositional phrase functions as a hal (circumstantial accusative) of the definite noun 'mother,' not as a simple adjective or related element. This meticulous enumeration demonstrates the Hanafi method of extrapolating rulings through the identification and application of causes ('ilal), and the systematic consideration of all logical permutations to exhaustively determine the law.

Key Terms
رضاع (Rada'ah): Fosterage relationship established through breastfeeding, which creates some of the same marriage prohibitions as lineage in Hanafi law.
علة ('Illa): The effective cause for prohibition: the existence of a relationship that would be prohibited in lineage (e.g., being mother, daughter, sister, etc.).
مضاف (Mudaf): The first term in a genitive construct (idafa), e.g., 'mother' in 'mother of his brother.'
مضاف إليه (Mudaf Ilayh): The second term in a genitive construct (idafa), e.g., 'his brother' in 'mother of his brother.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many total excepted cases does the author arrive at after adding his two new forms?
A) 66
B) 81
C) 24
D) 60

Key Takeaway
The cause of prohibition in fosterage is the existence of the same relationship that would be prohibited by lineage; where that cause is absent, marriage is permissible.

Enumeration of Permissible Fosterage Relations in Hanafi Fiqh
Counting all permissible and impermissible marriage relations through fosterage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the systematic enumeration of permissible fosterage relations in Hanafi fiqh and identify the additional cases added by Ibn al-Humam.

Core Idea
Fosterage creates marriage prohibitions analogous to blood lineage but with specific exceptions, leading to a precise enumeration of 81 scenarios.

This lesson unpacks a dense passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq that counts all possible marriage relations through fosterage. The author uses a combinatorial method, multiplying categories of relatives by considerations of permissibility for men and women, then adds two special cases. Understanding this enumeration helps a student appreciate how Hanafi jurists systematically applied the principles of rada' to real-life marriage decisions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base categories
The passage first mentions four female relatives (mother of paternal uncle, etc.) and then three others (mother of grandson's wife, grandmother, paternal aunt). List them.
These are the key relationships that can be prohibited through fosterage.
2
Apply the three considerations
For each relative, consider if the marriage prohibition applies: (1) from the man's perspective, (2) from the woman's perspective, (3) both. This yields 12 and 9 base images, each with two forms (him/her).
The 'three considerations' are the perspectives of the man, the woman, and the combination.
3
Calculate the initial total
Multiply: 4 categories × 3 considerations = 12, × 2 forms = 24. Then 3 categories × 3 considerations = 9, × 2 forms = 18. Sum = 42. But the text says 66. Find the missing 24.
The missing 24 likely come from sub-cases or additional relatives not explicitly listed. The passage does not detail them.
4
Add the two cases from Ibn al-Humam
Ibn al-Humam described two additional scenarios: (1) daughter of the son's sister, (2) daughter of the son's paternal aunt. Each has 3 aspects and 2 perspectives, giving 12+3=15 new scenarios.
These are permissible through fosterage but forbidden through lineage.
5
Verify the final total
The passage states the basic images are 66 (including the missing 24), plus 8 from Ibn Wahban, plus 15 from Ibn al-Humam, total 81. Understand that the addition of Ibn al-Humam's cases is an expansion accepted by the author.
The 'nayf' (additional) in Ibn Wahban's text refers to 6, but the author counts 8? The passage says 'النيف' is 6, but the breakdown is not given.

Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage is a detailed enumeration of permissible and impermissible marriage relations through fosterage (رضاع). The author explains that there are 66 basic scenarios, derived from three categories of relatives (the four, then three) multiplied by considerations. He then adds two more cases from Ibn al-Humam, bringing the total to 81. The reasoning hinges on whether the relation is through fosterage or lineage, and whether the prohibition applies to men, women, or both. For example, a man may marry the daughter of his son's sister (بنت أخت ولده) through fosterage because she is not a blood relative, but he cannot marry her through lineage as she would be his granddaughter or step-granddaughter. The author emphasizes that these calculations are specific to this commentary.

Key Terms
رضاع (rada'): Fosterage; the relationship created by breastfeeding a child, which establishes certain marriage prohibitions comparable to blood relations.
عم الرضاع (amm al-rada'): Paternal uncle through fosterage; a man who breastfed alongside the person's father.
بنت أخت الولد (bint ukht al-walad): Daughter of the son's sister; a woman who is the niece of the son through the son's sister.
النيف (al-nayf): Increment; additional number; here six.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school enumerates 81 distinct scenarios of marriage permissibility through fosterage, derived from combinatorial logic and expanded by later scholars.

Dispute on Fosterage: Mother of Paternal/Maternal Uncle
Refuting the blanket prohibition of the mother of a foster-uncle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on whether the mother of a paternal/maternal uncle is prohibited through fosterage and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Fosterage prohibition mirrors lineage, but the mother of an uncle may be a stranger if she only nursed the uncle.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the prohibition of marriage to the mother of a foster-paternal uncle (أم العم) or foster-maternal uncle (أم الخال). The commentator argues for blanket prohibition, while Fath al-Qadir refines the ruling based on the grammatical attachment of 'من الرضاع'. Understanding the different scenarios clarifies when such a woman is permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
Recognize the general Hanafi principle that fosterage prohibitions mirror lineage prohibitions. The core question: Is the mother of a foster-uncle prohibited?
The commentator claims universal prohibition.
2
Present the commentator's objection
The commentator argues that she must be either the grandmother through fosterage or the woman slept with by the grandfather, both prohibited.
He uses qiyas to lineage to assert exclusivity.
3
Analyse Fath al-Qadir's refutation
Fath al-Qadir breaks the exclusivity by showing she may be a stranger who only nursed the uncle, not the father or mother.
This introduces scenario-specific rulings.
4
Examine the four interpretations of jar-majrur
The phrase 'من الرضاع' can attach to different nouns, altering meaning. The text details four possible readings, each affecting the prohibition.
Only some readings lead to prohibition.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
Later authorities (Fath al-Qadir, al-Nahr) prefer the permissive view when the woman is a stranger. This is the relied-upon position.
Practical consequence: valid marriage when she is not grandmother/grandfather's wife.

ثم اعلم أنا قدمنا أن أم العم وأم الخال لا تحرم من الرضاع فقال الشارح: ومن العجب ما ذكره في الغاية أن أم العم من الرضاع لا تحرم وكذا أم الخال وهذا لا يصح لما ذكرنا أنه معتبر بالنسب، والمعنى الذي أوجب الحرمة في النسب موجود في الرضاع فكيف يصح هذا؟ بيانه أنها لا تخلو إما أن تكون جدته من الرضاع أو موطوءة جده وكلاهما يوجب الحرمة فلا يستقيم إلا إذا أريد بالعم من الرضاع من رضع مع أبيه، وبالخال من رضع مع أمه فحيئنذ يستقيم ا هـ. ورده في فتح القدير بقوله : ولقائل أن يقول بمنع الحصر لجواز كونها لم ترضع أباه ولا أمه فلا تكون جدته من الرضاع ولا موطوءة جده بل أجنبية أرضعت عمه من النسب وخاله ا والحاصل أن الشارح فهم أن الجار والمجرور أعني قوله من الرضاع متصل بالمضاف إليه فقط، وحينئذ يحرم التزوج وصورته أن يكون له عم وخال رضاعاً ولكل منهما أم نسب فحينئذ لا يجوز له التزوج بها لأنها كما قال إما جدته رضاعاً أو موطوءة جده، وغفل الشارح عن الوجهين الأخيرين اللذين هما مراد صاحب الغاية : أحدهما أنه متصل بالمضاف فقط أعني الأم بأن كان له عم وخال نسباً فأرضعتهما أجنبيه فله أن يتزوج بها لأنها ليست جدته ولا موطوءة جده، وعليه اقتصر في فتح القدير وغفل عن الوجه الآخر وهو أن يتصل بكل منهما بأن كان له عم وخال رضاعاً ولكل منهما أم رضاعاً فحينئذ يجوز له التزوج بها لما قلنا، وههنا وجه رابع يراد بالعم من الرضاع من رضع مع أبيه رضاعاً وبالخال من رضع مع أمه رضاعاً، هـ. أن وهو بالأم الخ) قال في النهر : هذا وهم للقطع بأنه أراد بالتعلق في قوله فإنما يتعلق بالأم» التعلق المعنوي وهو كونه وصفاً له لما استقر من أن الحال قيد في عاملها وصف لصاحبها وهذا هو المنفي لا متعلقاً بمحذوف هو صاحب الحال والتقدير إلا أم أخيه فإنها لا تحرم من الرضاع فيكون صاحب الحال هو الضمير في «يحرم» إذ لا محوج إليه، وهذا مما يجب أن يفهم في هذا المقام وكيف ينسب إلى مثل هذا الإمام أنه قد خفي عليه مثل هذا الكلام. يعني قوله : (لأنها كما قال إما جدته رضاعاً أو موطوءه جده أقول : لا يخفى أن المرضعة إن كانت
Then know that we have presented that the mother of the paternal uncle and the mother of the maternal uncle are not prohibited through fosterage. So the commentator said: 'And it is strange what was mentioned in al-Ghaya: that the mother of the paternal uncle through fosterage is not prohibited, and similarly the mother of the maternal uncle. Its form is that he has a paternal uncle and maternal uncle through fosterage, and each of them has a mother by lineage, so it is not permissible for him to marry her because, as he said, she is either his grandmother through fosterage or the one slept with by his grandfather. And the commentator neglected the other two aspects which are intended by the author of al-Ghaya: One is that it is connected only to the mudaf, i.e., the mother, such that he has a paternal uncle and maternal uncle by lineage, and a stranger breastfed them, so he may marry her because she is not his grandmother nor the one slept with by his grandfather. He said: ('that and it is with the mother etc.') Al-Nahr said: 'This is a delusion, certainly because he intended by attachment in his statement 'it attaches to the mother' the semantic attachment, which is being a description of it, as established that the hal is a restriction on its factor and a description of its owner, and this is what is negated, not what is related to a deleted element that is the owner of the hal. And the interpretation is 'except the mother of his brother, for she is not prohibited through fosterage', so the owner of the hal is the pronoun in 'yahrum' because there is no need for it. And this is something that must be understood in this context. How can it be attributed to such an imam that this speech was hidden from him? Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether the mother of a paternal uncle (أم العم) and mother of a maternal uncle (أم الخال) are prohibited through fosterage. The commentator (شارح) argues they are prohibited because they are either the grandmother through fosterage or the woman who nursed the grandfather. However, Fath al-Qadir refutes this, explaining that the phrase 'من الرضاع' can attach differently. If she only nursed the uncle (not the father or mother), she is a stranger and thus permissible. The text then discusses four possible interpretations of the attachment of 'من الرضاع', each affecting the ruling. Al-Nahr criticizes the commentator for misunderstanding the grammatical attachment, emphasizing that the phrase is a description of the mother, not a separate entity. The passage concludes with a note that what is meant by 'paternal uncle through fosterage' must be clearly defined.

Key Terms
أم العم (umm al-amm): The mother of a paternal uncle; a woman whose son is a paternal uncle (by birth or fosterage).
موطوءة الجد (mawtu'at al-jadd): A woman with whom the grandfather has had sexual intercourse; such a woman is prohibited for the grandson.
رضاع (rada'): Fosterage; the act of breastfeeding that creates familial relations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the dispute about the mother of the paternal uncle (أم العم) through fosterage, which scenario makes her permissible to marry?
A) She is both the grandmother and the grandfather's wife
B) She nursed only the uncle, not the father or mother
C) She is the grandmother through fosterage
D) She is the mother of a foster-brother

Key Takeaway
The mother of a foster-uncle is not automatically prohibited; she is only prohibited if she is also the grandmother or grandfather's wife through fosterage.

The Exception in the Fosterage Hadith: Disconnected Exception vs. Specification
Explaining the exception 'إلا أم أخته' in the fosterage hadith and its status as disconnected exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers the exception 'إلا أم أخته' a disconnected exception and refute the objection that it is an incorrect specification.

Core Idea
The hadith of fosterage covers only blood relations; exceptions based on affinity are disconnected, not specifications.

In this passage from Fatḥ al-Qadīr, the Hanafi position on the hadith 'يَحْرُمُ من الرَّضَاعِ ما يَحْرُمُ من النَّسَبِ' is defended against a Shafi'i objection. The key insight is that the hadith's general words refer only to blood relatives (mothers, daughters, sisters, etc.), not to relations by marriage (muṣāhara). Therefore, the exception 'إلا أم أخته' is not a specification but a disconnected exception, removing something that was never included. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying fosterage prohibitions in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and its scope
The hadith 'يَحْرُمُ من الرَّضَاعِ ما يَحْرُمُ من النَّسَبِ' is general (ʿāmm) for all women prohibited by lineage. What does 'lineage' (nasab) encompass in the Quranic verses? It includes blood relations: mothers, daughters, sisters, etc.
The Quranic verses (4:23) enumerate blood relations.
2
Recognize the exception in Kanz al-Daqā'iq
The text includes an exception: 'إلا أم أخته' (except the mother of his sister). A group argued this is a specification (takhṣīṣ) of the general hadith.
The exception is a juristic addition in Kanz al-Daqā'iq.
3
Analyze the investigators' reasoning
The muḥaqqiqūn argue it is not specification because the mother of one's sister is not a blood relative covered by the Quranic words (she is a relative by affinity). Since she was never included, excluding her is a disconnected exception.
Disconnected exception (istithnā' munqati') removes something not originally intended.
4
Address al-Baydawi's objection
Al-Baydawi claimed the exception is incorrect because those women are prohibited by affinity, not lineage. The response: a disconnected exception is valid in Arabic grammar, so the objection is unfounded.
Al-Baydawi's view represents a Shafi'i perspective.
5
Apply the criterion to other cases
The principle extends: any woman prohibited by affinity (not blood) is not covered by the hadith. For example, the sister of a son from fosterage (who is a relative by marriage) is not prohibited.
The criterion is whether the woman is a blood relative as enumerated in the Quran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي فتح القدير : ثم قالت طائفة هذا الإخراج تخصيص للحديث أعني يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب بدليل العقل والمحققون على أنه ليس تخصيصاً لأنه أحال ما يحرم بالرضاع على ما يحرم بالنسب هو ما يحرم بالنسب وما تعلق به خطاب تحريمه وقد تعلق بما عبر عنه بلفظ الأمهات والبنات وأخواتكم وعماتكم وخالاتكم وبنات الأخ وبنات الأخت، فما كان من هذه الألفاظ متحققاً مسمى من الرضاع حرم فيه والمذكورات ليس شيء منها من مسمى تلك، فكيف تكون مخصصة وهي غير متناولة؟ ولذا إذا خلا تناول الاسم في النسب جاز النكاح كما إذا ثبت النسب من اثنين ولكل منهما بنت جاز لكل منهما أن يتزوج بنت الآخر وإن كانت أخت ولده من النسب وأنت إذا حققت مناط الإخراج أمكنك تسمية صور أخرى. والاستثناء في عبارة الكتاب على هذا يجب أن يكون منقطعاً أعني قوله يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب إلا أم أخته إلى آخره وبهذا اندفع ما ذكره البيضاوي بقوله : واستثناء أخت ابن الرجل وأم أخيه من الرضاع من هذا الأصل ليس بصحيح فإن حرمتهما في النسب بالمصاهرة دون النسب ا هـ . لأن استثناء المنقطع صحيح إلا أن يريد الاستثناء المتصل.
And in Fatḥ al-Qadīr: Then a group said this exclusion is a specification (takhṣīṣ) of the hadith – I mean 'What is prohibited by fosterage is what is prohibited by lineage' – by rational evidence; but the investigators said it is not specification, because it refers what is prohibited by fosterage to what is prohibited by lineage; that is what is prohibited by lineage and what the address of its prohibition is attached to, and it has been attached to what is expressed by the words 'mothers, daughters, your sisters, your paternal aunts, your maternal aunts, daughters of brother, and daughters of sister'. So what is realized from fosterage from these words is prohibited in it; and the mentioned ones (i.e., the mother of a sister, sister of a son, etc.) are not among the referents of those. So how can they be specified while they are not included? Therefore, if the application of the name in lineage is vacant, marriage is permissible – as when lineage is established from two, and each has a daughter, it is permissible for each to marry the other's daughter, even if she is the sister of his child by lineage. And if you investigate the criterion of the exclusion, you can name other cases. The exception in the wording of the book on this basis must be disconnected (munqati') – i.e., his statement: 'What is prohibited by fosterage is what is prohibited by lineage, except the mother of his sister', etc. And by this is repelled what al-Baydawi mentioned: 'And the exception of the sister of the son of a man and his mother's brother's mother from fosterage from this principle is not correct, because their prohibition in lineage is by affinity (muṣāhara), not by lineage.' Because the disconnected exception is valid, unless he intends the connected exception.
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, discussing the interpretation of the famous hadith 'يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب' (What is prohibited by fosterage is what is prohibited by lineage). A group of scholars argued that the exception 'إلا أم أخته' (except the mother of his sister) is a specification (takhṣīṣ) of the general hadith. However, the investigators (muhaqqiqun) respond that it is not a specification because the general words in the Quran (such as 'mothers, daughters, sisters, etc.') do not include the mother of one's sister or the sister of one's son; those are prohibited by affinity (muṣāhara) in lineage, not by blood lineage. Therefore, they are not included in the general category of 'what is prohibited by lineage' in the context of the hadith, which only refers to blood relations. Hence, the exception must be disconnected (istithnā' munqati'), not a true specification. This refutes al-Baydawi's objection that the exception is incorrect because those women are prohibited by affinity, not lineage; the response is that a disconnected exception is valid in Arabic grammar.

Key Terms
الاستثناء المنقطع (al-istithnā' al-munqati'): A disconnected exception where the excepted item does not belong to the category of the general term; it is a rhetorical device to exclude something that was not originally included.
المصاهرة (al-muṣāhara): Affinity; relationship by marriage, such as in-laws.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the passage consider the exception 'إلا أم أخته' to be a disconnected exception (منقطع) rather than a specification (تخصيص)?
A) Because the mother of a sister is not mentioned in the Quran.
B) Because the mother of a sister is not a blood relative covered by the general words 'mothers, daughters, sisters' etc.
C) Because the hadith is weak.
D) Because the exception contradicts the general rule.

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب' prohibits only blood relatives through fosterage; relatives by affinity are not included, and exceptions for them are valid disconnected exceptions.
