Milk Fatherhood: The Husband of the Wet Nurse as Foster Father (Laban al-Fahl)
Stating the ruling that the husband (or master) of the wet nurse becomes the foster father due to his milk.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on milk fatherhood (laban al-fahl) and identify who becomes a foster father and the resulting marriage prohibitions.

Core Idea
The husband of the wet nurse becomes the foster father of the child, making his relatives foster relatives.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq establishes a key principle of fosterage: the milk produced by a woman because of a man's child creates a parent-child relationship between that man and the nursing child. Known as laban al-fahl (milk of the male), this principle extends the prohibition of marriage to include the husband and his close relatives, just as with blood relations. Understanding this rule is essential for determining permissible and impermissible marriages in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The text states that the husband of the wet nurse becomes a father to the foster child. This is based on the general hadith 'يَحْرُمُ من الرَّضَاعِ ما يَحْرُمُ من النَّسَبِ'.
The hadith equates fosterage to lineage.
2
Understand the scope of 'husband'
The word 'husband' is used for the predominant case; the master of a slave woman also qualifies, as clarified by al-Jawharah.
The condition is that the milk is produced due to a man's child (his semen).
3
Trace the consequences
The husband's children become siblings of the foster child, his brothers become uncles, his sisters become aunts, etc. This mirrors blood relations.
All relationships that are prohibited by blood become prohibited by fosterage through this chain.
4
Apply the prohibition
The foster child cannot marry the wet nurse (his foster mother) nor the husband's spouse (the wet nurse) because that would be incest. Similarly, the foster child cannot marry the wet nurse's parents.
The prohibition extends to all mahram relationships.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (زوج مرضعة لبنها منه أب للرضيع وابنه أخ وبنته أخت وأخوه عم وأخته عمة) بيان لأن لبن الفحل يتعلق به التحريم لعموم الحديث المشهور ، وإذا ثبت كونه أباً له لا يحل لكل منهما موطوءة الآخر. والمراد به اللبن الذي نزل من المرأة بسبب ولادتها من رجل زوج أو سيد فليس الزوج قيداً في كلامه قال في الجوهرة وإنما خرج مخرج الغالب، وإذا ثبتت هذه الحرمة من زوج المرضعة فمنها أولى فلا تتزوج الصغيرة أبا المرضعة لأنه جدها لأمها، أم العم أو الخال فعدم جواز التزوج بالأم النسبية وهي المرضعة هنا لكونها جدته رضاعاً، وموطوءة جده أي جده من الرضاع، وإن كانت المرضعة أجنبية فالأم النسبية ليست جدته من الرضاع ولا
His statement: 'The husband of the wet nurse whose milk is from him is a father to the foster child, and his son is a brother, his daughter is a sister, his brother is a paternal uncle, and his sister is a paternal aunt.' This is an explanation that milk of the male (the husband) entails prohibition due to the generality of the famous hadith. And when it is established that he is a father to him, it is not permissible for either of them to have intercourse with the other's spouse. And by it is meant the milk that descended from the woman due to her giving birth from a man, husband or master; so the word 'husband' is not a restriction in his statement; it is said in al-Jawharah: it was only expressed as the predominant case. And when this prohibition is established from the husband of the wet nurse, then from her (the wet nurse) it is even more so. So the young girl (the foster child) may not marry the father of the wet nurse because he is her maternal grandfather. As for the mother of the paternal uncle or maternal uncle, the impermissibility of marrying the mother by lineage, which is the wet nurse here, is because she is his grandmother by fosterage and the one who had intercourse with his grandfather, i.e., his grandfather from fosterage. And if the wet nurse is a foreign woman, then the mother by lineage is not his grandmother from fosterage nor...
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, establishing the concept of 'لبن الفحل' (milk of the male) and the foster relationships created through it. The text from Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that the husband of the wet nurse (whose semen caused the milk) becomes the father of the foster child. Consequently, the husband's children become siblings of the foster child, and his brothers become uncles, etc. This is based on the general hadith 'يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب'. The scholar al-Jawharah clarifies that the husband is not a necessary condition; the milk could also be from a master (in case of a slave woman), so 'husband' is just the typical case. The prohibition applies to the husband and the foster child as well, so the foster child cannot marry the husband's spouse (i.e., the wet nurse) because that would be marrying one's foster mother. The wet nurse herself is the grandmother if the child was nursed by the same woman? Actually, the text gets confusing at the end. It seems to be explaining the prohibition of marrying the wet nurse's mother (the foster child's grandmother). The last part is incomplete, but the general principle is clear: the husband of the wet nurse is a foster father, and his relatives become relatives of the foster child through fosterage.

Key Terms
لبن الفحل (laban al-fahl): Literally 'milk of the male'; refers to the legal principle that the man whose semen causes the woman to lactate becomes the foster father of the child who drinks her milk.
زوج المرضعة (zawj al-murdi'a): The husband of the wet nurse; the one whose child (or whose semen) caused the production of milk. He is considered the foster father of the child who drinks that milk.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The foster father

D) No relation

Key Takeaway
The husband (or master) of the wet nurse is considered the foster father due to his milk being the cause, creating a web of fosterage relationships that prohibit marriage.

Breastfeeding with Milk from Zina: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining intra-Hanafi dispute on milk from zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi reports on milk from zina and apply the preferred view (mufta bihi) to determine marriage prohibitions.

Core Idea
Milk from zina does not create milk-kinship with the adulterer because it is not from his sperm, so no partiality (bu'diyya) is established.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the ruling of breastfeeding when the milk originates from zina. The Hanafi school has two reports: one holds that the adulterer becomes a father through the milk, the other does not. The author, following Fath al-Qadir, determines which view is more correct based on reasoning (diraya) and the famous books.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Reports
Locate the two conflicting positions on whether milk from zina creates prohibition for the adulterer. Note which scholars support each view.
Report 1: al-Khulasa and al-Jawhara say yes. Report 2: al-Webari, al-Asbijabi, and al-Yanabi' say no.
2
Understand the Reasoning Behind Each
Examine the dalil for each report. The first uses analogy to lawful marriage; the second argues that the milk is not from the adulterer's sperm and no lineage is established.
The key term is 'bu'diyya' (partiality) – the child is considered a part of the father only through lawful reproduction.
3
Analyze the Tarjih Mechanism
Identify how Fath al-Qadir and al-Bahr al-Ra'iq weigh the reports. They prioritize diraya (reasoning) over riwaya (transmission) when the former aligns with the famous books.
The famous books (kutub mashhura) state that milk from a non-husband does not create prohibition for the husband, supporting the negative view.
4
Apply the Mufta Bihi to a Scenario
Given a case where a woman commits zina, gives birth, and breastfeeds a girl, determine who is prohibited from marrying the girl according to the preferred view.
Only the mother's side creates prohibitions. The adulterer and his ascendants/descendants may marry the girl.
5
Note the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Understand the practical difference between the two reports: whether the adulterer's father or son can marry the girl.
In both reports, the girl is prohibited on the adulterer himself by agreement (because she is his daughter biologically), but after that the dispute affects his relatives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرضاع ولم تلد منه ولا أخاها لأنه خالها، ولا عمها لأنها بنت بنت أخيه ولا خالها لأنها بنت بنت أخته، ولا أبناءها وإن كانوا من غير صاحب اللبن لأنهم إخوتها لأمها ولو كان لرجل زوجتان أرضعت كل منهما بنتاً لا يحل لرجل أن يجمع بينهما لأنهما أختان رضاعاً من الأب. قيد بقوله «لبنها منه لأن لبنها لو كان من غيره بأن تزوجت برجل وهي ذات لبن لآخر قبله فأرضعت صبية فإنها ربيبة للثاني بنت للأول فيحل تزوجها بأبناء الثاني، ولو كان الرضيع صبياً حل له التزوج ببناته من غير المرضعة، هذا ما لم تلد من الثاني، فإذا ولدت من الثاني انقطع لبن الأول وصار للثاني، فإذا أرضعت به صبياً كان ولداً للثاني اتفاقاً، وإذا حبلت من الثاني ولم تلد فهو ولد للأول عند أبي حنيفة. وقيدنا بكونه نزل بسبب ولادتها منه لأنه لو تزوج امرأة قط ونزل لها لبن وأرضعت به ولداً لا يكون الزوج أباً للولد لأنه ليس ابنه لأن نسبته إليه بسبب الولادة منه، فإذا انتفت انتفت النسبة فكان كلبن البكر، ولهذا لو ولدت للزوج فنزل لها لبن فأرضعت به ثم جف لبنها ثم در فأرضعت صبية فإن لابن زوج المرضعة التزوج بهذه الصبية، ولو كان صبياً كان له التزوج بأولاد هذا الرجل من غير المرضعة. كذا في الخانية. وأشار يذكر الزوج إلى أن لبن الزنا ليس كالحلال حتى لو ولدت من الزنا وأرضعت به صبية يجوز لأصول الزاني وفروعه التزوج بها، ولا تثبت الحرمة إلا من جانب الأم. ذكره القاضي الأسبيجابي واختاره الوبري وصاحب الينابيع، وفي المحيط خلافه. وفي الخانية والذخيرة وغيرهما: وهو الأحوط الذي ينبغي أن يعتمد والأول أوجه لأن الحرمة من الزنا للبعضية وذلك في الولد نفسه لأنه مخلوق من مائة دون اللبن إذ ليس اللبن كائناً من منيه لأنه فرع التغذي وهو لا يقع إلا بما يدخل من أعلى المعدة لا من أسفل البدن كالحقنة فلا إنبات فلا حرمة بخلاف ثابت النسب للنص. كذا في فتح القدير وإنما قيدنا محل الخلاف بأصول الزاني وفروعه لأنها لا تحل للزاني اتفاقاً لأنها بنت المزني بها، وقدمنا أن فروع المزني بها من موطوءة جده، وعلى كل فالترديد غير ظاهر قوله : (فإن حرمتهما في النسب بالمصاهرة دون النسب) في إطلاقه نظر لأن أخت ابن الرجل إنما تكون حرمتها بالمصاهرة إذا كانت أختاً لأم فتكون ربيبته بخلافها شقيقة أو لأب وأم أخيه إنما تكون حرمتها بالمصاهرة إذا كان الأخ أخاً لأب فإن أمه حينئذ امرأة الأب بخلاف الأخ الشقيق أو لأم فإن حرمة أمه بالنسب لأنها أم. قاله بعض الفضلاء. قوله : (وأشار بذكر الزوج قد قدم أن ذكر الزوج ليس قيداً فلا يفيد ما ذكر فالأولى التنبيه على مسألة الزنا مستأنفة قوله : (والأول أوجه أي دراية لا رواية كما توهمه عبارة صاحب البحر من إطلاقه كلام الكمال الأوجهية . وقيد أستاذنا بما قلناه في هامش نسخته من فتح القدير وعلله بما يأتي آخر كلام الكمال. كذا في الشرنبلالية. وقد وقع التقييد بما ذكر في شرح المقدسي أيضاً وفيه نظر يظهر لمن أمعن النظر في كلام الفتح كما نشير إليه قريباً قوله : (لأنها لا تحل للزاني اتفاقاً) في الرضاع حرام على الزاني ولذا قال في الخلاصة بعد ما ذكر حرمتها على الزاني، وكذا لو لم تحبل من الزنا وأرضعت لا بلبن الزنا. فإنها تحرم على الزاني كما تحرم بنتها من النسب عليه ا هـ. وظاهر كلامهم أن هذه الصبية لا تحرم على عم الزاني وخاله اتفاقاً لأنه لم يثبت نسبها من الزاني حتى يظهر فيها حكم القرابة والتحريم على آباء الزاني وأولاده عند القائلين به ا هـ. من لم يثبت. منه فهذا دعوى الاتفاق نظر ففي القهستاني أن فيه روايتين ونصه : لو زنى بامرأة فولدت وأرضعت صبية جاز له أن يتزوجها كما في شرح الطحاوي، ولكن في الخلاصة أنه لم يجز وقد مرأن فيه روايتين وفي الجوهرة: لو زنى رجل بامرأة فولدت منه وأرضعت صبية بلبنه تحرم عليه هذه الصبية وعلى أصوله وفروعه وذكر الخجندي خلاف هذا فقال : المرأة إذا ولدت من الزنا فنزل لها لبن أو نزل لها لبن من غير ولادة فأرضعت به صبياً فإن الرضاع يكون منها خاصة لا من الزاني، وكل بل كلام الوبري صريح في ذلك وهو الذي قال النسب لا يثبت منه الرضاع ا هـ . في الفتح إنه الأوجه كما تقدم وعبارة الفتح هكذا وذكر الوبري أن الجرمة تثبت من جهة الأم خاصة ما لم يثبت النسب فحينئذ يثبت من الأب وكذا ذكر الأسبيجابي وصاحب الينابيع وهو أوجه لأن الحرمة من الزنا إلى آخر ما تقدم فهذا صريح في أن الحرمة لا تثبت من جهة الزاني لأنه لم يثبت النسب منه ولهذا قال في الفتح راداً على كلام الخلاصة الآتي : وإذا ترجح عدم حرمة الرضيعة بلبن الزاني على الزاني كما ذكرنا فعدم حرمتها على من ليس اللبن منه أولى ا هـ . صريح في أن كلام الوبري وغيره في عدم ثبوت الحرمة على الزاني نفسه فيلزم منه بالأولى عدم ثبوت الحرمة على أصوله وفروعه وإذا ثبت أن في المسألة روايتين وظهر الوجه لإحداهما لا يعدل عنها لما قال في شرح منية المصلي من أنه لا يعدل عن الدراية إذا وافقتها رواية. وما تقدم عن الشرنبلالي وغيره من أن كلام الفتح محمول على أنه الأوجه دراية لا رواية في غير محله لثبوت كل من الروايتين وظهور الوجه لإحداهما وكأنهم توهموا من قول الفتح ولأنه خلاف المسطور في الكتب المشهورة أنه راجع إلى ما ذكره من أنه الأوجه مع أنه ليس كذلك، بل هو راجع إلى ما نقله عن الخلاصة كما سنذكره قوله : (ولذا قال في الخلاصة (الخ أقول ما قاله في الخلاصة رده في فتح القدير بأنه مخالف لما في الكتب المشهورة لأنه يقتضي تحريم بنت المرضعة بلبن غير الزوج على الزوج بطريق أولى اهـ. يعني أن المنصوص عليه في الكتب المشهورة أنه لو كان اللبن لغير الزوج لا تحرم الرضيعة على الزوج، وقول الخلاصة لو أرضعت لا بلبن الزنا تحرم على الزاني» يقتضي خلاف المسطور في الكتب المشهورة فهو مردود قوله : وظاهر كلامهم الخ) أي كما يستفاد من التقييد السابق بأصول الزاني وفروعه ومن التعليل للحرمة بالبعضية وفي الفتح عن التجنيس : لا يجوز للزاني أن يتزوج بالصبية المرضعة ولا لأبيه وأجداده ولا لأحد من أولاده وأولادهم ولعم الزاني أن يتزوج بها كما يجوز أن يتزوج بالصبية التي ولدت من الزاني لأنه لم يثبت نسبها من الزاني حتى يظهر فيها حكم القرابة والتحريم على آباء الزاني وألاوده لاعتبار الجزئية والبعضية ولا جزئية بينها وبين العم، وإذا ثبت هذا في حق المتولدة من الزنا فكذا في حق المرضعة بلبن الزنا ا هـ .
Book of Breastfeeding. And she did not give birth from him. Nor her brother because he is her maternal uncle, nor her paternal uncle because she is the daughter of his brother's daughter, nor her maternal uncle because she is the daughter of his sister's daughter, nor her sons even if they are from someone other than the owner of the milk because they are her maternal half-brothers. If a man has two wives and each one breastfeeds a daughter, it is not permissible for a man to marry both of them because they are milk-sisters from the father. He restricted with his statement "her milk from him" because if her milk were from someone else—such as if she married a man while she had milk from a previous man, and she breastfed a girl—then she is a stepdaughter for the second (husband) and a daughter for the first (husband). So it is permissible to marry her to the sons of the second. And if the infant was a boy, it is permissible for him to marry the daughters of that man other than the wet nurse. This is as long as she did not give birth from the second. If she gives birth from the second, the milk of the first is cut off and becomes for the second. If she then breastfeeds a boy with it, he becomes a child of the second by agreement. And if she becomes pregnant from the second but has not yet given birth, then the child is attributed to the first according to Abu Hanifa. We restricted it to the fact that it descended due to her giving birth from him because if a man married a woman and milk descended for her and she breastfed a child with it, the husband is not a father to the child because the child is not his son, since his lineage to him is from giving birth from him. If that lineage is negated, the relationship is negated, so it is like the milk of a virgin. For this reason, if she gave birth to a husband and milk descended for her and she breastfed with it, then her milk dried up, then flowed again and she breastfed a girl, then the son of the husband of the wet nurse may marry this girl. And if it was a boy, he may marry the children of this man other than the wet nurse. Thus in al-Khaniyya. And he indicated by mentioning "husband" that the milk of zina is not like lawful milk, such that if a woman gave birth from zina and breastfed a girl with it, it is permissible for the ascendants and descendants of the adulterer to marry her. And prohibition is only established from the mother's side. This was mentioned by al-Qadi al-Asbijabi and chosen by al-Webari and the author of al-Yanabi', while in al-Muhit there is the contrary. In al-Khaniyya, al-Dhakhira and others: it is the more cautious and what should be relied upon, but the first is more correct (awjah) because the prohibition from zina is based on partiality (al-bu'diyya) and that applies to the child himself, since he is created from the sperm, not to the milk, as the milk is not from his sperm, because it is a result of nutrition and occurs only from what enters from the upper stomach, not from the lower body like an enema, so it does not cause growth and thus no prohibition, unlike the case of established lineage by text. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And we only restricted the place of dispute to the ascendants and descendants of the adulterer because she is not permissible for the adulterer by agreement, since she is the daughter of the woman with whom he committed zina. And we have mentioned that the descendants of the woman with whom zina was committed from a grandfather's intercourse... etc. And in every case, the hesitation is not apparent. His statement: "Indeed their prohibition in lineage through marriage ties rather than lineage" - in its absolute form there is consideration because the sister of a man's son is prohibited through marriage ties only if she is a half-sister from the mother, making her his stepdaughter, contrary to if she is full sister or from the father. And the mother of the brother is prohibited through marriage ties only if the brother is from the father, because then his mother is the wife of the father, contrary to the full brother or from the mother, as the prohibition of his mother is by lineage because she is the mother. Said by some virtuous ones. His statement: "And he indicated by mentioning the husband" - it has been mentioned that mentioning the husband is not a restriction, so it does not benefit what was mentioned; thus it is better to draw attention to the issue of zina separately. His statement: "And the first is more correct (awjah)" meaning in understanding (diraya) not in transmission (riwaya), as one might understand from the words of the author of al-Bahr from his absolute statement of Kamal's awjahiyya. And our teacher restricted it with what we said in the margin of his copy of Fath al-Qadir, and he explained it with what comes at the end of Kamal's words. Thus in al-Sharniblaliyya. And the restriction with what was mentioned has also occurred in the commentary of al-Maqdisi, and there is consideration in it that is clear to anyone who ponders the words of al-Fath as we will point out soon. His statement: "Because she is not permissible for the adulterer by agreement" - breastfeeding is forbidden for the adulterer. For this reason, al-Khulasa said after mentioning her prohibition on the adulterer: "And similarly, if she did not become pregnant from zina and breastfeeds not with milk from zina, then she is forbidden for the adulterer just as her daughter from lineage is forbidden for him." End quote. And the apparent meaning of their words is that this girl is not forbidden for the paternal uncle of the adulterer or his maternal uncle by agreement, because her lineage from the adulterer is not established such that the ruling of kinship and prohibition becomes apparent regarding the fathers of the adulterer and his children according to those who hold it. End quote. The claim of agreement is questionable, for in al-Qahistani there are two reports. His text: "If a man commits zina with a woman, she gives birth and breastfeeds a girl, it is permissible for him to marry her as in Sharh al-Tahawi. But in al-Khulasa it is not permissible, and there are two reports about it." In al-Jawhara: "If a man commits zina with a woman, she gives birth from him and breastfeeds a girl with his milk, this girl is forbidden for him and for his ascendants and descendants." And al-Khujandi mentioned the contrary, saying: "If a woman gives birth from zina and milk descends for her, or milk descends for her without giving birth, and she breastfeeds a boy, then the breastfeeding is from her alone, not from the adulterer." And the words of al-Webari are explicit in that, and he said: "Lineage is not established from him [the adulterer] for breastfeeding." End quote. In al-Fath it is said that it is more correct (awjah) as previously mentioned. The text of al-Fath is: "And al-Webari mentioned that the prohibition is established from the mother's side only as long as lineage is not established, and then it is established from the father." And so too mentioned al-Asbijabi and the author of al-Yanabi', and it is more correct (awjah) because the prohibition from zina... up to what preceded. This is explicit that the prohibition is not established from the side of the adulterer because his lineage is not established. For this reason, al-Fath said, refuting the following statement of al-Khulasa: "If it is preponderant that the breastfed girl is not forbidden for the adulterer with milk from zina as we mentioned, then her not being forbidden for someone who is not the source of the milk is even more obvious." End quote. This is explicit that the words of al-Webari and others are about the non-establishment of prohibition on the adulterer himself, which implies as a priority the non-establishment of prohibition on his ascendants and descendants. And if it is established that there are two reports in the issue and one is apparently stronger, we do not turn away from it because of what was said in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli: "One does not turn away from understanding (diraya) when a transmission (riwaya) supports it." And what was mentioned by al-Sharniblali and others that the words of al-Fath are interpreted as meaning it is more correct in understanding (diraya) not in transmission (riwaya) is out of place, because both reports exist and one is apparently stronger. It seems they understood from al-Fath's statement "Because it contradicts what is recorded in the famous books" to be referring to his statement that it is more correct, but this is not so; rather it refers to what he quoted from al-Khulasa as we will mention. His statement: "For this reason he said in al-Khulasa" etc. I say: What al-Khulasa said is refuted in Fath al-Qadir because it contradicts what is in the famous books, as it would imply the prohibition of the daughter of the wet nurse with milk other than the husband's to the husband, as a priority. End quote. Meaning: what is explicitly stated in the famous books is that if the milk belongs to someone other than the husband, the breastfed girl is not forbidden for the husband. And the statement of al-Khulasa, "If she breastfeeds not with milk from zina, she is forbidden for the adulterer," implies a contradiction of what is recorded in the famous books, so it is rejected. His statement: "And their words apparently" etc. That is, as understood from the previous restriction to the adulterer's ascendants and descendants, and from the reasoning that prohibition is based on partiality (al-bu'diyya). In al-Fath from al-Tajnis: "It is not permissible for the adulterer to marry the breastfed girl, nor for his father and grandfathers, nor for any of his children and their children. But the paternal uncle of the adulterer may marry her, just as it is permissible to marry the girl who was born from the adulterer because her lineage from the adulterer is not established such that the ruling of kinship and prohibition appears regarding the fathers of the adulterer and his children, due to consideration of partiality (juz'iyya) and partialness (bu'diyya). And there is no partiality between her and the uncle. If this is established regarding the one born from zina, then similarly regarding the one breastfed with milk from zina." End quote.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion (sharh) on the topic of rada' (breastfeeding) and its effect on marriage prohibitions. The author addresses a complex scenario: when a woman breastfeeds a child with milk that originated from a previous husband (or from zina), does that milk create kinship with the previous husband or only with the current? The ruling is that if the milk is from a lawful marriage, the husband is considered the father of the breastfed child for purposes of mahram. However, if the marriage ends and she marries another, the milk from the first husband ceases when she gives birth to the second's child. A key point is that if she becomes pregnant but hasn't given birth, Abu Hanifa holds the child is still attributed to the first husband. The author then shifts to milk from zina (adultery). The main dispute within the Hanafi school is whether the adulterer becomes a father through the milk. One report (in al-Khulasa and al-Jawhara) says yes, the same prohibitions apply. The other report (favored by al-Webari, al-Asbijabi, and the author of al-Yanabi') says no, because the milk is not from his sperm and no lineage is established from the adulterer. This latter view is declared 'awjah (more correct) by Fath al-Qadir from a diraya (reasoning) perspective. The practical difference is that if the milk from zina does not create kinship, then the adulterer can marry the breastfed girl, and so can his father and son. But if it does, they cannot. The passage clarifies that even those who hold the prohibition for the adulterer agree that it does not extend to his uncle or other collaterals. The author notes that there are two riwayat (reports) within the school, and the wiser course is to follow the opinion that aligns with the famous books (kutub mashhura), which is that the milk from zina does not establish kinship with the adulterer. This is a nuanced intra-Hanafi debate that balances textual evidence and rational reasoning.

Key Terms
رضاع (rada'): Milk-kinship; a legal relationship established through breastfeeding that creates the same marriage prohibitions as blood relations.
لبن (laban): Milk; in this context, human breast milk that triggers milk-kinship.
زنا (zina): Adultery or fornication; illicit sexual intercourse.
بعضية (bu'diyya): Partiality; the concept that the child is a 'part' of the father, which is the basis for inheritance and marriage prohibitions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view (mufta bihi), what is the reason milk from zina does not create marriage prohibition with the adulterer?
A) Because zina is a sin and thus cannot produce legal effects.
B) Because the milk is not from the adulterer's sperm and no lineage is established.
C) Because the woman did not intend to create milk-kinship.
D) Because the breastfed child must be under two years old.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, milk from zina does not establish milk-kinship with the adulterer because the milk is not a part of him; only the mother's side creates prohibitions.

Nikah — Marriage
advanced
12 min
Milk from Zina and Its Effect on Foster Relations: The Hanafi Mufta Bihi
Clarifies Hanafi mufta bihi on milk from zina and its effect on foster relations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi on whether milk from zina creates marriage prohibition and explain the principle that fosterage follows lineage.

Core Idea
Fosterage follows lineage: milk from zina does not create prohibition for the father's relatives because the child's lineage is not established.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a nuanced issue: can milk produced from zina (illicit intercourse) or li'an (mutual imprecation) create fosterage relations that prohibit marriage? The author navigates apparent contradictions in the Hanafi school and clarifies the relied-upon position (mu'tamad). By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key principle and how it applies to concrete cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Issue
The central question is whether milk from zina (or li'an) attaches marriage prohibition (tahrim) to the father (the one who committed zina) and his ascendants/descendants.
The passage focuses on the father's side; there is consensus on the mother's side.
2
State the Mu'tamad Hanafi Position
According to the mu'tamad, milk from zina does NOT attach prohibition to the father's lineage (his father, sons, etc.). However, the father himself is prohibited from marrying the foster-child because she is his biological daughter (from zina), not because of the milk.
This resolves an apparent contradiction: earlier texts may seem to say prohibition applies, but they refer to the father's own case due to paternity.
3
Explain the Principle
The principle is: fosterage follows lineage (nasab). If the child's lineage from the man is established (as in lawful marriage or shubha), then fosterage relations create prohibition. Since zina does not establish lineage, no prohibition attaches for the father's relatives.
This is supported by the example of a man claiming a son from zina – the son does not inherit, and the slave-girl does not become umm walad.
4
Contrast with Other Schools
Imam Malik (in the famous view) holds that milk from zina does create prohibition for the father's lineage. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that it creates no prohibition at all, even for the father himself.
The Shafi'i position is consistent: since lineage is not established, no fosterage arises.

قلت : وهذا مخالف لما نقله المؤلف في فصل المحرمات من أنه تحرم عليه أخته من الزنا وبنت أخيه وبنت أخته وقدمنا الكلام فيه فليراجع قوله : (إن لبن الفحل الزاني لا يتعلق به التحريم) أي على أصوله وفروعه أما حرمة تلك الرضيعة على الزاني نفسه فليست بسبب اللبن بل لكونها بنت المزني بها كما مر وعلمت ما فيه وجعله هذا هو المعتمد في المذهب مفيد لحمله الأوجهية في كلام الكمال على الرواية أيضاً قوله : فالمراد بلبن (الفحل أي كما وقع في عبارة القدوري حيث قال : ولبن الفحل يتعلق به التحريم. قال : وتثبت الحرمة من اللبن النازل بالزنا وولد الملاعنة في حق الفحل عندنا وبه قال مالك في المشهور. وعند الشافعي لا يثبت في الزنا والمنفية باللعان وهكذا ذكر الوبري والأسبيجابي وصاحب الينابيع وتثبت في حق الأم بالإجماع ا.هـ. وظاهر ما في الخانية أنه المذهب فإنه قال : رجل زنى بامرأة فولدت منه فأرضعت بهذا اللبن صغيرة لا يجوز لهذا الزاني ولا لأحد من آبائه وأجداده نكاح هذه الصبية. وذكر في الدعوى رجل قال لمملوك هذا ابني من الزنا ثم اشتراه مع عتق المملوك ولا تصير الجارية أم ولد له ا هـ. وإنما تمسك بمسألة الدعوى لأنها دليل على أن الزنا كالحلال في ثبوت البنوة وإلا كان لغواً، وإن وطئ امرأة بشبهة فحبلت منه فأرضعت صبياً فهو ابن الواطئ من الرضاع. وعلى هذا كل من يثبت نسبه من الواطئ يثبت من الرضاع. ومن لا يثبت نسبه منه لا يثبت منه الرضاع كذا في الجوهرة. فالمراد بلبن الفحل على قول من جعل الزنا كالحلال لبن حدث من حمل رجل وعلى قول من فرق يقال لا من زنا
I say: This contradicts what the author transmitted in the chapter on prohibited women that his sister from zina, his brother's daughter, and his sister's daughter are prohibited for him, and we have already discussed it, so refer back. His statement: (Indeed, the milk of the adulterous man does not attach prohibition [to him and his ascendants and descendants]) meaning his statement: (except the prohibition of that foster-daughter on the adulterer himself is not due to the milk but because she is the daughter of the woman with whom he committed zina) as has passed, and you know what is in it. And his making this the relied-upon position in the school indicates that the interpretation of the ambiguity in the words of al-Kamal is also by narration. His statement: (So what is meant by milk of the man) as occurred in the expression of al-Quduri where he said: The milk of the man attaches prohibition. He said: And the prohibition is established from milk that falls by zina and the child of li'an in relation to the man according to us, and Malik said so in the famous view. According to al-Shafi'i, it is not established in zina nor in the woman expelled by li'an. Thus mentioned al-Obari, al-Asbijabi, and the author of al-Yanabi'. And it is established in relation to the mother by consensus. End. And what is apparent in al-Khaniyya is that it is the school, for he said: A man committed zina with a woman and she gave birth from him then she breastfed a small girl with that milk; this man, nor any of his fathers and grandfathers, may marry this girl. And he mentioned in the chapter of claims: A man said about his slave 'this is my son from zina' then he bought him, but the slave is not emancipated and the slave-girl does not become umm walad for him. End. He only held onto the case of the claim because it is evidence that zina is like lawful in establishing sonship, otherwise it would be futile. And if a man had intercourse with a woman erroneously (shubha) and she conceived from him and she breastfed a boy, then he is the son of the intercourse man by fosterage. Upon this, everyone whose lineage is established from the man is established from fosterage. And one whose lineage is not established from him is not established from fosterage. Likewise in al-Jawhara. So what is meant by milk of the man according to the one who treats zina like lawful is milk that occurred from a man's pregnancy, and according to the one who distinguishes, it is said: no, from zina.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage deals with the effect of milk produced from zina (illegitimate sexual intercourse) or from li'an (mutual imprecation) on marriage prohibitions. The author begins by noting a potential contradiction with an earlier statement, then explains that the relied-upon (mu'tamad) position in the Hanafi school is that milk from zina does not attach prohibition to the father (the one who committed zina) and his relatives. However, the prohibition on the father marrying the girl he breastfed himself is not due to the milk but because she is his daughter from the woman he committed zina with. The text quotes al-Quduri who says 'the milk of the man attaches prohibition' — this is interpreted as referring to lawful milk, not milk from zina. Then the author states the positions: according to Hanafis and Malik (in the famous view), milk from zina and from li'an establishes prohibition for the father. According to Shafi'i, it does not, for zina and li'an cases. For the mother, there is consensus that the milk establishes prohibition. The author then cites al-Khaniyya as supporting the view that milk from zina does make marriage impermissible for the father's lineage. To reconcile, the author explains that the father's prohibition is not due to the milk per se but due to paternity. The key principle is: fosterage follows lineage. If lineage is established (as in lawful birth), fosterage is established; if lineage is not established (as in zina), fosterage is not established. An example: if a man has intercourse with a woman under shubha (erroneous belief) and she gives birth, the lineage is established, so if that child breastfeeds someone, it creates foster relations. Therefore, 'milk of the man' in the classification of those who treat zina like lawful means milk from a conception by a man (i.e., from a valid or invalid marriage where lineage is established), while others say it does not apply to zina.

Key Terms
لبن الفحل (laban al-fahl): Milk produced as a result of a man's paternity; the milk that flows due to pregnancy from a specific man.
الزنا (al-zinā): Illicit sexual intercourse (fornication or adultery) that does not establish legal lineage.
الملاعنة (al-mulā'ana): Mutual imprecation (li'an) between spouses leading to negation of paternity.
المعتمد (al-mu'tamad): The relied-upon position in the Hanafi madhhab that is given preference (tarjih).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mufta bihi, why is the man who committed zina prohibited from marrying his biological daughter who was breastfed by another woman?
A) Because the milk from zina creates fosterage, making her his foster-daughter.
B) Because she is his biological daughter, and paternity creates prohibition regardless of milk.
C) Because the milk from any woman creates fosterage, and this includes zina.
D) Because the father's ancestors are also prohibited.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that milk from zina does not create marriage prohibition for the father's lineage; the father's own prohibition is due to paternity, not the milk.

Fosterage Prohibitions: Sharing the Same Breast
Ruling on fosterage prohibitions with commentary on conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which two children become foster-siblings and identify the relatives prohibited for marriage due to fosterage.

Core Idea
Sharing the same milk from the same breast makes children foster-siblings, regardless of time.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary in al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the fundamental rule of fosterage prohibitions. The key is that two children who suckle from the same breast become siblings by milk, and this kinship carries the same marriage prohibitions as blood relations. Understanding the precise conditions—especially the role of time and space—is crucial to applying this rule correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary rule
Two children who have suckled from the same breast are foster-siblings and cannot marry each other.
The text says 'لا حل بين رضيعي ثدي'.
2
Distinguish types of foster-siblings
If the milk comes from two different husbands, the children are maternal foster-siblings; if from one husband, full foster-siblings.
This affects who else is prohibited (e.g., paternal vs maternal relatives).
3
Extend prohibitions to relatives
The prohibition includes the foster-mother's biological children, her siblings, and her grandchildren – they are analogous to blood aunts and nephews.
The text mentions 'ولد مرضعة وولد ولدها' and 'أخت المرضعة'.
4
Clarify temporal condition
Temporal coincidence is not required; one child may be breastfed years before or after the other, yet they remain siblings.
The commentary emphasizes that being 'سابقاً بالسن' does not matter.
5
Understand spatial condition
Sharing the same breast (i.e., the same milk) is sufficient; the author mentions both temporal and spatial gathering to indicate that temporal is not necessary.
The commentary shows that if only spatial were mentioned, it would still be sufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا حل بين رضيعي ثدي أي بين من اجتمعا على الارتضاع من ثدي واحد في وقت واحد لأنهما أخوان من الرضاع، فإن كان اللبن من زوجين فهما أخوان لأم أو أختان م، وإن كان لرجل فأخوان لأب وأم أو أختان لهما، ولو كان تحت رجل امرأتان فأرضعت كل منهما صبية فهما أختان لأب رضاعاً. كذا في الفتاوى البزازية قوله : (وبين مرضعة وولد مرضعتها وولد ولدها والمرضعة الأولى بفتح الضاد اسم مفعول والثانية بكسرها أي لا حل بين الصغيرة المرضعة وولد المرأة التي أرضعتهما لأنهما أخوان من الرضاع، ولا فرق بين كون ولد التي أرضعت رضيعاً مع المرضعة أو كان سابقاً بالسن بسنين كثيرة أو مسبوقاً بارتضاعها بأن ولد بعده بسنين، وكذا لا يتزوج أخت المرضعة لأنها خالته، ولا ولد ولدها لأنه ولد الأخ. وفي آخر المبسوط : ولو كانت أم البنات أرضعت إحدى البنين وأم البنين أرضعت إحدى البنات لم يكن للابن المرتضع من أم البنات أن يتزوج واحدة منهن، وكان لإخوته أن يتزوجوا بنات الأخرى إلا الابنة التي أرضعتها أمهم وحدها لأنها أختهم من الرضاعة. وإنما لم يكتف المصنف بقوله ولا حل بين رضيعي ثدي عما بعده لأنه ربما أن الاجتماع من حيث الزمان لا بد منه فذكر الاجتماع من حيث الزمان ثم أردفه يوهم بإثبات الحرمة بالاجتماع من حيث المكان وهو الثدي ليفيد أنه لا فرق، لكن لو اقتصر على الثاني لاستغنى عن الأول قوله : (ولا فرق بين كون ولد التي أرضعت رضيعاً) اسم الكون ما أضيف إليه ورضيعاً خبره ومفعول أرضعت محذوف أي أرضعت المرضعة، وقوله مع المرضعة الاجتماع متعلق بـ رضيعاً وكان عليه أن يزيد بعد قوله أو مسبوقاً بارتضاعها أو لم ترضعه أصلاً أنه غير شرط كما يأتي قريباً عن النهر قوله : (وإنما لم يكتف اشتراط إرضاعها ولدها مع يوهم المصنف الخ) قال الرملي: من أين أن الاجتماع من حيث الزمان لا بد منه وليس فيه ما يدل يوهم عليه. قال في النهر وأفاد بالجملة الأولى اشتراط الاجتماع من حيث المكان في الأجنبيين وبالثانية
His statement: (And there is no marriage between two foster-children of a breast) meaning between two who gathered in suckling from one breast at one time because they are foster-siblings. If the milk is from two husbands, then they are maternal foster-siblings or two sisters; if from one man, then full foster-siblings or full foster-sisters. If one man has two wives and each one breastfed a girl, then they are paternal foster-sisters. Likewise in al-Fatawa al-Bazzaziyya. His statement: (And between a foster-mother and the child of her foster-mother and the child of her child) the first 'murdi'a' is passive participle, the second is active participle, meaning there is no marriage between the small girl who is being breastfed and the child of the woman who breastfed them because they are foster-siblings. There is no difference whether the child of the woman who breastfed was a foster-child with the foster-mother or was older by many years or was preceded by her breastfeeding such that he was born after her. Likewise, he may not marry the sister of the foster-mother because she is his maternal aunt, nor the child of her child because he is the brother's son. In the end of al-Mabsut: If the mother of daughters breastfed one of the sons and the mother of sons breastfed one of the daughters, then the son who was breastfed by the mother of daughters may not marry any of them, but his brothers may marry the other daughters except the one whom their mother breastfed alone because she is their foster-sister. The author did not suffice with his statement 'and there is no marriage between two foster-children of a breast' for what follows because perhaps the gathering in terms of time is necessary, so he mentioned gathering in terms of time then appended it implying establishing prohibition by gathering in terms of place which is the breast to indicate that there is no difference. But if he had sufficed with the second, he would have dispensed with the first. His statement: (And there is no difference between the child of the woman who breastfed being a foster-child) the noun of 'being' is what is added to it, and 'foster-child' is its predicate, and the object of 'breastfed' is omitted meaning the woman breastfed, and his statement 'with the foster-mother' the gathering is related to 'foster-child'. It was necessary for him to add after his statement 'or preceded by her breastfeeding' or 'she did not breastfeed him at all' that it is not a condition, as will come soon from al-Nahr. His statement: (And he did not suffice with the condition of her breastfeeding her child with the foster-mother implying the author etc.) al-Ramli said: Where does it indicate that gathering in terms of time is necessary? There is nothing in it that implies it. He said in al-Nahr: And he indicated by the first sentence the condition of gathering in terms of place for two unrelated persons, and by the second...
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq with commentary from al-Bahr al-Raiq explaining the prohibition of marriage between foster-children and their relatives. The base text states that there is no marriage between two children who shared the same breast at the same time; they are foster-siblings. The commentary elaborates: if the milk comes from two husbands, the children are maternal foster-siblings; if from one man, full foster-siblings. An example with two wives shows that daughters breastfed by different wives of the same man become paternal foster-sisters. The prohibition also extends to the foster-mother, her children, and grandchildren. There is no difference whether the foster-mother's child was breastfed later or earlier; any child of hers is a sibling to the breastfed child. Additionally, one cannot marry the foster-mother's sister (one's foster-maternal aunt) nor the foster-mother's grandchild. The commentary then discusses why the author did not suffice with the condition of temporal coincidence, explaining that both temporal and spatial (place of the breast) coincidence are considered, but spatial alone would suffice. Finally, the commentary notes a need to clarify that it is not a condition for the foster-mother to have breastfed her own child; even if she did not, her biological children are still siblings of the breastfed child.

Key Terms
رضيع (radī'): A child who has been breastfed by a woman, establishing foster-relationship.
رضيعة (radī'a): A female child who has been breastfed.
الرضاع (al-riḍā'): The legal concept of fosterage established by breastfeeding.
ثدي (thady): Breast; used in the phrase 'رضيعي ثدي' meaning two children who suckled from the same breast.
مرضعة (murḍi'a): The woman who breastfeeds (foster-mother).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a condition for two children to be considered foster-siblings?
A) They suckled from the same woman.
B) They suckled from the same breast.
C) They suckled at the same time.
D) The woman's milk is the same.

Key Takeaway
Two children who have suckled from the same breast become foster-siblings, and all the prohibitions of blood siblings apply, regardless of the timing of their feedings.

Ruling on Milk Mixed with Food: Abu Hanifa's Position and the Dispute with the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fosterage from mixed milk

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on milk mixed with food and explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the criterion of predominance.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa holds that milk mixed with food never establishes fosterage prohibition because food is the primary source of nourishment.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the ruling on milk mixed with food (e.g., bread soaked in milk). The base text from Kanz al-Daqa'iq states flatly that such a mixture does not cause prohibition. The commentator clarifies that this is Abu Hanifa's view, which considers nourishment as the basis and food as predominant. The Sahibayn disagree, looking at external predominance. The passage also discusses two narrations from Abu Hanifa regarding sipping the mixture.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and default position
The base text says milk mixed with food does not make marriage prohibited. This is Abu Hanifa's position, and it is the correct view (al-sahih).
The ruling is absolute — no distinction between cooked or uncooked, or whether milk is visibly predominant.
2
Understand the reasoning (illa)
The basis of fosterage prohibition is nourishment (taghadhdhī) that contributes to the child's growth. In a mixture, food is the primary source of nourishment, milk is subordinate. Predominance is considered at the time of digestion, not externally.
Abu Hanifa focuses on internal digestion; the Sahibayn look at external appearance.
3
Note the Sahibayn's objection
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that if the milk is externally predominant (e.g., it drips when the morsel is lifted), then prohibition attaches, based on the principle of considering the evident majority.
They analogize to other mixtures like wine and water.
4
Recognize the scope of ikhtilaf
The disagreement applies only to uncooked mixtures. If the mixture is cooked, all agree there is no prohibition because the milk is thoroughly incorporated. Bread is considered food.
Cooking changes the nature of the mixture.
5
Analyze the sipping nuance
Two narrations from Abu Hanifa: (1) no difference between eating and sipping (no prohibition), (2) sipping is like drinking milk separately, so prohibition attaches. The correct view is the first, but caution may be observed.
The commentator leans toward the first cause based on Muhammad's wording.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (واللبن المخلوط بالطعام لا يحرم أطلقه فأفاد أنه لا فرق بين كون اللبن غالباً بحيث يتقاطر عند رفع اللقمة أو لا عند أبي حنيفة وهو الصحيح مطبوخاً أو لا، لأن الطعام أصل واللبن تابع فيما هو المقصود وهو التغذي وهو مناط التحريم، ولأن الغلبة إنما تعتبر حالة الوصول إلى المعدة وفي تلك الحالة الطعام هو الغالب، وقالا ، إن كان اللبن غالباً تعلق به التحريم نظراً للغالب، والخلاف فيما إذا لم تمسه النار، أما المطبوخ فلا اتفاقاً. ويدخل في الطعام الخبز. وقال المصنف في المستصفى : إنما لم يثبت التحريم عنده إذا لم يشربه، أما إذا حساه ينبغي أن يثبت، ويؤيده ما في فتاوى قاضيخان. هذا إذا أكل الطعام لقمة لقمة، فإذا حساه حسواً ثبتت الحرمة في قولهم جميعاً. والحق أن لقول أبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه علتين كما ذكرنا، فعلى الأولى لا فرق بين الحسو وغيره، وعلى الثانية يفرق بين الحسو وغيره كما أفاده في المحيط قال : ووضع محمد في الأكل يدل على هذا ا هـ. وفي القاموس : حسا زيد المرق شربه شيئاً بعد شيء. وقيد بكونه مخلوطاً لأن لبن المرأة إذا جبن وأطعم الصبي تعلق به التحريم كذا في الجوهرة. وفي البدائع خلافه ولفظه: ولو جعل رضي الصواب عدم التقييد
His statement: (And milk mixed with food does not cause prohibition) He released it absolutely so it indicates that there is no difference between whether the milk is predominant to the extent that it drips when the morsel is lifted or not according to Abu Hanifa, and it is the correct view, whether cooked or not, because the food is the origin and the milk is subordinate in what is intended, which is nourishment, and it is the basis of prohibition. And because predominance is only considered at the time of reaching the stomach, and in that state the food is predominant. And they two said: If the milk is predominant, it attaches prohibition, looking at the predominant. The disagreement is when fire has not touched it; as for cooked, no disagreement. Bread is included in food. And the author said in al-Mustasfa: He only did not establish prohibition if he did not drink it; but if he sips it, it should be established. And it is supported by what is in the Fatawa of Qadikhan. This is if he ate the food morsel by morsel, but if he sips it as a drink, prohibition is established in all their statements. The truth is that Abu Hanifa's statement has two causes as we mentioned; according to the first, no difference between sipping and other; according to the second, there is a difference between sipping and other as stated in al-Muhit. He said: And Muhammad's placing in the matter of eating indicates this. End. In al-Qamus: 'Hasa' Zaid the soup: he drank it piece by piece. And it is restricted to being mixed because if a woman's milk is turned into cheese and fed to a boy, prohibition is attached. Likewise in al-Jawhara. And in al-Bada'i', there is a contrary view and its wording: And if he made... the correct opinion is not to restrict.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage discusses the Hanafi ruling on milk that is mixed with food and whether it establishes fosterage prohibition. The base text from Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that milk mixed with food does not cause prohibition. The commentator explains that Abu Hanifa holds this view absolutely: it makes no difference whether the milk is predominant (to the point that it drips when you lift the morsel) or not, whether it is cooked or not. The reasoning is that the purpose is nourishment, and food is the primary source while milk is subordinate. Predominance is considered only when the mixture reaches the stomach, and at that point food is predominant. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree: if milk is predominant in the mixture, then prohibition attaches; if food is predominant, no prohibition. This ikhtilaf applies when the mixture has not been cooked; if it is cooked, all agree there is no prohibition (because the milk is thoroughly incorporated). Bread is included as food. The commentator then notes a refinement from al-Mustasfa: Abu Hanifa's ruling applies only if the person eats the mixture morsel by morsel (solid). If he sips (drinks) the mixture, then prohibition should be established according to a narration, and this is supported by Qadikhan. However, the truth is that Abu Hanifa's position has two causes: one of them would still allow even sipping (no prohibition), while the other would distinguish (sip causes prohibition). The commentator also mentions that milk turned into cheese and fed to a child does establish prohibition (because it is pure milk). Finally, al-Bada'i' opposes some of this, and the correct opinion is not to restrict the ruling. This passage clarifies the nuances within the Hanafi school on when mixed milk triggers fosterage.

Key Terms
اللبن المخلوط بالطعام (al-laban al-makhlūṭ bil-ṭa'ām): Milk that has been mixed with food (like bread or soup) such that it is not pure milk.
الغالب (al-ghālib): The predominant component in a mixture. For the Sahibayn, if the milk is visibly predominant (e.g., drips when lifted), prohibition attaches.
التغذي (al-taghadhdhī): Nourishment; the basis for establishing fosterage. If the child's growth is primarily from the milk, prohibition arises.
الحسو (al-ḥasw): Sipping or drinking a liquid by taking it in small amounts. Here, it refers to drinking the liquid mixture (milk+food) rather than eating it solidly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling if a child eats bread soaked in milk where the milk is not visible separately?
A) Prohibition is established because milk is present
B) Prohibition is established only if the milk drips when the bread is lifted
C) No prohibition, because food predominates
D) No prohibition if cooked, but prohibition if uncooked

Key Takeaway
Milk mixed with food does not establish fosterage prohibition in the Hanafi school, because food predominates in nourishment, and the ruling is based on the child's growth, not the mere presence of milk.

Prohibition of Marriage with Foster Relatives
Ruling on prohibited marriages due to fosterage with explanation of conditions and commentary dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibited marriage relationships due to fosterage according to Hanafi fiqh and identify the conditions that trigger these prohibitions.

Core Idea
Suckling creates a mahram bond: foster mother and her close relatives become permanently prohibited for marriage.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq establishes the fundamental rules of fosterage (rida') in the Hanafi school. It lists who is prohibited to marry whom when children are breastfed by the same woman. The commentary clarifies that the prohibition extends beyond the immediate foster mother to her children, grandchildren, and even her sister, by analogy with blood relations.

Guided Path
1
Parse the Matn's Two Prohibitions
The matn first says 'no marriage between two suckling children of one breast' and then 'no marriage between a foster mother and the child of the foster mother and the child of her child.' Identify each prohibition.
The first prohibits marriage between two individuals who were breastfed by the same woman (they become foster siblings). The second prohibits marriage between the nursling and the foster mother's biological children and grandchildren.
2
Understand the Scope of Prohibition
The foster mother herself is prohibited (she becomes like a mother). The child of the foster mother (whether biological or also breastfed) becomes a sibling. The child of that child (grandchild) becomes a nephew/niece. All are mahram.
The commentary emphasizes that the time of suckling does not matter; even if the foster mother's child was born years later, the prohibition still applies.
3
Apply the Examples from al-Mabsut
Two families swap breastfeeding: the mother of daughters breastfeeds a son from another family, and the mother of sons breastfeeds a daughter. Determine which marriages are allowed.
The result: the suckling son cannot marry any daughter from either family because one mother is his foster mother (herself prohibited) and the other mother's daughters are his foster sisters.
4
Examine the Author's Wording and the Commentary Dispute
The author (Kanz) included two phrases to cover both the spatial condition (sharing the same breast) and the relationships with relatives. The commentary debates whether the first phrase (spatial) is necessary; al-Ramli argues it is not because the second phrase already covers relatives.
This shows the meticulousness of Hanafi jurists in ensuring no ambiguity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرضاع. لا حل بين رضيعي ثدي وبين مرضعة وولد مرضعتها وولد ولدها. قوله: (وبين مرضعة وولد مرضعتها وولد ولدها) والمرضعة الأولى بفتح الضاد اسم مفعول والثانية بكسرها أي لا حل بين الصغيرة المرضعة وولد المرأة التي أرضعتهما لأنهما أخوان من الرضاع، ولا فرق بين كون ولد التي أرضعت رضيعاً مع المرضعة أو كان سابقاً بالسن بسنين كثيرة أو مسبوقاً بارتضاعها بأن ولد بعده بسنين، وكذا لا يتزوج أخت المرضعة لأنها خالته، ولا ولد ولدها لأنه ولد الأخ. وفي آخر المبسوط: ولو كانت أم البنات أرضعت إحدى البنين وأم البنين أرضعت إحدى البنات لم يكن للابن المرتضع من أم البنات أن يتزوج واحدة منهن، وكان لإخوته أن يتزوجوا بنات الأخرى إلا الابنة التي أرضعتها أمهم وحدها لأنها أختهم من الرضاعة. وإنما لم يكتف المصنف بقوله ولا حل بين رضيعي ثدي عما بعده لأنه ربما أن الاجتماع من حيث الزمان لا بد منه فذكر الاجتماع من حيث الزمان ثم أردفه لئلا يوهم إثبات الحرمة بالاجتماع من حيث المكان وهو الثدي ليفيد أنه لا فرق، لكن لو اقتصر على الثاني لاستغنى عن الأول. قال الرملي: من أين أن الاجتماع من حيث الزمان لا بد منه وليس فيه ما يدل عليه. قال في النهر وأفاد بالجملة الأولى اشتراط الاجتماع من حيث المكان في الأجنبيين وبالثانية عدم اشتراطه في الأجنبية وولدها إذ المرضعة أخت لولدها رضاعاً، سواء أرضعت ولدها أو لا، وبهذا لا يستغنى بالثانية عن الأولى. هذا حاصل ما أفاد الشارح المحقق ووقع في البحر في تقرير هذا المحل خلط فاجتنبه. ا هـ كلام الرملي: نعم يظهر ما ذكره المؤلف في قول القدوري وكل صبيين اجتمعا على ثدي واحدة في مدة الرضاع لم يجز لأحدهما أن يتزوج بالآخر.
Book of Suckling. There is no marriage connection between two suckling children of one breast and between a foster mother and the child of the foster mother and the child of her child. He said: ('And between a foster mother and the child of the foster mother and the child of her child') – the first 'foster mother' (al-murdi'a) is with fatha on the dad, a passive participle, and the second is with kasra, meaning there is no marriage between the little girl who was suckled and the child of the woman who suckled her (the two boys) because they are brothers by suckling. There is no difference whether the child of the woman who suckled was suckled together with the nursling or was older by many years, or was preceded by her suckling (i.e., born after her). Likewise, one may not marry the sister of the foster mother because she is his maternal aunt, nor the child of her child because he is the child of a brother. And in the end of al-Mabsut: If the mother of the daughters suckled one of the sons and the mother of the sons suckled one of the daughters, the suckling son from the mother of the daughters may not marry any of them, but his brothers may marry the daughters of the other mother except the daughter whom their mother suckled alone, because she is their sister by suckling. The author did not suffice with his saying 'no marriage between two suckling children of one breast' after it, because perhaps being together in time is necessary, so he mentioned being together in time, then he added it to avoid giving the impression that the prohibition is established by being together in place (the breast) to indicate that there is no difference. But if he had limited to the second, he would have been independent of the first. al-Ramli said: Where does the necessity of being together in time come from? There is nothing in it indicating that. He said in al-Nahr: By the first sentence he indicated the condition of being together in place for two strangers, and by the second the absence of that condition for the stranger woman and her child, because the foster mother is the sister of her child by suckling, whether she suckled her child or not, and by this the second does not make the first dispensable. This is the summary of what the verifying commentator stated, and in al-Bahr there was confusion in this point, so avoid it. End of al-Ramli's speech: Yes, what the author mentioned in the saying of al-Quduri appears: 'Any two infants who share the same breast during the period of suckling may not marry each other.'
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, commented upon by al-Bahr al-Raiq. It establishes the prohibition of marriage between a child who was breastfed and the foster mother herself (who becomes his mother by suckling), as well as the child of the foster mother (her biological son or daughter) and the child of that child (i.e., her grandchildren). The prohibition is based on the principle that suckling creates mahram relationships akin to blood ties. The commentary clarifies that the foster mother is the woman who provides the milk, and the child of the foster mother becomes a sibling by suckling to the nursling. The time of the suckling is irrelevant—the prohibition applies whether the foster mother's child was born before or after the foster child. Additionally, the nursling cannot marry the foster mother's sister (who is like a maternal aunt) or her grandchildren (who are like nephews). The example from al-Mabsut illustrates a complex scenario: two families (one with daughters, one with sons) inter-suckle, and the rulings are applied to each child individually. The author of Kanz included two phrases ('two children of one breast' and 'foster mother and her children') to cover both the condition of sharing the same breast in time and the relationship with the foster mother's relatives. The commentary explains that the first phrase ensures the time condition, while the second covers the relatives. However, al-Ramli notes that the time condition is not actually required; the second phrase alone would suffice, but the author included both for clarity. The passage ends with a quote from al-Quduri confirming the basic rule: any two infants who share a breast during the suckling period are forbidden to marry.

Key Terms
الرضاع (al-rida'): The act of a child being breastfed by a woman other than his biological mother, which creates legal kinship.
المُرضِعَة (al-murdi'a): The woman who provides suckling; the foster mother.
الرَّضيع (al-radee'): The infant who is breastfed; the foster child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, a man who was breastfed by a woman is prohibited from marrying which of the following?
A) The foster mother's sister
B) The foster mother's niece
C) The foster mother's daughter-in-law
D) The foster mother's mother

Key Takeaway
Suckling creates a network of prohibited marriage partners equivalent to those from blood relations, extending to the foster mother's children, grandchildren, and siblings.
