Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
10 min
Exceptions to Fosterage: Enema, Male Milk, and Animal Milk
Commentary on what does not establish fosterage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three exceptions to fosterage according to the Hanafi school and explain the legal reasoning behind each exception.

Core Idea
Fosterage requires human milk consumed by mouth; enema, male milk, and animal milk do not create prohibition.

The Hanafi school establishes strict conditions for fosterage (rada‘) to create marriage prohibitions. This lesson explains three common scenarios that are often mistaken as creating fosterage: administering milk via enema, milk of a man, and milk of a sheep or any animal. Understanding these exceptions prevents erroneous rulings, as illustrated by the famous story of Imam al-Bukhari's mistake.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three exceptions
Enumerate each as mentioned in the text: enema (ihtiqan), male milk, animal milk.
2
Examine the reasoning for enema
It is not a means of nourishment; it does not reach the stomach via the mouth.
3
Examine the reasoning for male milk
A man cannot give birth; his milk is not considered true milk for fosterage.
4
Examine the reasoning for animal milk
Animal milk has the ruling of food, not human milk; the hadith's 'breast' refers to a woman's.
5
Analyze the al-Bukhari story
Misapplication of hadith due to not considering the specific conditions; learn the importance of proper istinbat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرضاع
لا الاحتقان ولبن الرجل والشاة ولو أرضعت ضرتها حرمتا ولا مهر للكبيرة إن لم تكن أرضعتها بإذنها لأنها أم امرأته، ولا يجوز الجمع بين هذه الرضيعة وبنت الميتة لأنهما أختان. وفي فتح القدير: لبن الميتة طاهر عند أبي حنيفة لأن التنجس بالموت لما حلته الحياة قبله وهو منتف في اللبن، وهما وإن قالا بنجاسته للمجاورة للوعاء النجس لا يمنع من الحرمة كما لو حلب في إناء نجس وأوجر به صبي تثبت. وهذا بخلاف وطء الميتة فإنه لا يتعلق به حرمة المصاهرة بالإجماع. والفرق أن المقصود من اللبن التغدي والموت لا يمنع منه، والمقصود من الوطء اللذة المعتادة وذلك لا يوجد في وطء الميتة. كذا في الجوهرة.
قوله: (لا الاحتقان) أي الاحتقان باللبن لا يوجب الحرمة لأنه ليس مما يتغذى به ولذا لا يثبت بالإقطار في الإحليل والأذن والجائفة والآمة. قال في المغرب: الصواب حقن إذا عولج بالحقنة واحتقن بالضم غير جائز. وفي تاج المصادر الاحتقان حقنه کردن فجعله متعدياً فعلى هذا يجوز استعماله على بناء المفعول وهو الأكثر في استعمال الفقهاء. كذا في المعراج والنهاية. وفي فتح القدير: وهذا غلط لأن ما في تاج المصادر من التفسير لا يفيد تعدية الافتعال منه للمفعول الصريح كالصبي في عبارة الهداية حيث قال: إذا احتقن الصبي بل إلى الحقنة والكلام في بنائه للمفعول الذي هو الصبي ومعلوم أن كل قاصر يجوز بناؤه للمفعول بالنسبة إلى المجرور والظرف كجلس في الدار ومر بزيد وليس يلزم من جواز البناء باعتبار الآلة والظرف جوازه بالنسبة إلى المفعول بل إذا كان متعدياً إليه بنفسه ا هـ. وفي المصباح: حقنت المريض إذا وصلت الدواء إلى باطنه من مخرجه بالمحقنة واحتقن هو والاسم الحقنة مثل الغرفة من الاغتراف ثم أطلقت على ما يتداوى به والجمع حقن مثل غرفة وغرف ا هـ.
قوله: (ولبن الرجل) أي لا يوجب الحرمة لأنه ليس بلبن على الحقيقة لأن اللبن إنما يتصور ممن تتصور منه الولادة فصار كالصغيرة التي لم تبلغ تسع سنين كما قدمناه. وإذا نزل للخنثى لبن إن علم أن امرأة تعلق به التحريم وإن علم أنه رجل لم يتعلق به تحريم، وإن أشكل إن قال النساء إنه لا يكون على غزارته إلا للمرأة تعلق به التحريم احتياطاً، وإن لم يقلن ذلك لم يتعلق به تحريم. كذا في الجوهرة.
وهي آلة الاحتقان، قوله: (حقنه كردن) أي فعل الحقنة فكردن مصدر ماضیه کرد و مضارعه کند و اسم فاعله کرده واسم المفعول كننده، فالأول بمعنى فعل والثاني بمعنى يفعل والثالث بمعنى فاعل، والرابع بمعنى مفعول و كردن بمعنی فعلاً فحقنه کردن بمعنى فعل الحقنة لأن الإضافة في اللغة الفارسية مقلوبة. كذا أفادنيه بعض من له خبرة بها. قوله: (وفي فتح القدير وهذا غلط الخ) قال في النهر: أنت خبير بأن هذا إنما يتم ا أن لو كانت الرواية محقنة كردن وكان هذا هو الواقع في نسخته، أما إذا كانت حقنه كردن كما مر أي فعل الحقنة ففي كونه غلطاً نظر فتدبر ا.هـ. وفيه نطر إذ لا يلزم من تفسير الاحتقان بفعل الحقنة تعديته للمفعول الصريح كما لو فسرت الاغتسال بفعل الغسل.
قوله: (والشاة) أي لبن الشاة لا يوجب الحرمة حتى لو ارتضع صبي وصبية على لبن شاة فلا أخوة بينهما لأن الأمومة لا تثبت به لأنه لا حرمة له ولأن لبن البهائم له حكم الطعام فلا فرق بين الشاة وغيرها من غير الآدمي. قيد بالثلاثة لأن الوجور والسعوط تثبت به الحرمة اتفاقاً. وإنما يفسد الصوم بما ذكر ما عدا الإقطار في الإحليل لأن الفطر يتعلق بالوصول إلى الجوف. والوجور بفتح الواو والدواء يصب في الحلق ويقال أوجرته ووجرته، والسعوط صبه في الأنف. وفي المصباح: والسعوط مثال رسول دواء يصب في الأنف، والسعوط مثل قعود مصدر، وأسعطه الدواء يتعدى إلى مفعولين واستعط زيد والمسعط بضم الميم الوعاء يجعل فيه السعوط وهو من النوادر التي جاءت بالضم وقياسها الكسر لأنه اسم آلة. وإنما ضمت الميم ليوافق الأبنية الغالبة مثل «فعلل» ولو كسرت أدى إلى بناء مفقود إذ ليس في الكلام مفعل ولا فعلل بكسر الأول وضم الثالث ا هـ. وقد حكي في المبسوط والكشف الكبير أن البخاري صاحب الأخبار دخل بخارى وجعل يفتي فقال له أبو حفص الكبير: لا تفعل فأبى أن يقبل نصيحته حتى استفتى في هذه المسئلة فأفتى بثبوت الحرمة بين صبيين ارتضعا من ثدي لبن شاة تمسكاً بقوله عليه السلام «كل صبيين اجتمعا على ثدي واحد حرم الآخر» وقد أخطأ لفوات الرأي وهو أنه لم يتأمل أن الحكم متعلق بالجزئية والبعضية فأخرجوه من بخارى. وفي فتح القدير بعد هذه الحكاية: ومن لم يدق نظره في مناط الأحكام وحكمها كثر خطؤه وكان ذلك في زمن الشيخ أبي حفص الكبير ومولده مولد الشافعي فإنهما ولدا معاً في العام الذي توفي فيه أبو حنيفة وهو سنة خمسين ومائة ا هـ.
قوله: (ولو أرضعت ضرتها حرمتا) أي لو أرضعت الكبيرة الصغيرة التي هي زوجة زوجها حرمتا على الزوج لأنه يصير جامعاً بين الأم والبنت رضاعاً ففسد نكاحهما، ولم ينفسخ لأن المذهب عند علمائنا أن النكاح لا يرتفع بحرمة الرضاع والمصاهرة بل يفسد حتى لو وطئها قبل التفريق لا يجب عليه الحد، اشتبه الأمر أو لم يشتبه. نص عليه محمد في الأصل، وذكره الشارح في باب اللعان. وعلى هذا فقوله في المعراج فينفسخ النكاح لا يخالفه لأن الانفساخ غيره. وفي البزازية: وبثبوت حرمة المصاهرة وحرمة الرضاع لا يرتفع بهما النكاح حتى لا تملك المرأة التزوج بزوج آخر إلا بعد المتاركة وإن مضى عليه سنون ا هـ. وقدمنا أنه لا بد في الفاسد من تفريق القاضي أو المتاركة بالقول في المدخولة وفي غيرها يكتفى بالمفارقة بالأبدان. وينبغي أن يكون الفساد في الرضاع الطارئ على النكاح، أما لو تزوج امرأة ثم أرضعتها زوجته الأخرى أو أجنبية فسد النكاح في الأصح. قيد بالثلاثة أي بالاحتقان ولبن الرجل والشاة وكان عليه أن يذكره عند قوله «لا الاحتقان» فيقول قيد به الخ إذ لا مدخل في ذلك اللبن الرجل والشاة فإنه لا فرق فيه بين الشرب والوجور والسعوط تأمل. قوله: (فقوله في المعراج فينفسخ النكاح لا يخالفه) كذا في أغلب النسخ، وفي بعضها يخالفه بدون «لا» وهو الظاهر بدليل التعليل. قوله: (أما لو تزوج امرأة الخ) قال الرملي: سيأتي آخر الباب.
Chapter of Fosterage
Enema with milk, and milk of a man and a sheep do not cause prohibition. If a woman breastfed her co-wife, both become forbidden (to the husband), and there is no mahr for the elder if she did not breastfeed with her permission, because she is the mother of his wife. And it is not permissible to combine this foster daughter with the daughter of the deceased because they are sisters. In Fath al-Qadir: The milk of a deceased woman is pure according to Abu Hanifa because impurity through death applies to what life had entered, and it is absent in milk. The two (companions) say it is impure due to proximity to an impure container, but that does not prevent prohibition (of fosterage), as if it were milked into an impure vessel and then fed to an infant, it establishes (fosterage). This is unlike intercourse with a dead woman, because by consensus it does not establish a marriage prohibition. The difference is that the purpose of milk is nourishment, and death does not prevent that, while the purpose of intercourse is customary pleasure, and that is not found in intercourse with a dead woman. Thus in al-Jawhara.
His statement: (Enema with milk) meaning enema with milk does not cause prohibition because it is not something that nourishes; therefore it is not established by instillation into the urethra, ear, perforated wound, or head wound. He said in al-Mughrib: The correct form is haqana (to treat with an enema) and ihtiqan (to receive an enema) with a damma (u) is not permissible. In Taj al-Masadir, al-ihtiqan means 'he performed an enema' (haqana kardan), making it transitive; accordingly, it is permissible to use it in the passive form, which is the prevalent usage among jurists. Thus in al-Mi'raj and al-Nihaya. In Fath al-Qadir: This is a mistake because the interpretation in Taj al-Masadir does not make the verbal noun (ifti'al) transitive to a direct object like 'the boy' in the statement of al-Hidayah: 'when the boy receives an enema' (ihtaqana al-sabi). Rather, the discussion is about its passive construction referring to the boy, and it is known that every intransitive verb can be built in the passive form relative to a prepositional phrase or adverb, as in 'he sat in the house' and 'he passed by Zaid'. And it does not necessarily follow that the permissibility of passive construction with respect to instrument and circumstance implies permissibility with respect to a direct object; rather, (only) if it is directly transitive. End. In al-Misbah: I gave an enema to the patient (haqantu al-marida) when I delivered medicine into his interior through his outlet using an enema, and he received an enema (ihtaqana). The noun is al-huqna (enema) like al-ghurfa from al-ightiraf. Then it was used for what is treated with, and the plural is huaqan like ghuraf and ghuraf. End.
His statement: (And milk of a man) meaning it does not cause prohibition because it is not truly milk. Indeed, milk can only be conceived from one who can give birth; thus it is like a young girl who has not reached nine years, as we mentioned. If milk descends for a hermaphrodite, if it is known that the person is a woman, prohibition attaches; if it is known that it is a man, no prohibition attaches; if it is ambiguous, if women say that such abundance only occurs in a woman, prohibition attaches as a precaution; otherwise it does not. Thus in al-Jawhara.
And it is the instrument of enema. His statement: (haqana kardan) meaning 'he performed the enema'; kardan is an infinitive: past tense kard, present tense kunad, active participle kunanda, passive participle karde; thus the first means 'he did', the second 'he does', the third 'doer', the fourth 'done'. And kardan means 'to do'; hence haqana kardan means 'to perform the enema' because the possessive construction in Persian is inverted. Thus informed by someone knowledgeable. His statement: (In Fath al-Qadir: 'this is a mistake, etc.') He said in al-Nahr: You are aware that this only holds if the reading was muhqana kardan and that was the version in his copy; however, if it was haqana kardan as mentioned, i.e., 'he performed the enema', then regarding its being a mistake there is consideration. So reflect. End. And there is consideration in it, because interpreting ihtiqan as 'performing an enema' does not necessitate making it transitive to a direct object, just as if one interpreted al-ightisal as 'performing a bath' (ghusl).
His statement: (And the sheep) meaning the milk of a sheep does not cause prohibition. So if a boy and a girl nurse on the milk of a sheep, there is no siblinghood between them because motherhood is not established by it, as it has no prohibition, and because the milk of animals has the ruling of food; thus there is no difference between a sheep and other non-human animals. He restricted to three because al-wajur (oral feeding) and al-sa'ut (nasal feeding) establish prohibition by consensus. Fasting is only invalidated by what was mentioned except instillation into the urethra, because breaking the fast is related to reaching the interior. Al-wajur (with fath of waw) is medicine poured into the throat; it is also said awjartuhu and wajartuhu. Al-sa'ut is pouring it into the nose. In al-Misbah: Al-sa'ut (like rasul) is medicine poured into the nose; al-sa'ut (like qu'ud) is the verbal noun. I administered it nasally (as'atuhu al-dawa') is transitive to two objects, and Zaid received it nasally (ista'ata). Al-mis'at (with damm on the mim) is the vessel in which the nasal medicine is placed; it is among the rare forms that occur with damm, while by analogy it should be kasr because it is a noun of instrument. It was given damm to match prevalent forms like fu'lul; if it were kasr, it would lead to a missing pattern, since there is no mif'il or fi'lil with kasr on the first and damm on the third. End. It has been narrated in al-Mabsut and al-Kashf al-Kabir that al-Bukhari, the hadith scholar, entered Bukhara and began issuing fatwas. Abu Hafs al-Kabir said to him: 'Do not do it.' He refused to accept his advice until he was asked for a fatwa on this issue; he ruled that fosterage prohibition is established between a boy and a girl who nursed from the udder of a sheep, clinging to the Prophet's statement, 'Any two infants who share the same breast become forbidden to each other.' But he was mistaken due to lack of insight, as he did not consider that the ruling is attached to partiality and particularity; so they expelled him from Bukhara. In Fath al-Qadir after this story: He who does not examine carefully the legal bases and their rulings will make many mistakes. That was in the time of Shaykh Abu Hafs al-Kabir; his birth was the same as al-Shafi'i's, for they were both born in the same year that Abu Hanifa died, which is 150 AH. End.
His statement: (And if she breastfeeds her co-wife, both become forbidden) i.e., if the elder (wife) breastfeeds the young one who is the wife of her husband, both become forbidden to the husband because he becomes a man combining between mother and daughter by fosterage. Thus his marriage to both becomes invalid (fasad), but not annulled, because the position of our scholars is that marriage is not lifted by the prohibition of fosterage or marriage affinity; rather, it becomes invalid. Thus if he had intercourse with her before separation, no hadd is required of him, whether the matter was ambiguous or not. Muhammad stated this in al-Asl, and the commentator mentioned it in the chapter of li'an. Accordingly, the statement in al-Mi'raj that 'the marriage is annulled' does not contradict it because annulment is different from invalidity. In al-Bazzaziyya: By the establishment of prohibition of affinity and prohibition of fosterage, the marriage is not lifted, so the woman does not have the right to marry another husband except after mutual separation, even if years have passed. End. And we previously stated that for an invalid marriage, separation by a judge or verbal separation is necessary in the case of a consummated marriage; in other cases, physical separation suffices. And invalidity in the case of supervening fosterage should be such. As for if a man marries a woman and then his other wife or a stranger breastfeeds her, the marriage becomes invalid in the more correct view. He restricted to three, i.e., enema, milk of a man, and milk of a sheep; he should have mentioned it at the statement 'la al-ihtiqan' and said 'restricted to three' etc., since there is no entry in that for milk of a man and sheep, for there is no difference between drinking, oral feeding, and nasal feeding regarding them. So consider. His statement: (Thus his statement in al-Mi'raj that 'the marriage is annulled' does not contradict it) is in most copies; in some it is 'contradicts it' without 'la', and that is evidently correct based on the reasoning. His statement: (As for if a man marries a woman, etc.) Al-Ramli said: It will come at the end of the chapter.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn from Kanz al-Daqaiq covering several rulings regarding fosterage (rada'). The author, Ibn Nujaym (or his supervisor al-Haskafi? Actually al-Bahr al-Raiq is by Ibn Nujaym), explains that three things do NOT establish fosterage prohibition: (1) enema with milk (ihtiqan bil-laban), (2) milk of a man, and (3) milk of a sheep (or any animal). The commentary first clarifies that enema with milk does not cause prohibition because it is not a means of nourishment; similarly, instilling milk into the urethra, ear, or wounds does not create fosterage. The text includes a linguistic discussion about the correct usage of the verb 'ihtaqana' and whether it can be used transitively. The author favors the passive construction common among jurists.

Next, the ruling on a man's milk: since a man does not normally lactate, his milk is not considered true milk for fosterage purposes. If a hermaphrodite lactates, the ruling depends on whether the person is determined to be male or female; if unknown, precaution may establish prohibition if women confirm the abundance is only from a woman.

Then, animal milk: the milk of a sheep or any non-human animal does not establish fosterage. The author recounts a story about Imam al-Bukhari (the hadith scholar) who mistakenly ruled that two infants who nursed from a sheep's udder become foster-siblings, based on a hadith. He was corrected by Abu Hafs al-Kabir and expelled from Bukhara. The correct understanding is that the hadith's 'breast' (thady) means a woman's breast, not an animal's udder, and the fosterage relationship requires the milk to be from a human female.

The passage then discusses the case where a wife breastfeeds her husband's other wife (co-wife). In this scenario, the breastfeeding wife becomes the mother of the co-wife by fosterage, and both women become permanently forbidden to the husband, as he would be marrying a mother and her daughter. However, the marriage is not automatically annulled (it becomes invalid/fasid), requiring separation by a judge or mutual separation. This is an important distinction in Hanafi fiqh: the marriage is not lifted automatically but must be terminated.

The commentary also addresses the question of mahr: if the elder wife breastfeeds the younger without the latter's permission, the younger is not entitled to mahr from the husband because the marriage was invalid from the start due to the fosterage relationship. The text ends with a note that the ruling on a man marrying a woman and then having her breastfed by another wife will be discussed at the end of the chapter.

Key Terms
الرضاع (al-rada'): Fosterage or milk kinship; the legal relationship established when an infant consumes the milk of a woman, creating certain prohibitions analogous to blood relations.
الاحتقان (al-ihtiqan): Administering an enema; in this context, pouring milk into the anus for medicinal purposes, which does not establish fosterage.
الثدي (al-thady): Breast; refers specifically to the human female breast in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does enema with milk not create fosterage?
A) Because enema is disliked.
B) Because it is not a means of nourishment.
C) Because the milk is mixed with impurities.
D) Because the child is not conscious.

Key Takeaway
Fosterage requires human milk consumed orally; enema, male milk, and animal milk do not establish prohibition.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Fosterage Between Co-Wives: Prohibition and Legal Consequences
Ruling on co-wife breastfeeding and its consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling when a wife breastfeeds her co-wife, including the consequences regarding marriage validity and mahr.

Core Idea
If a wife breastfeeds her husband's other wife, both wives become forbidden to the husband, but the marriage is invalid (fasid), not automatically annulled.

A unique scenario in fosterage law is when one wife breastfeeds her co-wife. This creates a relationship of mother and daughter by fosterage, making both women permanently forbidden to the husband. However, the Hanafi school distinguishes between invalidity (fasad) and annulment, requiring a formal separation. This lesson examines the ruling and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
An elder wife breastfeeds a younger co-wife. Note that the breastfeeding must meet the conditions of fosterage (human milk, oral consumption, etc.).
2
Determine the prohibition
Both wives become forbidden to the husband because he is marrying a mother and her daughter by fosterage.
3
Assess marriage validity
The marriage becomes fasid (invalid), not automatically annulled. This is the Hanafi position.
Annulment would mean the marriage never existed; fasid means it is flawed but requires separation.
4
Understand consequence for mahr
If the younger wife was breastfed without her permission, no mahr is due because the marriage was invalid from the start.
5
Note the need for separation
A formal separation (mutaraka) is required to end the marriage; it is not automatically lifted.

Source Text

كتاب الرضاع
لا الاحتقان ولبن الرجل والشاة ولو أرضعت ضرتها حرمتا ولا مهر للكبيرة إن لم تكن أرضعتها بإذنها لأنها أم امرأته، ولا يجوز الجمع بين هذه الرضيعة وبنت الميتة لأنهما أختان. وفي فتح القدير: لبن الميتة طاهر عند أبي حنيفة لأن التنجس بالموت لما حلته الحياة قبله وهو منتف في اللبن، وهما وإن قالا بنجاسته للمجاورة للوعاء النجس لا يمنع من الحرمة كما لو حلب في إناء نجس وأوجر به صبي تثبت. وهذا بخلاف وطء الميتة فإنه لا يتعلق به حرمة المصاهرة بالإجماع. والفرق أن المقصود من اللبن التغدي والموت لا يمنع منه، والمقصود من الوطء اللذة المعتادة وذلك لا يوجد في وطء الميتة. كذا في الجوهرة.
قوله: (لا الاحتقان) أي الاحتقان باللبن لا يوجب الحرمة لأنه ليس مما يتغذى به ولذا لا يثبت بالإقطار في الإحليل والأذن والجائفة والآمة. قال في المغرب: الصواب حقن إذا عولج بالحقنة واحتقن بالضم غير جائز. وفي تاج المصادر الاحتقان حقنه کردن فجعله متعدياً فعلى هذا يجوز استعماله على بناء المفعول وهو الأكثر في استعمال الفقهاء. كذا في المعراج والنهاية. وفي فتح القدير: وهذا غلط لأن ما في تاج المصادر من التفسير لا يفيد تعدية الافتعال منه للمفعول الصريح كالصبي في عبارة الهداية حيث قال: إذا احتقن الصبي بل إلى الحقنة والكلام في بنائه للمفعول الذي هو الصبي ومعلوم أن كل قاصر يجوز بناؤه للمفعول بالنسبة إلى المجرور والظرف كجلس في الدار ومر بزيد وليس يلزم من جواز البناء باعتبار الآلة والظرف جوازه بالنسبة إلى المفعول بل إذا كان متعدياً إليه بنفسه ا هـ. وفي المصباح: حقنت المريض إذا وصلت الدواء إلى باطنه من مخرجه بالمحقنة واحتقن هو والاسم الحقنة مثل الغرفة من الاغتراف ثم أطلقت على ما يتداوى به والجمع حقن مثل غرفة وغرف ا هـ.
قوله: (ولبن الرجل) أي لا يوجب الحرمة لأنه ليس بلبن على الحقيقة لأن اللبن إنما يتصور ممن تتصور منه الولادة فصار كالصغيرة التي لم تبلغ تسع سنين كما قدمناه. وإذا نزل للخنثى لبن إن علم أن امرأة تعلق به التحريم وإن علم أنه رجل لم يتعلق به تحريم، وإن أشكل إن قال النساء إنه لا يكون على غزارته إلا للمرأة تعلق به التحريم احتياطاً، وإن لم يقلن ذلك لم يتعلق به تحريم. كذا في الجوهرة.
وهي آلة الاحتقان، قوله: (حقنه كردن) أي فعل الحقنة فكردن مصدر ماضیه کرد و مضارعه کند و اسم فاعله کرده واسم المفعول كننده، فالأول بمعنى فعل والثاني بمعنى يفعل والثالث بمعنى فاعل، والرابع بمعنى مفعول و كردن بمعنی فعلاً فحقنه کردن بمعنى فعل الحقنة لأن الإضافة في اللغة الفارسية مقلوبة. كذا أفادنيه بعض من له خبرة بها. قوله: (وفي فتح القدير وهذا غلط الخ) قال في النهر: أنت خبير بأن هذا إنما يتم ا أن لو كانت الرواية محقنة كردن وكان هذا هو الواقع في نسخته، أما إذا كانت حقنه كردن كما مر أي فعل الحقنة ففي كونه غلطاً نظر فتدبر ا.هـ. وفيه نطر إذ لا يلزم من تفسير الاحتقان بفعل الحقنة تعديته للمفعول الصريح كما لو فسرت الاغتسال بفعل الغسل.
قوله: (والشاة) أي لبن الشاة لا يوجب الحرمة حتى لو ارتضع صبي وصبية على لبن شاة فلا أخوة بينهما لأن الأمومة لا تثبت به لأنه لا حرمة له ولأن لبن البهائم له حكم الطعام فلا فرق بين الشاة وغيرها من غير الآدمي. قيد بالثلاثة لأن الوجور والسعوط تثبت به الحرمة اتفاقاً. وإنما يفسد الصوم بما ذكر ما عدا الإقطار في الإحليل لأن الفطر يتعلق بالوصول إلى الجوف. والوجور بفتح الواو والدواء يصب في الحلق ويقال أوجرته ووجرته، والسعوط صبه في الأنف. وفي المصباح: والسعوط مثال رسول دواء يصب في الأنف، والسعوط مثل قعود مصدر، وأسعطه الدواء يتعدى إلى مفعولين واستعط زيد والمسعط بضم الميم الوعاء يجعل فيه السعوط وهو من النوادر التي جاءت بالضم وقياسها الكسر لأنه اسم آلة. وإنما ضمت الميم ليوافق الأبنية الغالبة مثل «فعلل» ولو كسرت أدى إلى بناء مفقود إذ ليس في الكلام مفعل ولا فعلل بكسر الأول وضم الثالث ا هـ. وقد حكي في المبسوط والكشف الكبير أن البخاري صاحب الأخبار دخل بخارى وجعل يفتي فقال له أبو حفص الكبير: لا تفعل فأبى أن يقبل نصيحته حتى استفتى في هذه المسئلة فأفتى بثبوت الحرمة بين صبيين ارتضعا من ثدي لبن شاة تمسكاً بقوله عليه السلام «كل صبيين اجتمعا على ثدي واحد حرم الآخر» وقد أخطأ لفوات الرأي وهو أنه لم يتأمل أن الحكم متعلق بالجزئية والبعضية فأخرجوه من بخارى. وفي فتح القدير بعد هذه الحكاية: ومن لم يدق نظره في مناط الأحكام وحكمها كثر خطؤه وكان ذلك في زمن الشيخ أبي حفص الكبير ومولده مولد الشافعي فإنهما ولدا معاً في العام الذي توفي فيه أبو حنيفة وهو سنة خمسين ومائة ا هـ.
قوله: (ولو أرضعت ضرتها حرمتا) أي لو أرضعت الكبيرة الصغيرة التي هي زوجة زوجها حرمتا على الزوج لأنه يصير جامعاً بين الأم والبنت رضاعاً ففسد نكاحهما، ولم ينفسخ لأن المذهب عند علمائنا أن النكاح لا يرتفع بحرمة الرضاع والمصاهرة بل يفسد حتى لو وطئها قبل التفريق لا يجب عليه الحد، اشتبه الأمر أو لم يشتبه. نص عليه محمد في الأصل، وذكره الشارح في باب اللعان. وعلى هذا فقوله في المعراج فينفسخ النكاح لا يخالفه لأن الانفساخ غيره. وفي البزازية: وبثبوت حرمة المصاهرة وحرمة الرضاع لا يرتفع بهما النكاح حتى لا تملك المرأة التزوج بزوج آخر إلا بعد المتاركة وإن مضى عليه سنون ا هـ. وقدمنا أنه لا بد في الفاسد من تفريق القاضي أو المتاركة بالقول في المدخولة وفي غيرها يكتفى بالمفارقة بالأبدان. وينبغي أن يكون الفساد في الرضاع الطارئ على النكاح، أما لو تزوج امرأة ثم أرضعتها زوجته الأخرى أو أجنبية فسد النكاح في الأصح. قيد بالثلاثة أي بالاحتقان ولبن الرجل والشاة وكان عليه أن يذكره عند قوله «لا الاحتقان» فيقول قيد به الخ إذ لا مدخل في ذلك اللبن الرجل والشاة فإنه لا فرق فيه بين الشرب والوجور والسعوط تأمل. قوله: (فقوله في المعراج فينفسخ النكاح لا يخالفه) كذا في أغلب النسخ، وفي بعضها يخالفه بدون «لا» وهو الظاهر بدليل التعليل. قوله: (أما لو تزوج امرأة الخ) قال الرملي: سيأتي آخر الباب.
Chapter of Fosterage
Enema with milk, and milk of a man and a sheep do not cause prohibition. If a woman breastfed her co-wife, both become forbidden (to the husband), and there is no mahr for the elder if she did not breastfeed with her permission, because she is the mother of his wife. And it is not permissible to combine this foster daughter with the daughter of the deceased because they are sisters. In Fath al-Qadir: The milk of a deceased woman is pure according to Abu Hanifa because impurity through death applies to what life had entered, and it is absent in milk. The two (companions) say it is impure due to proximity to an impure container, but that does not prevent prohibition (of fosterage), as if it were milked into an impure vessel and then fed to an infant, it establishes (fosterage). This is unlike intercourse with a dead woman, because by consensus it does not establish a marriage prohibition. The difference is that the purpose of milk is nourishment, and death does not prevent that, while the purpose of intercourse is customary pleasure, and that is not found in intercourse with a dead woman. Thus in al-Jawhara.
His statement: (Enema with milk) meaning enema with milk does not cause prohibition because it is not something that nourishes; therefore it is not established by instillation into the urethra, ear, perforated wound, or head wound. He said in al-Mughrib: The correct form is haqana (to treat with an enema) and ihtiqan (to receive an enema) with a damma (u) is not permissible. In Taj al-Masadir, al-ihtiqan means 'he performed an enema' (haqana kardan), making it transitive; accordingly, it is permissible to use it in the passive form, which is the prevalent usage among jurists. Thus in al-Mi'raj and al-Nihaya. In Fath al-Qadir: This is a mistake because the interpretation in Taj al-Masadir does not make the verbal noun (ifti'al) transitive to a direct object like 'the boy' in the statement of al-Hidayah: 'when the boy receives an enema' (ihtaqana al-sabi). Rather, the discussion is about its passive construction referring to the boy, and it is known that every intransitive verb can be built in the passive form relative to a prepositional phrase or adverb, as in 'he sat in the house' and 'he passed by Zaid'. And it does not necessarily follow that the permissibility of passive construction with respect to instrument and circumstance implies permissibility with respect to a direct object; rather, (only) if it is directly transitive. End. In al-Misbah: I gave an enema to the patient (haqantu al-marida) when I delivered medicine into his interior through his outlet using an enema, and he received an enema (ihtaqana). The noun is al-huqna (enema) like al-ghurfa from al-ightiraf. Then it was used for what is treated with, and the plural is huaqan like ghuraf and ghuraf. End.
His statement: (And milk of a man) meaning it does not cause prohibition because it is not truly milk. Indeed, milk can only be conceived from one who can give birth; thus it is like a young girl who has not reached nine years, as we mentioned. If milk descends for a hermaphrodite, if it is known that the person is a woman, prohibition attaches; if it is known that it is a man, no prohibition attaches; if it is ambiguous, if women say that such abundance only occurs in a woman, prohibition attaches as a precaution; otherwise it does not. Thus in al-Jawhara.
And it is the instrument of enema. His statement: (haqana kardan) meaning 'he performed the enema'; kardan is an infinitive: past tense kard, present tense kunad, active participle kunanda, passive participle karde; thus the first means 'he did', the second 'he does', the third 'doer', the fourth 'done'. And kardan means 'to do'; hence haqana kardan means 'to perform the enema' because the possessive construction in Persian is inverted. Thus informed by someone knowledgeable. His statement: (In Fath al-Qadir: 'this is a mistake, etc.') He said in al-Nahr: You are aware that this only holds if the reading was muhqana kardan and that was the version in his copy; however, if it was haqana kardan as mentioned, i.e., 'he performed the enema', then regarding its being a mistake there is consideration. So reflect. End. And there is consideration in it, because interpreting ihtiqan as 'performing an enema' does not necessitate making it transitive to a direct object, just as if one interpreted al-ightisal as 'performing a bath' (ghusl).
His statement: (And the sheep) meaning the milk of a sheep does not cause prohibition. So if a boy and a girl nurse on the milk of a sheep, there is no siblinghood between them because motherhood is not established by it, as it has no prohibition, and because the milk of animals has the ruling of food; thus there is no difference between a sheep and other non-human animals. He restricted to three because al-wajur (oral feeding) and al-sa'ut (nasal feeding) establish prohibition by consensus. Fasting is only invalidated by what was mentioned except instillation into the urethra, because breaking the fast is related to reaching the interior. Al-wajur (with fath of waw) is medicine poured into the throat; it is also said awjartuhu and wajartuhu. Al-sa'ut is pouring it into the nose. In al-Misbah: Al-sa'ut (like rasul) is medicine poured into the nose; al-sa'ut (like qu'ud) is the verbal noun. I administered it nasally (as'atuhu al-dawa') is transitive to two objects, and Zaid received it nasally (ista'ata). Al-mis'at (with damm on the mim) is the vessel in which the nasal medicine is placed; it is among the rare forms that occur with damm, while by analogy it should be kasr because it is a noun of instrument. It was given damm to match prevalent forms like fu'lul; if it were kasr, it would lead to a missing pattern, since there is no mif'il or fi'lil with kasr on the first and damm on the third. End. It has been narrated in al-Mabsut and al-Kashf al-Kabir that al-Bukhari, the hadith scholar, entered Bukhara and began issuing fatwas. Abu Hafs al-Kabir said to him: 'Do not do it.' He refused to accept his advice until he was asked for a fatwa on this issue; he ruled that fosterage prohibition is established between a boy and a girl who nursed from the udder of a sheep, clinging to the Prophet's statement, 'Any two infants who share the same breast become forbidden to each other.' But he was mistaken due to lack of insight, as he did not consider that the ruling is attached to partiality and particularity; so they expelled him from Bukhara. In Fath al-Qadir after this story: He who does not examine carefully the legal bases and their rulings will make many mistakes. That was in the time of Shaykh Abu Hafs al-Kabir; his birth was the same as al-Shafi'i's, for they were both born in the same year that Abu Hanifa died, which is 150 AH. End.
His statement: (And if she breastfeeds her co-wife, both become forbidden) i.e., if the elder (wife) breastfeeds the young one who is the wife of her husband, both become forbidden to the husband because he becomes a man combining between mother and daughter by fosterage. Thus his marriage to both becomes invalid (fasad), but not annulled, because the position of our scholars is that marriage is not lifted by the prohibition of fosterage or marriage affinity; rather, it becomes invalid. Thus if he had intercourse with her before separation, no hadd is required of him, whether the matter was ambiguous or not. Muhammad stated this in al-Asl, and the commentator mentioned it in the chapter of li'an. Accordingly, the statement in al-Mi'raj that 'the marriage is annulled' does not contradict it because annulment is different from invalidity. In al-Bazzaziyya: By the establishment of prohibition of affinity and prohibition of fosterage, the marriage is not lifted, so the woman does not have the right to marry another husband except after mutual separation, even if years have passed. End. And we previously stated that for an invalid marriage, separation by a judge or verbal separation is necessary in the case of a consummated marriage; in other cases, physical separation suffices. And invalidity in the case of supervening fosterage should be such. As for if a man marries a woman and then his other wife or a stranger breastfeeds her, the marriage becomes invalid in the more correct view. He restricted to three, i.e., enema, milk of a man, and milk of a sheep; he should have mentioned it at the statement 'la al-ihtiqan' and said 'restricted to three' etc., since there is no entry in that for milk of a man and sheep, for there is no difference between drinking, oral feeding, and nasal feeding regarding them. So consider. His statement: (Thus his statement in al-Mi'raj that 'the marriage is annulled' does not contradict it) is in most copies; in some it is 'contradicts it' without 'la', and that is evidently correct based on the reasoning. His statement: (As for if a man marries a woman, etc.) Al-Ramli said: It will come at the end of the chapter.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn from Kanz al-Daqaiq covering several rulings regarding fosterage (rada'). The author, Ibn Nujaym (or his supervisor al-Haskafi? Actually al-Bahr al-Raiq is by Ibn Nujaym), explains that three things do NOT establish fosterage prohibition: (1) enema with milk (ihtiqan bil-laban), (2) milk of a man, and (3) milk of a sheep (or any animal). The commentary first clarifies that enema with milk does not cause prohibition because it is not a means of nourishment; similarly, instilling milk into the urethra, ear, or wounds does not create fosterage. The text includes a linguistic discussion about the correct usage of the verb 'ihtaqana' and whether it can be used transitively. The author favors the passive construction common among jurists.

Next, the ruling on a man's milk: since a man does not normally lactate, his milk is not considered true milk for fosterage purposes. If a hermaphrodite lactates, the ruling depends on whether the person is determined to be male or female; if unknown, precaution may establish prohibition if women confirm the abundance is only from a woman.

Then, animal milk: the milk of a sheep or any non-human animal does not establish fosterage. The author recounts a story about Imam al-Bukhari (the hadith scholar) who mistakenly ruled that two infants who nursed from a sheep's udder become foster-siblings, based on a hadith. He was corrected by Abu Hafs al-Kabir and expelled from Bukhara. The correct understanding is that the hadith's 'breast' (thady) means a woman's breast, not an animal's udder, and the fosterage relationship requires the milk to be from a human female.

The passage then discusses the case where a wife breastfeeds her husband's other wife (co-wife). In this scenario, the breastfeeding wife becomes the mother of the co-wife by fosterage, and both women become permanently forbidden to the husband, as he would be marrying a mother and her daughter. However, the marriage is not automatically annulled (it becomes invalid/fasid), requiring separation by a judge or mutual separation. This is an important distinction in Hanafi fiqh: the marriage is not lifted automatically but must be terminated.

The commentary also addresses the question of mahr: if the elder wife breastfeeds the younger without the latter's permission, the younger is not entitled to mahr from the husband because the marriage was invalid from the start due to the fosterage relationship. The text ends with a note that the ruling on a man marrying a woman and then having her breastfed by another wife will be discussed at the end of the chapter.

Key Terms
الضرة (al-durra): Co-wife; a woman who is a wife of the same husband as another woman.
المتاركة (al-mutaraka): Mutual separation; the formal cessation of a marital relationship, either by a judge's decree or by verbal agreement.
فساد (fasad): Invalidity; a contract that is flawed but not void ab initio. In marriage, it does not automatically dissolve the marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a wife breastfeeds her co-wife, what is the status of the husband's marriage to both wives?
A) The marriages are automatically annulled.
B) The marriages become invalid (fasid) but require separation.
C) Only the younger wife's marriage becomes invalid.
D) The marriages remain valid because fosterage does not affect existing marriages.

Key Takeaway
Co-wife breastfeeding makes both wives forbidden, but the marriage becomes fasid, not annulled; formal separation is required.

Sheep's Milk Does Not Create Fosterage: Ruling and Reasoning
Explanation of a ruling with reasoning and a cautionary anecdote

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sheep's milk and fosterage, explain why animal milk does not create mahram relationships, and identify the correct legal cause for fosterage.

Core Idea
Only human milk establishes fosterage; animal milk is food, not a source of mahram bonds.

This lesson examines a specific ruling: if a boy and a girl drink from the same sheep's milk, they do not become foster siblings. We will explore the reasoning behind this, the definitions of related terms like 'wajur' and 'sa'ut', and a historical incident where Imam al-Bukhari erred in this issue. Understanding the precise legal cause is crucial to avoid similar mistakes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is infants drinking sheep's milk. The ruling is that no fosterage (and thus no mahram relationship) is established.
2
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
Animal milk is treated as food, not as a substance that creates motherhood. Fosterage requires human milk because it is the basis for the maternal bond.
3
Note the exceptions: wajur and sa'ut
If milk is administered via the throat (wajur) or nose (sa'ut), it does establish fosterage by agreement, because it reaches the stomach like suckling.
These methods are equivalent to suckling in delivering milk to the child's body.
4
Analyze the story of Imam al-Bukhari
Al-Bukhari mistakenly ruled that two infants suckling from the same sheep become foster siblings, clinging to a hadith about 'two infants on one breast.' He failed to realize the ruling is tied to partiality and part-whole relationship (i.e., the milk must be a part of a human female).
This story warns against superficial reasoning without understanding the precise legal cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والشاة) أي لبن الشاة لا يوجب الحرمة حتى لو ارتضع صبي وصبية على لبن شاة فلا أخوة بينهما لأن الأمومة لا تثبت به لأنه لا حرمة له ولأن لبن البهائم له حكم الطعام فلا فرق بين الشاة وغيرها من غير الآدمي. قيد بالثلاثة لأن الوجور والسعوط تثبت به الحرمة اتفاقاً . وإنما يفسد الصوم بما ذكر ما عدا الإقطار في الإحليل لأن الفطر يتعلق بالوصول إلى الجوف . والوجور بفتح الواو والدواء يصب في الحلق ويقال أو جرته ووجرته، والسعوط صبه في الأنف. وفي المصباح : والسعوط مثال رسول دواء يصب في الأنف، والسعوط مثل قعود مصدر، وأسعطه الدواء يتعدى إلى مفعولين واستعط زيد والمسعط بضم الميم الوعاء يجعل فيه السعوط وهو من النوادر التي جاءت بالضم وقياسها الكسر لأنه اسم آلة. وإنما ضمت الميم ليوافق الأبنية الغالبة مثل «فعلل» ولو كسرت أدى إلى بناء مفقود إذ ليس في الكلام مفعل ولا فعلل بكسر الأول وضم الثالث ا هـ. وقد حكي في المبسوط والكشف الكبير أن البخاري صاحب الأخبار دخل بخارى وجعل يفتي فقال له أبو حفص الكبير : لا تفعل فأبى أن يقبل نصيحته حتى استفتى في هذه المسئلة فأفتى بثبوت الحرمة بين صبيين ارتضعا من ثدي لبن شاة تمسكاً بقوله عليه السلام كل صبيين اجتمعا على ثدي واحد حرم الآخر» وقد أخطأ لفوات الرأي وهو أنه لم يتأمل أن الحكم متعلق بالجزئية والبعضية فأخرجوه من بخارى . وفي فتح القدير. بعد هذه الحكاية ومن لم يدق نظره في مناط الأحكام وحكمها كثر خطؤه وكان ذلك في زمن الشيخ أبي حفص الكبير ومولده مولد الشافعي فإنهما ولدا معاً في العام الذي توفي فيه أبو حنيفة وهو سنة خمسين ومائة ا هـ
He said: (And the sheep) meaning the milk of a sheep does not cause prohibition, for if a boy and a girl suckle on the milk of a sheep, there is no siblinghood between them because motherhood is not established by it, since it has no sanctity, and because the milk of animals has the ruling of food, so there is no difference between a sheep and other non-human animals. He restricted it to three because the wajur and sa'ut establish prohibition by agreement. And fasting is only broken by what was mentioned except for the enema in the urethra because breaking the fast is related to reaching the interior. Wajur (with fatha on waw) is medicine poured into the throat, and it is said 'awjartuhu' and 'wajartuhu'. Sa'ut is pouring it into the nose. In al-Misbah: 'Sa'ut (like rasul) is medicine poured into the nose; the masdar is su'ut (like qu'ud). As'atuhu al-dawa' is transitive to two objects; ista'ata Zayd. The mis'at (with damm on mim) is the vessel containing sa'ut, and it is from the rare words that come with damm, while its analogy is kasr because it is an instrument noun. The mim is given damm to match predominant patterns like fu'lul; if it were kasr, it would lead to a missing pattern, as there is no maf'al or fa'lul with kasr of the first and damm of the third, end quote. It has been narrated in al-Mabsut and al-Kashf al-Kabir that al-Bukhari, the hadith scholar, entered Bukhara and began giving fatwas. Abu Hafs al-Kabir told him: 'Do not do so,' but he refused his advice until he was asked about this issue, and he gave a fatwa that prohibition is established between two infants who suckled from a sheep's breast, clinging to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Any two infants who unite upon one breast are prohibited to one another.' But he erred by missing the insight, namely that he did not reflect that the ruling is attached to partiality and part-whole relationship, so they expelled him from Bukhara. And in Fath al-Qadir: After this story, 'Whoever does not examine precisely the loci of rulings and their wisdom will err frequently.' This was in the time of Shaykh Abu Hafs al-Kabir, whose birth was the same as al-Shafi'i's; they were both born in the year Abu Hanifa died, which is 150 AH. End quote.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a line from the matn regarding sheep's milk. It states that sheep's milk does not establish fosterage because fosterage requires a human relationship of motherhood, which is not established with animal milk. Animal milk is treated like food. The passage then defines the terms 'wajur' and 'sa'ut', which are methods of administering medicine that, if used to feed milk, still establish fosterage by agreement. Finally, it relates a story about Imam al-Bukhari who mistakenly ruled that two infants suckling from the same sheep's breast become foster siblings, and he was criticized for failing to consider the precise legal cause (al-juz'iyya wa al-ba'diyya). This story serves as a warning against superficial reasoning in fiqh.

Key Terms
الوجور (al-wajur): Medicine poured into the throat.
السعوط (al-sa'ut): Medicine poured into the nose.
البخاري (al-Bukhari): The hadith scholar and author of Sahih al-Bukhari.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why does sheep's milk not establish fosterage?
A) Because sheep's milk is impure
B) Because the hadith about fosterage only applies to human milk
C) Because animal milk is treated as food and does not create motherhood
D) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly excluded sheep's milk

Key Takeaway
Only human milk establishes fosterage; animal milk is simply food and does not create mahram bonds.

Ruling When a Wife Breastfeeds Her Co-Wife: Both Become Forbidden
Ruling with proof from Imam Muhammad's al-Asl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a wife breastfeeds her co-wife, explain why the marriage becomes fasid (invalid) rather than annulled, and apply the distinction to similar scenarios.

Core Idea
Fosterage between co-wives forbids both to the husband, but the marriage is only invalidated (fasid), not annulled.

The marriage contract is sacred, but certain prohibitions can render it defective. In Hanafi fiqh, when a wife breastfeeds her co-wife, a foster mother-daughter relationship is established, making it impermissible for the husband to be married to both simultaneously. This lesson clarifies that the marriage becomes fasid (invalid) and requires formal separation, but it is not automatically annulled (infisakh) as in the case of lineage-related prohibitions. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct application of marriage and divorce rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A wife (kabira) breastfeeds the other wife (saghira) of the same husband. Recognize that this creates a foster mother-daughter relationship.
The breastfeeding must be within the accepted conditions (e.g., before two years, sufficient milk).
2
Determine the legal consequence
Both wives become forbidden (haram) to the husband because he would be simultaneously married to a mother and her daughter through fosterage.
This prohibition is based on the Qur'anic verse that forbids marrying foster mothers and daughters.
3
Classify the marriage status as fasid, not infisakh
The marriage becomes invalid (fasada) but is not automatically annulled (lam yanfasikh). In Hanafi law, fosterage does not terminate the marriage contract; it only makes it defective, requiring a separation process.
Fasid means the contract is valid in origin but defective due to a prohibition. Infisakh means complete termination without need for divorce.
4
Note additional rulings
If the husband has intercourse before separation, no hadd punishment is due. The woman cannot remarry until a mutual parting (mutaraka) is agreed upon, even if years pass.
In a consummated fasid marriage, separation requires a judge's ruling or verbal mutaraka. In non-consummated, physical parting suffices.
5
Distinguish from similar cases
Contrast with a case where the wife is proven to be the husband's sister by lineage: there, the marriage is completely annulled, hadd applies, and she may remarry after idda without mutaraka.
The restriction 'if she breastfeeds her co-wife' is not exclusive; similar prohibitions apply to other combinations of relatives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ولو أرضعت ضرتها حرمتا) أي لو أرضعت الكبيرة الصغيرة التي هي زوجة زوجها حرمتا على الزوج لأنه يصير جامعاً بين الأم والبنت رضاعاً ففسد نكاحهما ، ولم ينفسخ لأن المذهب عند علمائنا أن النكاح لا يرتفع بحرمة الرضاع والمصاهرة بل يفسد حتى لو وطئها قبل التفريق لا يجب عليه الحد، اشتبه الأمر أو لم يشتبه . نص عليه محمد في الأصل، وذكره الشارح في باب اللعان. وعلى هذا فقوله في المعراج فينفسخ النكاح لا يخالفه لأن الانفساخ غيره. وفي البزازية وبثبوت حرمة المصاهرة وحرمة الرضاع لا يرتفع بهما النكاح حتى لا تملك المرأة التزوج بزوج آخر إلا بعد المتاركة وإن مضى عليه سنون ا هـ . وقدمنا أنه لا بد في الفاسد من تفريق القاضي أو المتاركة بالقول في المدحولة وفي غيرها يكتفى بالمفارقة بالأبدان. وينبغي أن يكون الفساد في الرضاع الطارئ على النكاح، أما لو تزوج امرأة فشهد عدلان أنها أخته ارتفع النكاح بالكلية حتى لو وطئها يحد ويجوز لها التزوج بعد العدة من غير متاركة والتقييد بأنها أرضعت ضرتها ليس احترازياً لأن أخت الكبيرة وأمها وبنتها نسباً ورضاعاً إن دخل بالكبيرة كهي للزوم الجمع بين المرأة وبنت أختها في الأول. وبين الأختين في الثاني، وبين المرأة وبنت بنتها في الثالث، وليس له أن يتزوج بواحدة منهما قط ولا المرضعة أيضاً، وإن لم يكن دخل بالكبيرة في الثالثة فإن المرضعة لا تحل له قط لكونها أم امرأته، ولا الكبيرة لكونها أم أم امرأته وتحل الصغيرة لكونها ابنة بنت امرأته ولم يدخل بها.
He said: (And if she breastfeeds her co-wife, both become forbidden) Meaning if the large wife breastfeeds the small wife who is the wife of her husband, both become forbidden to the husband because he becomes a gatherer between the mother and daughter through fosterage, so their marriage becomes invalid (fasada), but it is not annulled (lam yanfasikh) because the madhhab of our scholars is that marriage is not terminated by the prohibition of fosterage or in-law relationship, but rather becomes invalid. So even if he has intercourse with her before separation, the hadd punishment is not obligatory upon him, whether the matter is clear or ambiguous. This was explicitly stated by Muhammad in al-Asl, and the commentator mentioned it in the chapter of li'an. According to this, his statement in al-Mi'raj that 'the marriage annuls' does not contradict it because 'annulment' is other than this. In al-Bazzaziyya: 'With the establishment of in-law prohibition and fosterage prohibition, marriage is not terminated by them, so the woman does not have the right to marry another husband except after mutaraka, even if years pass.' End quote. And we have already stated that in an invalid marriage, separation by a judge or mutaraka verbally is necessary in a consummated marriage; in other cases, separation by physical parting suffices. It should be that the invalidity occurs in fosterage that arises after marriage. As for if a man marries a woman and two just witnesses testify that she is his sister, the marriage is completely annulled (irtafa'a), so that if he has intercourse with her, he is hadded, and she may marry after the idda without mutaraka. The restriction that she breastfed her co-wife is not exclusionary, because the sister of the large wife, her mother, and her daughter by lineage or fosterage, if he has consummated with the large wife, are like her due to the necessity of combining between a woman and her sister's daughter in the first, between two sisters in the second, and between a woman and her daughter's daughter in the third. He may never marry any of them, nor the wet nurse either. If he has not consummated with the large wife in the third case, then the wet nurse is never permissible for him because she is the mother of his wife, nor the large wife because she is the mother of the mother of his wife, but the small wife is permissible because she is the daughter of the daughter of his wife, and he has not consummated with her.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling when a wife (kabira) breastfeeds the other wife (saghira) of the same husband. Both become forbidden to the husband because he would be simultaneously married to a mother and her daughter through fosterage. The marriage becomes invalid (fasid) but is not automatically annulled (infisakh). The Hanafi position is that fosterage and in-law relationships do not automatically terminate the marriage contract; rather, the marriage becomes defective and requires separation by a judge or mutual parting. The husband does not incur the hadd punishment if he has intercourse before separation, whether the situation is clear or ambiguous. The passage then compares this to a case where two witnesses testify that the wife is the husband's sister, in which case the marriage is completely annulled and the husband is subject to the hadd penalty. This distinction highlights the legal nuance between different types of prohibitions.

Key Terms
فسد (fasada): Became invalid; the marriage becomes fasid (defective) and requires separation.
انفسخ (infasakha): Annulment; the marriage is completely terminated without need for separate divorce.
متاركة (mutaraka): Mutual separation by agreement, often verbal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a wife breastfeeds her co-wife, what is the status of the marriage?
A) It is automatically annulled (infisakh)
B) It becomes invalid (fasid) and requires separation
C) It remains valid but the husband must abstain from intercourse
D) It becomes void (batil) from the start

Key Takeaway
When a wife breastfeeds her co-wife, the marriage becomes fasid (invalid) but not annulled; both wives become permanently forbidden to the husband, and separation must occur through judge's ruling or mutual parting.

Detailed Scenarios of Fosterage Among Multiple Wives
Detailed scenarios on fosterage among multiple wives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for various fosterage scenarios involving multiple wives and apply them to determine which marriages become forbidden.

Core Idea
Fosterage creates the same marriage prohibitions as blood relations; timing and consummation determine which wives become forbidden.

This passage from al-Bada'i' presents a set of detailed scenarios involving multiple wives and fosterage through breastfeeding. Understanding these scenarios is crucial for applying the Hanafi ruling that fosterage (rida') establishes the same mahram relationships as lineage. The key variables are the number of wives, the order of breastfeeding, and whether the husband has consummated the marriage with the breastfeeding wife.

Guided Path
1
Identify the relationships created
For each breastfeeding act, determine whether the relationship created is mother-daughter or sister-sister.
Breastfeeding a child makes the child a child of the nursing mother and a sibling to her other children.
2
Trace the timing of breastfeeding relative to marriage
Note when each breastfeeding occurred: before or after the marriage of the breastfeeding wife, and whether it was simultaneous or sequential.
The status of the breastfeeding wife (whether she was married to the man at the time) affects the prohibition.
3
Check for consummation
Determine if the husband had consummated with the breastfeeding wife. Consummation makes the prohibition stricter.
If consummated, all wives may become forbidden regardless of order.
4
Apply the principle of combining mahrams
A man may not be simultaneously married to two women who are mother-daughter or sisters through fosterage.
This principle determines which marriages become invalid.
5
Determine the outcome for each wife
Based on the above, state which wives separate (become forbidden) and which remain valid.
The order of breastfeeding often determines which wife is considered the 'older' relationship.

قال في البدائع : ولو أرضعتها عمة الكبيرة أو خالتها لم تبن لأنها صارت بنت عمتها أو بنت خالتها قال : ويجوز الجمع بين امرأة وبنت عمتها أو بنت خالتها في النسب والرضاع. ولو كان تحته صغيرتان وكبيرة فأرضعت الكبيرة الصغيرتين واحدة بعد واحدة ولم يكن دخل بالكبيرة فإنها تبين الكبيرة والصغيرة التي أرضعتها أولاً لكونهما صارا أماً وبنتاً، ولا تبين التي أرضعتها أخراً لأنها حين أرضعتها لم يكن في نحاكه غيرها، ولو أرضعتهما معاً بن جميعاً لأنهن صون أماً وبنتين وليس له أن يتزوج ،الكبيرة، وله أن يتزوج أي الصغيرتين شاء، ولو كان دخل بالكبيرة بنَّ جميعاً سواء أرضعتهما معاً أو على التعاقب. كذا في المبسوط. وقد علم به أن في مسألة الكتاب لو كان دخل بالكبيرة أو كان لبنها الذي أرضعت به الصغيرة من زوجها لا يتزوج واحدة منهما قط وإلا له أن يتزوج الصغيرة فقط لأن العقد على الأم لا يحرم البنت والعقد على البنت يحرم الأم، ولو كان تحته صغيرتان فأرضعتهما امرأة حرمتا عليه للأختية، سواء كان الإرضاع معاً أو متفرقاً، فإن كن ثلاثاً فأرضعتهن واحدة بعد واحدة بانت الأوليان لا الثالثة لأن الثالثة أرضعت وقد وقعت الفرقة بينه وبينهما فلم يحصل الجمع، وإن أرضعت الأولى ثم الثنتين معاً بنَّ جميعاً، وإن أرضعتهن معاً بأن حلبت لبنها في قارورة وألقمت إحدى ثدييها إحداهن والأخرى الأخرى وأوجرت الثلاثة معاً بن جميعاً لأنهن صرن أخوات معاً، وإن كن أربعاً فأرضعتهن واحدة بعد الأخرى بنّ جميعاً لأن الثانية صارت أختاً للأولى فبانتا فلما أرضعت الرابعة صارت أختاً للثالثة فبانتا أيضاً. كذا في الجوهرة. ولو كن كبيرتين وصغيرتين فأرضعت كل من الكبيرتين صغيرة حرمت عليه الأربع للزوم الجمع بين الأمين وابنيتهما، ولو أرضعت إحدى الكبيرتين الصغيرتين ثم أرضعتهما الكبيرة الأخرى وذلك قبل الدخول بالكبيرتين فالكبرى الأولى مع الصغرى الأولى بانتامنه، والصغرى الثانية لم تبن بإرضاع الكبرى الأولى والكبيرة الثانية إن ابتدأت بإرضاع الصغرى الثانية بانتا منه، أو أنه لا تقع الفرقة إلا بتفريق القاضي فراجعه وتأمل قوله : (أو) كان لبنها الذي أرضعت به الصغيرة من زوجها كذا في النهر وشرح المقدسي وأورد عليه أن عطفه على ما قبله يقتضي إمكان انفراد كون اللبن منه عن كونها مدخولة وهو فاسد لأنه يلزم من كون اللبن منه أن تكون مدخولة اللهم إلا أن البحر الرائق / ج ٣/ ٢٦٥
He said in al-Bada'i': If her paternal aunt or maternal aunt breastfeeds her, she does not separate (tabin) because she becomes the daughter of her paternal aunt or daughter of her maternal aunt. He said: Combining a woman and her paternal uncle's daughter or maternal uncle's daughter is permissible by lineage and fosterage. If he has two small wives and one large wife, and the large wife breastfeeds the two small ones one after the other, and he has not consummated with the large wife, then the large wife and the one she breastfed first separate from him because they became mother and daughter, but the one she breastfed later does not separate because at the time she breastfed her, there was no one else in his marriage besides her. If she breastfed them together, all separate because they become mother and two daughters. He may not marry the large wife, and he may marry whichever of the two small ones he wishes. If he had consummated with the large wife, all separate, whether she breastfed them together or consecutively. Thus in al-Mabsut. From this it is known that in the issue of the book, if he had consummated with the large wife, or if her milk with which she breastfed the small one was from her husband, he may never marry any of them; otherwise, he may marry only the small one, because the contract on the mother does not prohibit the daughter, but the contract on the daughter prohibits the mother. If he has two small wives and a woman breastfeeds them both, they become forbidden to him due to sisterhood, whether the breastfeeding is simultaneous or separate. If there are three, and she breastfeeds them one after the other, the first two separate, not the third, because the third was breastfed after separation had occurred between him and them, so no combination happened. If she breastfeeds the first, then the two together, all separate. If she breastfeeds them all together by milking her milk into a bottle and putting one of her nipples into one of them and the other nipple into the other, and she makes the third drink from the bottle simultaneously, all separate because they become sisters simultaneously. If there are four, and she breastfeeds them one after the other, all separate because the second becomes a sister of the first, so they separate; then when she breastfeeds the fourth, she becomes a sister of the third, so they also separate. Thus in al-Jawhara. If there are two large wives and two small ones, and each of the large wives breastfeeds a small one, the four become forbidden to him due to the necessity of combining two mothers and their two daughters. If one of the large wives breastfeeds the two small ones, then the other large wife breastfeeds them both, and this is before consummation with the large wives, then the first large wife and the first small wife separate from him, the second small wife does not separate due to the first large wife's breastfeeding, and the second large wife, if she began by breastfeeding the second small wife, both separate from him, or that separation does not occur except by a judge's separation. So refer to it and reflect on his statement: '(or) her milk with which she breastfed the small one was from her husband.' Thus in al-Nahr and Sharh al-Maqdisi. It was objected that his conjunction to what precedes implies the possibility of the milk being from him independently of her being consummated, which is invalid because from the milk being from him it necessarily follows that she is consummated, unless... al-Bahr al-Ra'iq vol. 3 p. 265.
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage from al-Bada'i' presents a series of detailed scenarios involving multiple wives and fosterage through breastfeeding. It covers cases where a wife breastfeeds her co-wife's relatives, such as the co-wife's aunt, which does not create a prohibition because it only makes the child a niece. It also discusses scenarios with two small wives and one large wife, timing of breastfeeding, and whether the husband has consummated the marriage with the large wife. The rulings vary based on whether the breastfeeding creates a relationship of mother-daughter or sister-sister, and whether the husband has already consummated the marriage. The key principle is that fosterage creates the same prohibitions as blood relation, and the timing of the breastfeeding relative to marriage and consummation determines which marriages become invalid.

Key Terms
البدائع (al-Bada'i'): A Hanafi fiqh work by al-Kasani, often cited as a source of detailed rulings.
المبسوط (al-Mabsut): A Hanafi fiqh work by al-Sarakhsi, one of the six core books of the zahir al-riwayah.
الجوهرة (al-Jawhara): A Hanafi fiqh work by al-Ghaznavi or another author, used as a reference.
تبين (tabin): She separates (becomes forbidden) from the husband due to fosterage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man has two small wives and a large wife, and the large wife breastfeeds both small ones simultaneously before consummation with the large wife, what is the ruling?
A) Only the large wife becomes forbidden
B) All three become forbidden and separate from him
C) Only the two small ones become forbidden
D) None separate because they are sisters

Key Takeaway
The outcome of multiple fosterage relationships depends on the order, timing, and consummation; each breastfeeding creates a mahram tie that may prohibit marriage.
